After I have completed the book for you, my sons, which is the last concerning knowledge in medicine and its supplement, and after I have come to an end in it, by means of its explanations and its own declarations, it seemed good to me that I should complete it for you with this Treatise, which is a part of surgery, namely, chirurgery with hand.
Since the operation with hand has been laid down in our region and during our time entirely prohibited: until perhaps the knowledge of it perished, and its trace vanished: and there remain only small descriptions in ancient books, which have been altered by hands; and error and hesitation occurred in them, until their intentions were closed and the impulse of it was prolonged: It seemed good to me that I should revive it with this Treatise's arrangement according to the way from the position, the declaration, and abbreviation; and that I come with forms of iron tools of Cautery and the rest of instruments' operation: with making additions to declarations and obtaining what is necessary.
The reason why a good craftsman of this is not found with his hand in our time, is because the art of medicine is long, and it is necessary for its author to exercise before that in the science of anatomy, which Galen narrated, until he knows the remedies of members, and their forms, and their conjunction and separation, and has knowledge of bones, nerves, muscles, and their number, and their exit, and the pulsations and quiets of veins, and their locations.
And for this reason, Hippocrates said that much is the name with the name, and little is the work, especially in the art of hand.
We have already said about it at the beginning of this book.
Since one who is not skilled in what we have said about anatomy will not be purged, but rather fall into error, in which men are slain: as I have seen many of those who are formed from this science, and boast about it without knowledge, and without experiment.
I have seen a foolish physician cut off a scrofulous apostema on a woman's neck and accidentally cut some arteries in the neck: therefore, the woman bled to death before his very eyes.
And I have seen another physician who presumed to extract a stone from an old man who had grown it, and the stone was large. Therefore, he came upon him and extracted the stone along with a fragment of the bladder. Wherefore the man died on the third day.
And I myself had been called to extract it; and I saw from the size of the stone and the state of the patient that he would die.
I have seen another physician who was receiving a stipend from some Duke of our land on account of his medicine: and a black eunuch who was with him suffered a fracture in the leg near the heel; and the physician, ignorant in this matter, bound up the fracture over the wound with ligatures and forceps, and did not allow the wound to breathe.
Then he treated him according to his own ideas. Later he dismissed him for some days and ordered him not to loosen the bandage; and so he stood thus until a tumor formed on his leg, and his foot, and came to ruin.
Therefore I was called upon him: and I hastened to undo the bandage; and quiet came over him, and he was relieved of his pains.
But the corruption had already become established in the limb: and I could not stop it.
The decay shall cease to spread through the member until it has perished.
And I saw another physician who perforated a malignant ulcer: and after days it was healed when the wickedness of it was revealed to its master.
Because when a cancer is pure from the humor of melancholy, then it should not be reached with iron entirely unless it is in a member that can bear it, so that the whole thing may be cut off.
And for this reason, O Sons, it is necessary for you to know that the operation is divided into two divisions: namely, an operation associated with health; and an operation, with which there is danger in various dispositions.
And I have already risen up in every place of this book where the operation comes, in which there is fear and dread.
Therefore it is necessary for you to be careful of this and to separate it yourself so that fools do not find a way to speak and disgrace themselves.
Take then the measure with care and protection, and use your sick ones with ease and firmness, and make use of a better way leading by the grace of God to health and praiseworthy success; and leave behind the terrible illnesses that are difficult to heal; and deliver yourselves from that which causes you fear, so that hesitation may not enter into your faith and comfort.
For it remains more for your glory, and higher in this world, and finally to your quantities.
For Galen has already said in some of his warnings. Do not heal evil diseases, lest you be called evil physicians.
Now I have divided this Treatise according to three Chapters.
First Chapter.
On cautery with fire and cautery with sharp medicine, this is the first chapter arranged from head to foot, and the forms of instruments for cautery, and its tools; and all that is necessary for the operation.
Chapter second.
On section and perforation, phlebotomy and ventosities, and wounds: and extraction of arrows, and similar things: and the whole chapter, arranged in forms of instruments. Â¶
Chapter third.
On restoration, and dislocation, and treatment of twisting, and similar things: the chapter is arranged from head to foot, and forms of instruments.
Before I remind you of the operation with it, it is necessary that I say the quality of its remedies and its harms, and in what composition it should be presented.
I therefore say that the discussion of the quality of the remedy and harm of the cautery is a long, subtle, scientific, and hidden knowledge.
Also there was a multitude of wise men who debated on it and disagreed among themselves; and to me, at least, a little of their discussions is sufficient for me, fearing prolongation.
I therefore say that the cautery applies universally to every composition, whether with material or without; except for two compositions, which are the hot composition without material and the dry composition without material.
In the hot and dry composition with material, they disagreed. Some said that the cautery is beneficial in it. Others said the opposite of this, namely that the cautery is not suitable for the illness which is from heat and dryness; because the nature of fire is heat; and it is inconvenient to be healed from a hot and dry illness with heat and dryness.
And he who says the opposite of this said that the cautery is beneficial for all hot and dry illnesses which happen in the bodies of men; because when you compare the body of a man and his humors to the composition of fire, you find the body of the man cold.
And I myself say by that speech: because it has often been proven to me in practice.
Nevertheless, it is not necessary for it to come up again unless he who has been tested and experienced in the last chapter of cautery exercise, and knows the diversity of men's compositions, and the disposition of illnesses within themselves, and the causes and accidents of them, and the duration of their span.
From the remaining temperaments (complexions), there is no fear for you; and especially in cold and moist diseases. For indeed, all physicians have agreed on them (cauteries); and they have not disagreed on the use of cautery with them.
And know, my sons, that from the secret of treatment by cautery with fire and its goodness on cautery with medicine burning, since fire is simple, whose action does not reach except to the member which is being cauterized; and it does not harm another joint connected with it, unless in a slight degree.
But the action of medicine burning reaches that which is stretched out from the members; and perhaps it causes pain in a member and perhaps kills it.
Fire, however, because of its subtlety and goodness of substance, does not do that unless it is in excess.
Now indeed it has become known to us through experiment, because of the length of service and diligence with skill, and the position concerning truth; and because of that I excuse myself from the length of speech.
And if it were not that it is not allowed for this book of mine, I would bring to you the secret concealed in fire, and the quality of its operation in bodies, by which it expels diseases, which could be demonstrated philosophically, and which would become clear to your minds.
And know, my sons, that they (physicians) themselves differ as to the time when a cautery should be made, and they put the better time in truth.
And I say that a cautery is appropriate at any time; for this reason, any harm resulting from the time (of the operation) is immersed in the benefit which is drawn near by the cautery. And especially if a cautery is for pains from necessary pains, strong, frequent, which do not tolerate delay; for this reason it is feared that there may occur a greater harm which would exceed the slight damage caused by time.
And let not that thought enter your minds, O sons, that it is not believed, except by the common people and foolish physicians, namely that there is no return for the ailment that is cured by cautery; and they put forth this as a consequence, but things are not so as they think: therefore because cautery is not, except in place of medicine, which alters complexion, and drives out humidities that are causes, wherefore pains occur.
However, the cautery is not always necessary for medicine due to the swiftness of its health, and the power of its operation, and the intensity of its dominion: it is possible that the ailment returns after a certain hour of time according to the complexion of the sick person, and the location of his ailment, and the strength of its effect: and whatever is prepared in his body from the accumulation of superfluities within him: and whatever reaches it in its acquisition from food, and similar things as causes, unless the ailment occurs where cautery is administered.
A subtle ailment in the member of small superfluities and humidities, such as cautery for teeth, due to pain, etc., it is possible that that pain will not return in him. But that happens in a few cases.
However, the speech of the common people again, that cautery is the last resort of medicine, is correct, not for what they intend in it: because they believe that there is no cure which gives with medicine or anything after the fall of cautery.
But the matter is contrary to theirs, and their intention, that cautery is the last resort of medicine, is not, except when we administer modes of cure for some ailments, and those do not give with medicine: then we administer cautery at the end, and it cures: then it falls out that cautery is the last resort of medicine, not according to the intention which the common people and many foolish physicians understand.
The ancients said that a cautery with gold is better than a cautery with iron; and they did not say this except because of the equality of gold, and the refinement of its substance; and they said that it does not cause pus at the site of cauterization. That is not entirely true; for I have already proven that it does not do this in certain bodies without any other effects.
And a cautery with it is good, and better than with iron, as they said. However, when you heat the cautery in fire from gold, it is not known to you when heated according to the quantity desired due to the redness of gold; and when it approaches the same coldness, if you add more heat to it, it liquefies in the fire and turns into sheets.
Therefore, the craftsman falls out of occupation because of this; and for that reason a cautery with iron is more expedient and closer at hand among us for the purpose of the operation.
And I myself have already arranged this Chapter on the Cautery, according to chapters; and I have ordered it from head to foot: so that those who seek it may find what they want from it.
Chapter II.
Here cauterization is applied for the lordship of humidity and coldness over the brain; which are two causes of scurvy, and flow of many fluids from the head to the parts of the eyes and ears, and sleepiness, toothache, sore throat, and in general any sickness that occurs due to coldness, such as paralysis, scurvy, epilepsy, apoplexy, and similar diseases.
The method of cauterization is to order the sick person: to evacuate it first with medicine dissolved in warm water for three or four nights, according to the strength of the sick person, and his age, and his habit.
Then command him to make an incision on his head with a new lancet. Then make him sit facing your hands, so that he now places his hands upon his chest.
Then place the palm of your hand on the root of his nose between his eyes. Wherever your middle finger comes to rest, mark that place with charcoal.
Then heat the cautery oil: this is its shape. (Here follows a description of the tool.)
Then place it on the marked spot with charcoal, pressing down gradually with your hand, and you turn it. Then quickly withdraw your hand and look at the place.
If you see it has been burned away a quantity of bone from the skull or of hair, then quickly withdraw your hand. And if not, keep pressing with the iron itself or with another until you see the bones that I told you about.
Then take some salt and dissolve it in water, dip a cloth in the solution, and place it on the spot; let it remain for three days.
Then place a cloth dipped in butter over the burn and leave it until the scab of fire is destroyed. Then treat it with the four-ingredient ointment until it heals. (Here follows a recipe for the ointment.)
They have said that as long as a wound remains open, it discharges pus; therefore it is better and more healing.
Some of them have said that the skin should be cauterized up to the bone; and hold the cautery until something of the thickness of the bone is burned.
Then grind down the burnt bone, then treat it.
Others say that when the cautery is used to its limit, an impression should be made on the bone for as long as it falls off like a layer of skin, or an instrument similar to what women use for infusing a small amount of alcohol, and they believe that vapors of the head escape from this place; and leave the open wound for a long time.
Then it shall be treated until it solidifies.
To me, these two kinds of cautery do not appear at all except in certain men according to the way of fear.
And let him be sent away, with me it is better for his own safety.
For indeed the head is weakened by the continuity of its own solution; as we have testified in other members; and especially when the head of the weak is naturally frail; and the first kind of cautery is safer and better according to me, and I use it; therefore, operate with it for safety.
Chapter III.
When a chronic pain occurs throughout the whole head: and it is prolonged in the sick, and uses herbs, and poultices, and leeches, and oils, and plasters. Moreover, if it has already been cauterized with one cautery, as we have mentioned, and it does not improve from these [measures]: then consider. If the head of the sick person is strong by nature and not weak, and it finds intense coldness: then cauterize with another cautery gently under that [part]. Then cauterize it on the whole horn of his head with a cautery, so that the skin is not pierced through, and an amount of bone is uncovered as we have mentioned. And cauterize it with one cautery on the occiput of his head, at the place which is called a vessel; and it is a place where a vent is placed; pour your warm oil into this, and do not uncover the bone. For the sick person finds intense pain from that [source of pain], and different from the pain of all other cauteries of the head.
And I will say this cautery for the place itself; and it is necessary that it be a cautery which cauterizes horns of the head, and the occiput more delicately with a cautery which cauterizes the middle of the head.
Chapter III [The third chapter]
When there is pain and swelling in part of the head, or the pain extends to the eye, and it is treated with purifying medicines for the head, and further treatment is administered as I have said in the division of illnesses, and it does not improve: then cauterization is applied to this [condition] according to two methods: either cauterization with a sharp hot medicine; or with iron.
The cautery with a sharp burning medicine is to receive one garlic clove, peel it, and cut off its ends from both sides. Then divide the place of pain at the time with a wide lance, until there is a place under the skin where the tooth can be captured.
Introduce it into the same place under the skin until it is hidden: then press on it with a suitable ligature and leave it for fifteen hours, then dissolve it and extract the garlic, and leave the wound for two or three days; afterwards put a hot plaster submerged in butter over it until a pus forms: then care for it with an ointment until it heals.
And if you wish to perform that procedure with certain burning medicines which I have written about in the twelfth treatise on poisons.
But cauterization of this kind is as follows: Fire Cautery, whose form is as follows:
And it is called Clauilis: because its head's form resembles a nail, in which there is some curved part, and in the middle of it there is a small projection.
Then place it on the location and hold your hand; and you rotate the iron slowly with speed; let the quantity to be cauterized be of skin thickness, as its half. And lift your hand, so that an artery below it is not burned and blood flow occurs.
Then immerse the cotton in a saltwater solution and place it on the location, leave it for three days; then immerse the cotton with butter; afterwards treat it with ointment until it heals.
And if you wish, cauterize this hemicania with a second part of the Cautery cutlery. Beware not to make an incision in the artery of this hemicania, not anciently.
[Heading] On the method of cauterization in ancient hemicania.
When you treat a hemicania, as we have said in the previous treatment and what we have said in the divisions of diseases, and the treatment does not help; and you see from the disease that it is insufficient for what we have said with the first cautery with medicine, or with cautery with fire, then it is necessary to heat the Cautery cutlery until it becomes white, after you mark the location of pain with a line whose length is half a finger, or about that; and lay your hand aside once, and press it until you make an incision in the artery, and reach the bone.
However, it is necessary for you to beware of the continuous movement of the jaw, which occurs during chewing, so that the side or nerve that moves it is not burned, and a spasm does not occur.
And it should be concerning the care and caution regarding the flow of blood from a severed artery. In the cutting (of an artery), fear is present and particularly for him who does not know what he is doing and is not diligent or experienced; and he should first abandon the operation with this person.
And I shall come (again) with a reminder of the management of bleeding from an artery according to its own method, and in its proper place in this book.
If you see that this cautery does not suffice for the patient and you see the body of the weak one bearing the cautery in the middle of the head, as we have narrated, care for the wound until it heals.
And if you wish, administer cautery, as we have said in the chapter on the extraction of an artery with cautery having two knives. Indeed, cauterization is better in this way and more beneficial.
On the method of cauterizing in pain of an ear.
When there is pain in the ear due to cold and it is treated with solvents, and with other treatments as we have said in division, and yet the pain does not subside, then cauterize with fire: this is what is called Punctum; its form is as follows.
Then the punctum is made with it after its ignition around the entire ear, as it is described; or around both if pain occurs on both sides. And extend the cautery slightly away from the root of the ear after marking the spots with pitch; and let the quantity of the cauterization be ten puncta in every ear, and about that.
Then care for the spots until they heal.
On the method of cauterizing in a torture.
Chapter VII.
The torture that is cured with cauterization, is not other than those occurring by phlegm, according to what we said in the divisions of illnesses.
And to be avoided are cauterization and bleeding of those occurring by excision, and spasm of a nerve.
When this kind of torture cannot be cured by herbs, and purges, and gargles, then it is necessary that you cauterize the sick person with three Cauteries: one at the root of the ear, and second a little below his earlobe, and third at the junction of the two lips.
Place your Cautery on the weaker side of the body. Since softening does not occur unless in the healthy part.
And the form of cauterization is that you cauterize with the Cautery itself directly on the upper end of the ear lobe near the vertex, and another at the earlobe; whose length should be according to the length of the thumb. And place your hand with the Cautery until a quantity equal to half the thickness of the skin is burned.
And this is the form of the Cautery, and it is of the type of a scalpel, whose shape was mentioned before; but it should not be too thin, as you can see; and it is necessary that there be a scalpel in it of excessive thickness a little less.
Then take care of the places where this was done until they are healed.
Chapter on the method of cauterizing in ancient apoplexy.
When apoplexy occurs and it cannot be cured with what has been said, and the sick person does not have a fever, then cauterize him with four Cauteries over all his skull, and a Cautery in the middle of his head, as was mentioned before, and a Cautery on the back of his head, according to what has been described; and the method of cauterization should be according to what has been described.
Also cauterized on the face of the stomach with a cautery; and it is more ultimate.
Then cured when that which preceded has been done.
Head IX.
It is necessary that in drink, for the sick head, there be first great hyerae, and purifying pills of brain.
Then shave the sick head entirely, and place on its backside ointment from synapi described in the treatise of ointments; place it there often.
For that is the method of cautery; and make it in the same order as I said there.
If then he is healed by this, it is good. If not: then make for him three cauteries on the backside of his head, which are descending from the upper part of the head to the lower part of the eye; and place between every cautery a thickness of finger.
Then care for the cautery, as for what went before.
If however you wish an addition, and the sick one can bear it; then make a cautery in the middle. And if you want an addition: then cauterize it over two horns.
Then care for it until he is healed; and let the cautery be anointed according to the shape that was given before.
Chapter on the method of cauterization in paralysis, and softening.
Head X.
It is necessary to proceed with cleansing the head with hyeers and as was said before.
Then shave the sick head; afterwards cauterize it with a cautery in the middle of the head, and with a cautery on every horn of the head, and with a cautery on the backside of it, and with three on the spine of the neck.
If however in sickness you require softening of the body with more of these, and the sick one can bear it, and the illness is strong: then cauterize it with four cauteries on the spine, and the last one with a cautery until it burns through the skin most of it, and loosen your hand. Then take care of yourself until you are healed: and thus cauterize with oil.
On the method of cauterization for epilepsy.
An epileptic is not cauterized unless his epilepsy is due to phlegm.
Therefore it is necessary to clean the brain of the epileptic patient first with hyssop and with the rest of the treatment that we have mentioned earlier, when the patient is critically ill or tolerant of medication.
If the patient is a child who cannot tolerate medication, then administer gargarisma and cleansing food for the brain, many days before with good nourishment.
Then shave his head, then cauterize the patient himself with a single cautery in the middle of the head according to what has been described earlier; and with another cautery on the back of his head and over all the horn of his head. If the patient is strong and tolerant, then cauterize him with the cauteries mentioned earlier for paralysis, and mollification of the body on vertebrae of the neck and backbone; and let it be oil-cauterized as described earlier.
If the patient is a child, then place a subtle cautery according to this method.
On the method of cauterization for melancholy.
When the cause of melancholy is corrupted humors and thick phlegm, then cauterize the patient with the cauteries mentioned for paralysis.
And if the cause of melancholy is an excess of declivis leading to melancholy and the body of the patient is moist, then give him a drink that cleanses his brain as described earlier; then shave the head of the patient, and make a well-centered bandage from linen, similar to a circle.
Then place it in the middle of the head, and the weak person sitting square should hold it from all sides.
Then apply the liniment. And it is more suitable for ancient butter of sheep. Heat it over the fire with a suitable temperature measure, so that when the finger is introduced into it, it can tolerate it. Then evacuate it from the middle of his head in a circle, and release it until it cools down.
Make him do this once a week with the rest of his good regimen until he is cured.
Or if you wish, cauterize it by making many small punctures in it, as long as you hold it with the cautery; it should be aromatic.
For this type of cauterization moistens the brain with its quality.
Then place a warm cloth soaked in butter or goose fat on it.
[Chapter Title] Method of Cauterization as the Water Descends to the Eye.
Chapter 13.
When the beginning of water appears in the eye through the signs that I said in the division, then begin and wash the sick person while cleansing his head.
And keep him away from all moisture, and make him sit in a bath for several days while fasting.
Then order him to shave his head, and cauterize it in the middle of his own head. Then cauterize it over two temples with two cauteries, if the descent of water appears in both eyes at once; or from one side, if the water appears in only one eye; and cut off all veins and arteries that are under the skin using the cautery, and let the cauteries be long in length equal to the temples' width; and avoid bleeding.
If you see something coming out of it, then cut it off immediately with any medicine that is possible; and I will come with the wisdom that is in extracting arteries and cutting them off, and taking care to avoid bleeding.
And sometimes, it is cauterized in the neck, under two bones, with two cauteries emitted lastly.
On the ancient method of cauterizing in the tear ducts.
When tears of the eyes are chronic and on veins and arteries that are visible externally on the head, it is verified that it is due to an excess of cold, phlegmatic humors; then cauterize with a cautery as I have described in the beginning concerning descending water, a cautery in the middle of the head, and two cauteries above the two temples, and two cauteries on the neck under the two bones. And if necessary, then cauterize it carefully on all sides of the eye, above the eyebrow with a small cautery.
Chapter on the method of cauterizing in nasal stench.
Chapter 15. When treating it as mentioned above, and the medication does not work; then hurry, and give infirmocochia for three nights; then shave its head, and cauterize it with a medium-sized cautery along with an oil cautery. Then cauterize it with a claw-shaped cautery and two cauteries under the eyebrows, slightly above the hairline.
And be careful not to cut the artery.
And this is the form of the claw-shaped cautery.
Chapter on the method of cauterizing in softening the eyelid.
Chapter 16. When the eyelid of the eye is softened by illness or moisture; then cauterize the eyelid with one cautery, along with this lunar cautery.
And if you wish, cauterize it above the eyebrows with two small cauteries in all parts; and they should extend from the temples; and the length of the entire cautery should be according to the length of the eyebrows; and do not bring your hand with the cautery too close, rather according to the quantity that is burned by the third eyelash.
In the manner of cauterizing the eyelid, when hairs are turned inward and piercing the eye.
The cautery is in two modes: either a cautery with fire, or a cautery with a burning medicine.
In the cautery with fire, command the sick person to release his hairs if he is among those who clean them, until they grow out and are evened. If they pierce him at the root of his eye: then bind his eyes with a plaster so that they do not move until they grow out.
When they grow out and are evened, then place the head of the sick person on your lap. Then mark the eyelids of his eyes with wax, mark that it is in the shape of a myrtle leaf; let the beginning of the mark be near the hairs.
Then put a warm dish on cheesecloth or on psyllium gum over the eye.
Then apply fire to the cautery, whose form is this.
Then cauterize according to the shape you marked, slowly in several places until the surface of the skin is burned, which is like the shape of a myrtle leaf, entirely appearing properly.
And your mark of health is that if you see the eyelid of the eye already contracting and hairs rising at the site of piercing the eye.
Then lift up your hand then, and let him go for three days.
Then put a warm dish with butter on him until the scab falls off. Then care for him with an ointment until he is healed.
If some of the hairs return after an hour and the eyelid becomes soft: then repeat the cautery on that spot as you did at first.
If hairs are in the lower part [of the body]: then cauterize it until it is brought to its natural place; and ensure that the hairs do not prick the eye.
You should advise the sick person to let go of his hairs until they grow longer and match. Make from parchment a shape of a myrtle leaf.
Then take from known soap and unabsorbed lime from each a weight of one ounce or approximately that; then grind them together with good grinding, so that it is done quickly, lest it becomes cold. Then from the ointment spread on parchment as a shape of a myrtle leaf, and place it on the eyelid of one or both eyes. And place under the eye a heated cotton soaked in egg white, and the head of the sick person should be in your lap.
And place your index finger on the medicine and press it slightly. And you move it whenever the sick person feels the bite of the medicine, since its bite is like fire.
While he continues to feel this bite, then release the medicine and move it with your finger. When the bite ceases, then remove the medicine, and wash the eye with water.
And then consider if you see the eyelid raised like when it is drawn up by heat or incision, it is good: and if not, then repeat on the same place from the medicine where the medicine does not press and does not discolor, until your operation is equal and the eye contracts.
Then place on it a cotton with butter until the burnt skin is removed. Then care for it with diaphinicon ointment, or another, until it heals.
It is necessary for you during the operation that you keep the final safeguard, lest anything from the medicine fall into the eye.
If the eyelid becomes softened after days and something fights from hairs within the eye, then repeat the medicine upon that place which became soft due to the eyelid, just as you did at first. Then care for it until it heals.
And this is the shape of the myrtle leaf.
And know that the eyes of men are diversified in size and smallness. Therefore according to this your consideration should be: and not hidden the way of rightness for him who has devotion for this art.
Chapter on the method of cauterization in the lacrimal fistula.
When you treat the fistula, if your treatment does not help as we said in the classification of diseases, then it is necessary that you cauterize it according to this method.
Order the sick man to put his head in your lap, and hold his head by your hands in such a way that it is not moved or shaken with his head.
Then place the cotton soaked in oil or psillium poultice on his eye: then cauterize it with this cautery whose shape is as follows.
Be hollowed like the form of a goose feather quill from one end, with which the cautery is made: and if you wish it to penetrate up to the other end, and if you wish it to be bent upward in this way.
Nevertheless, it is better for your use that it is hollowed.
Then squeeze the fistula if it is open and extract pus from it, and excise it: and if it is not open, then open it and extract its pus.
Then place upon it the cautery, which is made very hot.
Hold your hand near the cautery, at the nose's part, close to the eye, so that your hand does not wander or tremble; and you place the cautery on the eyelid fat, and burn it.
If you therefore reach at the beginning of your cautery to the bone, it will be good. And if not: then heat the cautery again, once or twice, as needed; and leave it for three days.
Then place the cotton with butter, and care for it with an drying ointment until healed.
If it exceeds forty days and is not healed: then place on it a sharp corrosive medicine until the bone appears; and grind it according to what comes in its chapter.
And there is another method of cautery for abscesses, which some first ones said. Direct yourself to the place of the abscess, and open it; then place into the same opening a thin camel bone, that is, a fine cannula, whose shape this is. And pour into it a weight of drachmae in melted lead, and hold your hand with the cannula's retention good, and not move at all weak, so that it does not run or reach the melted lead to its eye.
And it is necessary that you place on the eye of the weak a cotton soaked in egg white or water.
For lead burns the abscess place, and heals it wonderfully with its healing.
If the abscess heals as we said with cautery and treatment, it is good. If not, then it is necessary to make a hole in the nose and lead the abscess to the nasal passage, according to what comes in its place itself.
Method of Cauterization in Fissures of Lips.
Chapter XX.
When you treat these fissures, as we said in the division of diseases, and the treatment does not help, then prepare a small cautery tool shaped like this.
And let its concavity be like that of a scalpel, fine.
Then place it (the cautery) quickly on the fissures until the cauterization reaches the depth of the fissures.
Then care for it with pitch, until it heals.
Chapter on Cauterizing a Mouth Fistula.
If a boil occurs on the root of the gum, or in the palate, or in the roots of the teeth: then it becomes pus and bursts; afterwards it turns into an old abscess, and the pus runs and forms a fistula: then treat it, but if treatment does not help, then it is necessary to cauterize it with fire according to its size, so that it can fill the fistula. Then insert the hot iron into the hole of the fistula and hold your hand until the heated iron reaches its depth and end; do this once or twice.
Then take care of it after that, as we said about treatment, until it is cured.
If the pus separates and heals, it will be good. And if not, then it is necessary to expose the place and remove the rotten bone according to what comes into its head.
Chapter on Cauterizing the Softened Gum and Teeth.
If the gum becomes soft due to moisture and the teeth move, and treatment with medicine does not help, then place the head of the patient on your lap.
Then fire-cauterize, and the shape will come after this so that you can place a Cannula on the tooth and insert the heated cautery quickly into it: hold your hand for a short while until the patient feels the heat of the fire has reached the root of the tooth.
And move your hand: then repeatedly apply the cautery as often as you wish.
The sick person should fill his own mouth with water of salt and hold it for an hour; then he should spit it out.
For the tooth which is moved firms, and the gums, being softened, are closed, and the corruption of moisture dries up.
On the method of cauterizing dental pain.
When the pain of a tooth is due to coldness or there is coldness itself, or worms, and cure with medicines does not help: then cautery in it should be done according to two methods: either cautery with butter; or cautery with fire.
The cautery with butter is that you take warm butter and boil it in an iron kettle or in a cow's horn. Then take the heated cautery and apply it to the tip of the tooth. Then immerse it in the boiling butter and place it quickly on the painful tooth and hold it until it cools; then apply it again several times until the power of the fire reaches the root of the tooth.
And if you wish, immerse wool or the cautery in cold butter and place it on the painful tooth; then place a hot iron on top of it until the heat reaches the depth of the hollow of the tooth.
The cautery with fire is to prepare a pipe of brass or iron. And let there be something bulky in its body so that the sharpness of the fire does not reach the sick bone.
Then heat the cautery and place it on the tooth; hold your hand until the cautery cools.
Do this repeatedly, for pain will be relieved either on the same day or on another day.
And it is necessary that in the application of that Cautery, the sick person fills his bone with good oil and holds it for an hour; then he should spit it out.
And this is the form of the cautery.
Apply the cautery with any end as possible; and this is the form of the cannula.
[Chapter Title] On the method of cauterizing boils.
When boils are caused by phlegm and cold humors, and do not obey digestion through medicines, and fire digests them quickly; then use a concave cautery with this form.
Having two open ends, so that the smoke may come out from one end of the cautery; place it on top of the boil once, and a second time if necessary, until it reaches the depth of the boil.
If the boil is small; then place the cautery according to the size of the boil.
Then leave it for three days, and place a hot cloth soaked in oil on top of it until what the fire burned is removed.
Then care for it with tooth ointment until the form of the cannula heals.
[Chapter Title] On the method of cauterizing a hoarseness and constriction of the breath.
When moisture collects over the trachea of the lung, and especially when it is with coldness of the constitution, then it is necessary that the sick one be evacuated first with soluble medicines.
Then cauterize it at the neck near the root of the throat in a depressed place; and take care that with the cautery you do not reach the throat, nor the skin, unless something of its kind.
Then cauterize it with another cautery at the junction of the neck and shoulder at its end; and let the cautery be a nail, according to the manner that preceded.
Then treat it with what preceded until it is cured.
Chapter on the method of cauterization for diseases of the Lung and Cough.
When cough and disease of the lung are from cold moisture, and the sick one does not have fever nor phthisis (consumption), and the illness is old: then cauterize it with two cauteries above the clavicle in depressed, smooth, empty places. And with another cautery in the middle of the chest between the two breasts; and let the cautery be a tube, according to the form that preceded.
And if your cauterization is to be done by pricking with a cautery called "Punctum", whose form preceded in the section on the pain of the ears; and let the pricks be thirty or so, up to the other (side).
Then treat it with what preceded until it is cured.
And now let the cautery have three branches; according to this form. Why is cauterization accompanied, when you do it with one cautery in place of three?
Head Chapter XXVII.
When the head is dislocated due to reasons of humidity, and it does not return by itself within the hour following its dislocation, when this habit of returning has become established for it, then the dislocation should be reduced first. Then the sick person lies down on his back or on his sound side. Then you press the skin that is on the inner part of the cheekbone towards the top with your left hand fingers, and if there is a joint dislocation towards the inner parts.
Then taking two-pronged cautery in fire. Its form is as follows.
Then cauterize the skin until it penetrates to the other side, and the figure of cauterization with four cauteries will come.
And when the cautery has three prongs, it forms a figure of cauterization with six cauteries, and there are prongs according to the subtlety of the skin being treated.
And this is the form of the cautery with three prongs.
And sometimes one is added to this method, making eight cauteries.
Then place the compressed stylets (porrons) on top of the cautery with salt. Then make the sick person remain calm so that the limb is not moved at any time until it recovers.
And if the dislocation is upwards (towards the shoulder), which rarely happens, then cauterize it with a flat iron cautery on the shoulder, or with many small pricks using several cauteries.
For the joining (of bones) strengthens and removes moisture; the sick person recovers.
Chapter on the method of cauterizing the stomach.
When cold and excessive moisture occur in the stomach until it is expelled from its state, and they multiply catarrhs on it, and various methods of treatment are not effective, then the sick person should lie down on his back, spread his legs, and extend his hands. Then cauterize with three cauteries: one cautery of the size of a finger-tip for the cochlea of the breast, another cautery like a nail, and two cauteries below, from both sides of one cautery; until the figure of the cauteries becomes triangular. And extend between each so that they do not join, when pus forms.
And the depth of the cautery be the size of two finger-widths of skin.
And the shape of the cauteries be according to this form without addition: and if you wish to cauterize with a large cautery in the middle of the stomach according to this form, let the cautery that does this be one, shaped like a circle according to this form.
The stomach is cauterized by pricking it with a cautery that restrains it: and there are signs upon the stomach to mark the spot according to your wish with wax: then cauterize it with the cautery for the spot, then care for it with the remedy that preceded until it heals.
Chapter on how to cauterize the epactus (epigastric hernia) with cold cautery.
When pain occurs in the epigastrium due to coldness and humidity, or due to excessive gas that cannot pass through its natural exit, and the patient is weak, even when treated as we have said, it does not improve: then the patient should lie on his back with his head, and mark three cauteries with wax according to this form, and the same size below the epigastrium, where the elbow of a man reaches: let the space between each cautery be the width of a finger: let the cautery be of the length of the body upright: and do not press your hand tightly with the cautery.
And let the thickness of what is to be burned be half its size without addition: and let the patient stand on his feet.
If it is not standing, then it should be lying down, which has already extended its legs, and raised its arms.
This is the form of the cautery.
And indeed it is possible for you to perform cauteries with this cautery using a sharp cautery tool when you are skillful and wise in your craft.
And beware that you do not proceed too far in cauterization so that the entire thickness of the skin is burned, for the entire body is being burned, and it reaches the intestines; because there the skin is delicate, therefore know this.
Chapter on the method of cauterizing liver abscesses.
When there is discharge, and you want to know if the abscess is in the liver flesh or its membrane; then if it is in the liver flesh, an indolent pain and heaviness without sharpness occurs; but if it is in the liver membrane, with a painful sharpness. And now you see that the treatment of this has exhausted the doctors.
The patient must therefore lie down with his head resting. Next, place the lancet in the form of an apostate's position with the encaustic: then heat the cautery resembling a ray. And this is its form. And cauterize it with the cautery until the whole skin is burnt and it reaches the siphac until all pus comes out: then care for him with healing of the wounds, until he is healed.
And it is not appropriate to use this cauterizing method, unless one's dedication to the art of medicine continues: and through whose hands these diseases occur with repeated experience: then he may dare on such operations.
But rather, let it be released, is better with me.
Section on Cauterization in Pleurisy.
Ancients said that cauterization with roots of Aristolochia for cold pleurisy in this way. And it is to take from the dry roots of Aristolochia a longer root, which is found among them, and let it be as thick as a finger. Then immerse it in oil and light it on fire. Then cauterize it with one cautery where there is continuation of the neck with the collarbone, and with two small cauteries near the area that is beneath the chin.
And with two cauteries also where there is between the fifth and sixth ribs near the back, and with another cautery in the middle of the chest, and another above the stomach. And with three cauteries from the back: one where there is between two scapulas, and with two cauteries on either side of the chest, the lower cautery where it is between two scapulas.
And do not press your hand with a cautery, rather let it be clearly smelling the skin.
And some of the ancients have said that there are people who use a cautery made from iron like a ray and burn it inside where it is between the ribs until it reaches the abscess, and the pus comes out: as we said in the case of the abscess of the liver.
But in this perforation with a cautery, there is fear because either the sick person dies immediately, or a fistula occurs in the place where there is no healing.
Chapter 32: On the method of cauterizing the spleen.
When you treat the illness of the spleen, as we said in the treatment and division of diseases, and your treatment is not effective, then cautery is applied to it according to three methods, all of which are correct.
One is that you make three or four cauteries, lining them up along the length of the spleen in the shape of the cauteries for the liver, whose figure was described earlier.
And the thickness between each cautery should be the size of a finger, or more or less.
The method of cauterization should be equal, as we have said in the cauterization of the liver.
And do not press your hand with the cautery: let the weak one lie on his back.
Another method of cauterization is: having the cautery with two openings, as we have said in the chapter on dislocation of the humerus; and remove the skin, which is directly above the spleen, where the weak one's elbow comes to be; and your removal should be in accordance with the width of the body, so that the cauteries fall according to the length of the body.
Then insert two openings with very hot fire until it penetrates the skin on the other side; then remove the cautery; so four cauteries are made.
And if you want to cauterize with a cautery having three openings.
Then care for the cautery after you release it, to emit pus for many days; for it is more beneficial than the rest that came before in the treatment.
Chapter on the method of cauterizing in hydropsis.
The cautery does not fall in hydropsis, unless properly placed on the bladder.
When you treat a hydropsic person with the methods of treatment that we have mentioned in the division, and the treatment does not work, then it is necessary to cauterize it with four cauteries around the umbilicus, one on the stomach, another on the liver, another on the spleen, two behind the spine, and one on the chest and another on the stomach; and the quantity of the depth of the cautery should be close to the thickness of the skin.
Then release the open cautery, so that it may emit pus for a long time.
And do not evacuate the weak one from treatment after cauterization with it; for two intentions should be applied to him: and healing will hasten to him with the help of God.
The form of the cautery used to cauterize the abdomen should be a claw-like shape, following its previous form. And the form of the one used to cauterize the back should be olive-shaped, according to its previous form.
On the method of cauterizing Feet and Legs.
When draining in Hydropsy and filled with citrus water, it is necessary to cauterize on the top of the foot at the shin, which is between the auricle and ankle; then lift your hand with the cautery, and do not twist it; then lift your hand again; and do not go near it completely.
Citrus water will flow out, and let the cautery be in this shape.
Then make two cauteries on both legs, and let the cautery be at the end of a scalpel-shaped cautery; and let the cautery be along the length of the leg, one below the knee, and the other lower by about half the leg's length; and over the entire hip place two cauteries; leave the open cautery without long treatment, so that some water flows out of it; then treat it with what we have said.
On the method of cauterizing in the dissolution of the Abdomen.
Chapter XXXV.
When the solution of the stomach is softened by cold and humidity, until its retentive and digestive powers are weakened which are in the stomach and intestines: and it is cured with methods of treatment, but it does not heal: then one cauterizes it with a large cautionery on the stomach itself, according to what was described before in the cauterization of the stomach with a circular cautionery, and four subtle cauteries around the navel, with a subtle cautery claw: and with a subtle cautionery on top of alum over aloes, or with two cauteries.
If you see humidities in excess and the patient enduring it, then cauterize it with a cautionery on the sternum and a cautionery over the whole ilium: perhaps you may also add two small cauteries near the stomach.
For indeed, the cure is progressing, and its help does not deceive.
Chapter on the method of cauterizing Hemorrhoids.
Chapter XXXVI.
When in the anus there are many old hemorrhoids, or one, and they are of gross humors, cold, or corrupted by humidity, and are cured with what was said in the division, but the cure does not help: then cauterize them with three cauteries on the lower part of the lumbar vertebra under the almeidate triangle a little, and with a cautionery under the navel as if with two fingers.
And if you think that the stomach of this one is chilled and its food is not digested, and you see his face pallid, then cauterize it on the stomach with a large cautionery, according to what was described before: and with a cautionery over the liver of the same, and another over the spleen of the same, with a cautery claw: and let the open cautionery rest for some time: then care for him until he is healed.
Head Chapter 37.
When you excise althelul, then ignite the cautery that resembles a rod. Then introduce the burning cautery into the excised althelul and bring your last hand to it, until the cautery reaches the opening of the vein from which blood flows. Do this once or twice.
If there are many althelul, then cauterize each one with a separate cautery as we have described. Then care for them with that which you apply to them from the ointments until they heal up.
And if you cauterize it with a large cautery upon an alcatin, it is more final in its benefit.
Method of Cauterizing a Fistula in the Anus.
Head Chapter 38.
When the sick person does not obey the incision and operation as we have described in its place, and he is afraid of it, perhaps he will heal with cauterization.
When there occurs any fistula, and it breaks, pus flows from it, and the humors are corrupted. Therefore, it is necessary to test it with a thin probe. Then recognize the depth of it with a probe.
Then heat the cautery that is like a rod. Then insert yourself (into the fistula) heated, and the depth where the probe has entered.
And repeatedly heat the cautery over it until all the corrupted bodies are burned, once or twice or three times, according to the necessity of your case.
And beware of burning the nerve or large vein if there is one nearby; or if the fistula flows toward the bladder or intestine, then beware of these places altogether.
And do not perform it unless the fistula is in a fleshy place; and remember that it does not penetrate.
Then take care of the place until it heals.
If however the place is sealed and the matter is cut away from it, and remains in that state for a long time; then you will know that it is healed completely.
If however the matter is not cut away from it, then you will know that it penetrates, or that its deep part has become corrupted, or something like that, which will remind itself at its place.
[Chapter on cauterizing kidneys]
When pain occurs in the kidneys from cold or from thick wind, and it decreases due to the weakness of the body, then it is necessary that you cauterize it over alum on top of the kidneys, with a cautery over all the kidney with cautery claw, whose preceded remembrance.
And perhaps we cauterize it for the second time in the same alum. Because three lines will come. Therefore, there will be more benefit in the liniment.
