Â§ On the method of cauterizing the womb.
When coldness and dampness occur in the matrix (womb) and it is forbidden by that from conception, and its menstrua are corrupted, and their provocation is delayed, and pain occurs at their approach, then it is necessary to be cauterized with three cauteries around the umbilicus, as we said in the cauterization of the bladder, and a cautery on top below the back, or with two cauteries: and let the cautery be claw-shaped.
On the method of cauterizing the anus in dislocation.
When the humidities of the mucosa flow out to the perianal area, and become the cause of its exit from its place; and a sign of this is that the leg is stretched over the other when they are compared with each other; and a place of dislocation is found empty in it.
Therefore it is necessary to be cauterized weakly over the perianal area with a similar cautery circle; after you have marked it with the encaustic (beeswax) around the perianal area, as it is described; and so that the perianus falls in the middle of the circle.
If this cautery is not present to you, then be cauterized with three cauteries, with a large oil-soaked (oiled) cautery; and let the depth of the cautery be according to the thickness of the skin in total.
Then take care of it until it is healed.
On the method of cauterizing in Sciatica.
When there is pain in an ulcer of the anus and its cause is coldness and moisture: it should be treated as mentioned in the division, but the treatment does not help, then that should be aged: then it is necessary to dissolve the sick person from thick fluids with stinking pills or with artificial pills or similar ones. Then cauterize him.
And the method of cauterization is according to two methods: either cauterization with medicines advancing or cauterization with fire.
Cauterization with fire, is according to many modes.
One of them is that you cauterize on the ulcer of the anus itself with three triangular cauteries in this way. And make a good or bad depth for them. And let the space be between each cautery of the thickness of a finger, and let the cautery be oiled.
Sometimes it is done that the cautery takes place in the middle on the head of the anus itself. Why are there four cauteries?
And if you want to cauterize with a circle whose form preceded the cauterization of the displacement of the anus, one: so that the circle contains the entire anus.
And burn the thickness of the skin all over.
This is the method of cauterization for Sciatica, when the pain is attached to the anus itself, and it does not extend to the hip and leg.
If it extends to the hip and leg, then cauterize it with two cauteries on the hip, at the place where the sick person indicates, where there is pain, and your cautery four fingers on the forest part a little: let the cautery be sharp.
And the depth of the cautery should be according to the thickness of the skin.
If the sick person indicates that the pain extends near the toes of the foot, then cauterize it there where he indicates, with a cautery of points, three, or four, or more, if necessary.
If he indicates that the pain is turned towards the shin of the leg, then cauterize it there with a knife-like cautery.
And be careful in all your cauterizations that you do not burn a nerve or the great artery with it, and draw harm upon the sick person by that, or cause shrinkage (contraction).
And I myself have seen one and another of those who cauterized above the heel, and burned in the cauterization, and the leg became swollen until it reached the foot, and it was completely perforated, and the whole foot was corrupted: then follows the opening of the stomach, and death after that.
If the pain is in two parts at once, cauterize each one according to this method.
And some wise men have said in cauterizing the anus, that this method of cautery is appropriate for it. Make a similar probe of iron, whose diameter is half the breadth of the palm: and let it be at its opening according to its size, that of the nucleus of the thumb or less: and within this probe there should be a third probe.
And let the distance between all probes be the size of a knuckle: and let the probes be open at two ends: and their height should be like that of a knuckle, or two knuckles: and make handles of iron suitably placed on the probes.
Then it is heated in the fire until it turns red and sparks fly: then it should be placed on a basin for the anus of the sick person lying on his healthy side. Cauterize it therefore with three round cauteries at one time.
Then let him be for three days. Afterward, pack it with butter: and let the open wound be for many days. Then care for him with ointment, until he is healed.
Says Albucasis, in this manner of cauterizing, we are not used to it much, due to the frightening appearance of it: and therefore, few are found who will wait on it.
Nevertheless, it is good for him who endures it, and finds a place for it.
The cautery with medicines for the ailment is that you should make two openings on each side of the perforated armillary sphere, through which goes the key of its door from bronze or iron, the length of the wall: whose height in them shall be two knots, or almost themselves.
And let the space that is between both be of the thickness of a finger's joint, and let it be open below and above: and let them contain each other according to this shape.
Then place it on an ointment box, with the weak one lying on the healthy side. And press your hand strongly upon the ointment box. Then pour water between two circles which has been slightly heated by fire and hold it for the amount of an hour: and let the weak one bear the biting of it, and his burning, for he finds the biting as if by fire, until the biting stops.
Then clean your hand with the tool and remove hot water from the ointment box along with sweet water: then let it be for three days.
And place butter on it until the soot of burning is removed: and let it be for some days, and pus will flow from it. It is indeed the last aid.
Then treat it with ointments until it heals.
If the pain extends to the hip or leg, make a splint for him in such a way as you made the splint for an ankle equally.
This is the method of hot water: and I have already written it in the treatise on the correction of drugs. Take alkali and half of unburnt lime: grind both of them well, and put them in a new pot, whose lower part is perforated with a small hole according to the quantity that enters the radius: and place another earthen pot below it: and pour over alkali and lime from sweet water, so that they are submerged by about a finger: after which you press them with your hand: and leave the pot until the water becomes sharp at the lower part of the earthen pot.
Then gather up all that water and pour it over another lime: and boil until it returns.
For indeed it will then be very strong for sharpness, which is administered in many operations of medicine, and in the cauterization of other members. Since it performs the operation of fire itself.
And among the medicines are those with which the anal fissures, and also tes-sie, and honey of cardamom, and lime with soap, so that both are mixed. [Section break]
And Galen himself reported the cure of a certain man from the ancients, who was cured of pain in the anal fissure and sciatic vein: and he praised it very highly. And he said that it does not require another cure, and that he was cured from the disease in one bath, until he reported that perhaps he himself was bathed and came out already healed.
And it is to be taken from green senna: and if not found, dry one may be used, recently prepared: and grind a lot with some fat, and place it on the anal fissure, or thigh, or hip: and bind it, and leave for three hours, or until he feels weak sensation of burning. Then introduce him into the bath (or basin).
When his body becomes hot, introduce him into the bed. For pain retreats, and it heals (or gets cured).
And know that no one should use cautery with these medications unless after evacuation of the body.
And Dioscorides said that the feces of a goat, when it is cauterized upon the sciatic vein, gives it: and it becomes cautery according to this method. Wool is taken, and it is soaked in old oil, and it should be placed over a deep place which is between the big toe of the foot and the heel, and is closer to the heel.
Then take dry feces of a goat, and burn it in fire until it becomes charcoal.
Then place it upon the wool, and let it be until it is extinguished (or quenched). And then repeat this (procedure) again. Do not stop doing that until the sensation arrives over the middle (point), up to the ankle, and the pain rests.
And this method of cautery is named cautery "Vaccinum".
Chapter on Cauterizing Pain in the Back.
When pain occurs in the back due to many causes, either from a fall, or blow, or excessive evacuation, and similar things, from the influx of cold and moist matter: and cauterization indeed does not apply unless in this single manner, which is made by the influx of cold and moist matter.
Therefore, after the evacuation of a sick person with foul pills and similar things, they should be placed on the back where there is pain, three lines according to the width of the palm, after signing them with encaustic in each line five times, or more according to the quantity that comes from the strength of the patient: and cauterization shall be made with cauteriopuncti (cauterizing punctures).
And if you wish, cauterize with three or four cauteries, along with a middle claw cautery, in this manner.
On the method of cauterizing in the beginning of a Hump.
This disease frequently occurs among small children.
And the sign of its beginning in children is that it happens on top of a stridor in breathing during elevation and movement; and you find at the end of the backbone and its knots, which has already begun to emerge above the other vertebrae.
When you see that and wish to do it, then cauterize it with a circular cautery in this manner.
And the cautery should envelop all parts of the vertebrae equally; and if you wish to cauterize around the vertebrae with a pointed cautery, take two or three lines; let the points be close to each other.
Then take care of the place until it heals as previously described.
And be careful not to administer cautery in a hump that occurs due to a muscle spasm.
Chapter on the method of cauterizing in Gout and joint pains.
When joint pains occur from cold humors that are discharged to any part of the body, then when pains occur in the feet, it is customary among physicians to call it gout properly.
When cold gout is being treated with the methods of treatment and the pain does not subside, then cautery can remove them.
And it is to be cauterized after evacuation around the joint of the foot, with many cauteries; and the cautery should be an Olive one.
If it is necessary to make punctures on the face of the foot, then do so with a cautery. If the pains ascend to the knees or other joints, and this often happens, then cauterize it on all the knee with three or four cauteries from every side, using the same cautery of Clavius.
If more than one cautery is necessary for you, then cauterize it. Do not immerse your hand with the cautery, rather let it be about the thickness of the skin.
If pains ascend to the knees and back: then administer what we have said in its own chapter.
If there are pains only in the hands, then puncture around the hinges of the fingers, just like two lines are rolled up.
If there remain pains in the fingers, then puncture them on every knot and on the back of the hand.
If the pain ascends after days to the elbows or shoulders, then cauterize them from every side.
Do not evacuate a sick person from good care, from receiving medications. For if the regimen becomes good and phlegm is evacuated, it will be cured with the help of God using this cautery.
Chapter on Cauterizing in Ruptures.
When a rupture occurs in the groins and the intestine or bladder descends to the testicle, which is beginning: then it is necessary to order the sick man to fast on his own day. And he should use lenients so that the feces will descend from his own bowels.
Then let him sit on your hands upon his back; and command him to hold his breath until it comes out, or a hernia or intestine appears.
Then reduce him with your fingers and mark the place of rupture on his neck, with the sign whose end is like half a circle above the body.
Then apply the cautery of this shape until it turns white and let it drop seeds. Then reduce the intestine or hernia into its hollow place. Then let the servant place his hand on the place so that the intestine does not come out; and you have already opened between the legs of the weak one, and placed a weight there, and another servant is over his legs, and another over his chest who holds his hands.
Then place the cautery on the mark with your hand holding the cautery straight. And hold him until you come to the bone with it; or repeat with another tool if you have not reached the bone with it the first time.
And be careful when the exit of the intestine occurs during your cauterization lest you burn him and it happens over the weak one or death or great harm.
And know that when you do not reach the bone with the cautery, your operation does not succeed.
And it is necessary that the cautery for children be delicate, according to their measure.
Then care for him with the rest of the ointments until he is healed.
And let the weak one lie on his back for forty days until the wound is healed.
And it is necessary that you give him nourishment of the duration of his treatment to soften his stomach so that the intestine does not come out during effort and evacuation.
Then when he wants to get up after forty days, then administer a well-made bandage and let him hold it for another forty days.
And it should be diminished by labor, and filling with food and drink, and vehement voices.
When using this regimen, it is cured with an entire cure.
And I will say the treatment of ruptures with incision in its own chapter.
But if ruptures occur in the remaining abdomen and are beginning, and force does not add to them, then cauterize the rupture with a round cautery according to its size; and let that which is burned be as the third of it from then on. Then care for it, just as we said; no more should be added.
And some of the first have said: that the rupture should be cauterized with a triangular cautery in this shape.
After it is marked with the enkaustrum, and a line is placed that is across its width on the upper side of the rupture, and another line downward. And place your hand in the middle with the clawed cautery.
But the first cautery is easier and better.
Chapter on the method of cauterization for pain due to a fall or blow.
Chapter 48.
If pain occurs in certain limbs from a fall or blow and it persists for a long time and does not help with medicine, then it should be cauterized with the puncture cautery.
And the puncture cautery for every limb should be according to its size and the part affected by it, and its weakness and strength, and the location of the twist, and the pain from it.
If it is cured by the first cautery, it is good. If not: then apply a second cautery to it.
Because by custom the pain of these limbs is, that they are changed from one member to the other which approaches it. Because it is necessary that you follow them with a cautery, until the sick person heals.
On the method of cauterizing leprosy.
Leprosy is sometimes greatly helped by cautery. And especially the kind of leprosy that occurs due to corruption of phlegm and melancholy: when considering the need to cauterize it.
If leprosy is beginning and you have treated it as I said in the division, but it does not subside or stop: then beware of corruption spreading over the entire body of the sick person. Then cauterize him on the head with five cauteries: one in the middle of the head, known as the "fifth spot," and a second below it, facing the forehead at the end of the hairline, two on either side of the horns, and one behind, on the nape of the neck.
And with the last finger of your hand, apply the cautery slightly, so as to make a small impression on the bone, and let the scabs be displaced: to relieve the expiration of coarse vapors from it, and cauterize also the spleen, according to what has preceded.
If leprosy has spread over the sick person and is manifestly apparent: then it is necessary to cauterize with these cauteries that I have mentioned on the head, and with a cautery on the end of the nose, and two on either side of the cheeks, and two on the spondyles of the neck, and six on the spondyles of the back, and one large one over the alhahosos at the base of the coccyx, and another above it, in the same place as the anus: and two more on the hips: that is, one on each hip and two on either shoulder, and two on each elbow, and two on the soft parts of the chest: and cauterize him over all the joints, from the joints of his fingers and toes, and cauterize over every calcaneum of his feet, and the fleshy parts of his hands.
Be careful not to burn the nerves that are above the last heel bone (calcaneus).
Whenever cauterization is performed using a cautery on the ear lobe (pectinus), on the ear (stomachi) and another place (epar).
Know that the more you apply the cautery, it is more helpful and effective.
Know that the sick person does not feel pain from the cautery as the healthy ones do; this is because his body is already anesthetized.
The cauteries should be in proportion to the size and shape of the limbs and joints according to their respective species (types) of iron tools.
Then, care for the cautery by applying powdered herb flour mixed with honey and the rest of the treatment until it heals.
Chapter on Cauterization in Anesthesia.
When a part of the body is anesthetized and treated with medicines, oils, plasters and it does not heal, then cauterize the anesthetized part using appropriate cauteries according to the size or smallness of the member.
Let your cautery penetrate only a little deeper than the skin. Then care for it with an ointment until it heals.
Whenever cauterization is performed for a numbness that occurs in the hand and foot, in the joints of the spine near the nerve exits, which move that member; the numbness is removed.
But do not presume to do it unless you are wise in the study of body anatomy and the exit of the nerves moving the body.
Chapter LI (chapter 62): Cauter
When Albaras (piles) are old and do not respond to any medical treatment; then cauterize it with a deep cautery, according to the thickness of the skin, until the white part is removed and the color changes.
Then care for yourself with the flour of herbs, and with oil of roses, and leaves of arnoglossa, and blood of a dove, and blood of a heron: let each part be one: mix all these together, and anoint them on a cloth, and adhere to the place until it heals.
Method for cauterizing in Cancer.
When Cancer is beginning, and if you want to stop it: then cauterize it with a ring-shaped cautery around it, as it rotates.
But the wise said that it should be cauterized by a last cautery in the middle.
It does not seem good to me: because I fear that it will burn: and I have already seen that many times.
And it is more correct to cauterize around it with a ring, as we said, or with several cauteries.
Method for cauterizing in Adubelati (ulcerated skin).
When someone has Adubelati and it delays in maturing, either due to excessive amounts causing delay or due to the weakened state of an aged person, when there is scarcity of blood, or due to time, and a hurry to mature Adubelati, then cauterize around it with many small cauteries. Then let it be released. For it will hasten with the maturation.
If you wish to perforate it with a cautery, then heat the cautery in fire, and this is its form: (drawing or description follows)
Place it in the middle of Adubelati until it penetrates the skin; and let the cautery be weakened so that the flow of pus may cease.
Then care for it until it heals.
Chapter on Cauterizing in a cancerous growth.
Chapter LIV: (numbering may be off due to differences in numbering
A cancer is not anything other than a walking corruption that devours the member; just as fire consumes dry wood.
If you see a cancer in a place that can tolerate cautery with fire, then use many small and large cauteries according to the location where the cancer is.
Then cauterize it from all sides until you completely remove the corruption and nothing remains deep within.
Then let it be released for three days, and place over the cauterized places sulfur powder with oil until all scabs and corruption are removed.
Then care for it with unguents that promote healing of the flesh.
If after three days you see that fresh flesh is growing in a healthy manner without corruption, it is good.
And if not: then cauterize again over the remaining parts from the corrupted areas.
A cancer is sometimes treated with a sharp medicine. The text arises in the place of cautery.
Nevertheless, cautery with fire is quicker in aid: and I myself have already said the cauterization of it with sharp medicine in division: therefore take it when you need it there.
Section on the method of cauterizing in nails and warts.
Chapter LV.
Often occurs in the lower parts of the feet this disease: and it is a thick, filtered matter that injures the foot.
The cautery indeed is for them in two ways: cauterization with fire, and cauterization with hot water.
As for the one with fire, it should be made convex like a vulture's claw, which is made of iron, in accordance with its size to contain a nail from all sides: and it should have a thin edge.
Then place the heated object upon the nail. Then turn the hand with the cautery around the nail, until the cautery reaches the depth of the nail: and leave it for three days, until it begins to emit pus. Then apply ointment made of forest mints, crushed with salt: and leave the ointment upon it during the night. For this reason, it will be uprooted from its roots.
Then care for the place with an ointment for generating flesh, until it is healed.
If they are not turned around and often occur on the surface of the body, especially in hands and feet: then administer cauterization with hot water: and it is to be noted that you receive a cannula made of brass, iron or vulture's claw: and place it upon the nail or athlete's foot. Then pour a small amount of hot water into the cannula: retain your hand, and you turn it with the compression of your hand slightly, so that the edge of the cannula is pressed against the root of the nail, and the hot water finds its way to the depth, to the root of the nail: and let the patient wait for a short time over the bite of the hot water, for an hour.
Then release it, as the nail is uprooted with its roots.
Follow them one after another until you reach all who are among them in the body.
Then care for them after they have been removed, with that which generates flesh from unguents.
On the method of cauterizing in tremor (trembling or shaking).
When a tremor occurs in a nerve due to cold or quartan fever or something else: then it is necessary that you cauterize it with four or five cauteries on the dorsal vertebrae, and with a cautery between every vertebra, and with a cautery on its chest, and with a cautery on its stomach.
The tremor subsides when it is cauterized with oil, and hastens the health of cold sickness.
Chapter on the method of cauterization by Albucasis.
Chapter LVII.
At times, Albucasis expels foul matter from the body, that is, pustules, which are produced by rotten substances.
Therefore, when they appear, it is necessary to first cauterize over every head of the pustule with a subtle cautery together with myrtle wood, whose tip is burned with fire. Or with the long root of Aristolochia. Or with a lentil-shaped cautery.
And sometimes they cauterize bladder stones, at the beginning of their expulsion according to this method: and they are not increased: and the excess is torn away making them, and it heals from them.
Nevertheless, it must be done after evacuation with bloodletting.
Chapter on the method of cauterization for bleeding from an artery in a wound.
Many times there is bleeding from an artery that has been cut at a wound which happens externally, or at the incision of an abscess, or cauterization of a limb, and similar to these: and it is difficult to separate it.
When this happens to someone, then quickly come with your hand to the opening of the artery and place your index finger on top of it: and squeeze it very much until the blood is compressed under your finger and nothing escapes from it.
Then place in fire small oil-burning cauteries, and many in number: and blow upon them until they become very hot.
Then take one of them, either small or large, according to the wound and place where the artery is severed, and place the cautery on top of the vein, after you have quickly removed your finger: then hold the cautery until the blood is cut off.
If it is pushed out along with the removal of your finger from the opening of the artery and the cautery is extinguished, then take another cautery quickly, from those which are prepared in the fire.
Therefore, do not stop doing that with one after the other until the blood is cut off.
And beware lest you burn the nerve which is there and another mischief happen to the weak.
And know that when blood flows from the artery, then it is not possible to cut it: especially because the artery is large, unless with one of four methods. Or with a cautery, as we have said. Or with extraction, when it has not been extracted. For when it is drawn out, the ends of it contract and the blood is cut off. Or it is tied with a strong thread. Or medicine with the property of cutting off blood is placed on it and it is tightened with a decent ligature.
Whoever administers the cutting off of it with a ligature and tightening with cloth or with things burning and similar, does not completely benefit him, unless rarely.
If it happens to anyone that, and the doctor is not present nor medicine: then begin with the position of the index finger on the opening of the vein as we have said, and with strong constriction, until the blood is surrounded from above by the wound, and over the artery. Do not remove the finger, place it on top with cold water of intense coldness always until the blood freezes and becomes swollen, and then cut it off.
And meanwhile, consider what it needs from cautery or medicine.
On incisions, perforations, and phlebotomy on wounds and similar things.
We have said in Chapter 1 that every disease where burning with fire is appropriate and medicine, its occasions, causes, instruments, and forms of cautery should be discussed.
And there I placed chapters from head to foot.
And I shall proceed in this chapter by the same way: to relieve the seeker of his sought-after thing.
And before I begin that, you sons should learn what is in this chapter regarding the fear that was mentioned in Chapter 1 about cautery.
And for that reason, there should be a greater caution because, during the operation that is in this chapter, evacuation often occurs with blood, on which life depends when opening a vein, or an incision over a boil, or opening of an abscess, or treatment of a wound, or extraction of an arrow, or incision over a stone, and similar things: from all of these, tremor, fear, and death occur in many cases.
And I warn you, lest that happen to you where there is hesitation, for sometimes, when dealing with this art, people like you fall into the modes of weak and frail men. For there are those who get angry with their disease and death is easy for him because of his excessive anger, which comes from his weakness and length of wickedness. And when sickness is from fear which signifies death.
And it is he who gives you his trumpet and tells you with it that he hopes for health, but his illness is fatal.
Therefore, it is not appropriate to agree with him who comes to you from those whose manner is such. And let your caution be greater than your desire and your greed. And do not presume about anything from it unless after certain knowledge, which verifies at your place the praiseworthy result of that to which it has reached.
And use in the care of all your patients, prediction and indication as to what it is appropriate for healing to be attained.
For in that there is help for you in acquiring fame and glory, memory and praise.
May God inspire you, O sons, with his understanding and not take away from you guidance and inspiration, for that is in his hand.
And I myself have arranged this chapter by dividing it into sections according to what preceded in the chapter on cautery, from neck to feet: so that you may be relieved of what you seek from it and what you need.
Chapter on the cure of water that collects in children's heads.
Chapter 1.
Know that this weakness often happens to boys during childbirth: or when the midwife tightens the boy's head without mercy.
And sometimes it also occurs due to unknown causes that are not known.
And indeed, I myself have not seen this illness in anyone other than boys: and to every one of them whom I saw it approached death: therefore it seemed to me fitting to abandon the operation in that case.
And indeed, I myself have seen a boy whose head was filled with water and his head grew every day until he could not sit on himself due to the size of his head: and the moisture increased until he died.
And this moistness, it either collects between the skin and the bone: or it collects under the skull bone.
And the operation on this case, if the moistness is between the skin and the bone and there is a small abscess, then it is necessary to make a middle split in the skull: and the width of the split should be as two knots, until the moisture runs out.
And this is the form of a trepan.
If therefore the moistness is more increased and the abscess is larger, then place these two splits according to this form.
And if the moistness is under the skull and there is a sign of it that you see that the openings of the skull are wide open from all sides: and water sinks down when you press it with your hand towards the inside, and it does not hide itself from you: then it is necessary to make three splits in the middle of the skull according to this method.
And after the incision, remove all the moistness completely. Then tie up the splits with cloths and plugs. Then pour oil and wine over it until the fifth day.
Then untie the knot, and care for the wound with salves and ointments.
And thou shalt not let go of binding the head with equality. Feed the sick person with all dry food of slight moisture until the member is strengthened and healed.
Another method of cutting is that you consider where it appears the size of the abscess, and the collection of water.
Whenever it is more in the occiput, or in the skull, or in the right, or in the left.
Therefore ascend with an incision where it appears to you that there is an abscess and fill it with water: and cut it as far as possible.
And observe that you do not cut an artery, and there be a flow of blood, and the sick person die from that flow with the evacuation of moisture.
Chapter on the incision of the arteries that are behind the ears.
Head II.
When someone has cataracts on the eyes, or on the chest, and it becomes old and medical treatment does not help: then the final cure is more in him, incision of these two arteries.
Therefore, when one wants to cut them, let the sick man shave his head. Then rub the place with a rough cloth, so that the arteries appear. Then let the sick man tighten his neck with any cloth of his. Then consider where the vein pulses. And the places of both are places that are depressed below the ears: and it is rarely hidden, unless in some men.
Then mark with wax both sides: and cut each side with a lancet on both sides, the incision reaching to the bone: and let it be made in the width of the head.
And if you wish, insert the lancet under the artery, and cut it with the incision upward.
Let the length of the incision be about two joined fingers.
For when a vein is cut, blood flows out with a pulsating flow, which jumps to the inside frequently.
If, however, the artery does not appear to the senses, then it is necessary that measurements from the ear determine the quantity of space of three fingers. Then mark with wax and cut to the bone.
And what is necessary to be taken out from blood is VI ounces, and perhaps you may take more or less out of it. The whole thing according to the quantity that appears to you from the strength of the sick person and the filling of the artery of it.
Then consider the wound. Then if something remains on the bone from the wound, then cut it so that no abscess forms hot: then tighten the wound with linens from a linen cloth.
Then care for it with an ointment until it heals.
On the extraction of arteries that are in the temples.
Chapter III.
When an old hemicrania or acute catarrh due to acid, moist humours and heat in the temples occurs, or an old sores, vehement and similar: and it is treated with methods of curative medicine, but it does not help: then we have experience in dealing with these ailments by extracting the arteries from the temples, or cauterizing them, as we have narrated.
The method of operation in extracting them is that the sick person shaves the hairs on the temples and exposes the visible artery in the temple. It is indeed shown to you by its pulse, and it rarely hides itself unless in a few men, or from violent cold.
If it is hidden to you, then let the sick person squeeze his head with any cloth of his, and then rub the place with a rough cloth. Or boil the place with hot water until it appears to you in a clear manifestation. Then take the probang that I have prepared earlier. Then peel off the skin with it easily until you reach the artery. Then thrust a hook into it and draw it out towards the top until you extract it from the skin, and make it come out from all sides of the layers beneath it.
If the artery is delicate: then roll it up with the end of the hook. Then cut off a portion according to the length that its ends will extend and contract, so as to avoid blood flow. For if it is not cut, and if it is not severed, the blood does not rise up deeply.
Then evacuate the blood to six ounces, down to three.
If the artery is large: then it must be tied in two places with a thick thread, strong, of silk or hemp; or with cords made of wool, so that decay does not approach it before the wound is consolidated and blood flow occurs.
Then cut off the excess which is between two ligaments. Do this at that hour, or after another hour.
And if you wish, cauterize it with a cautery to the bone, with a small-bladed cautery: until its ends are cut off, and it remains in place for this same operation.
And it is better work, unless he who is ill has a fever, or his condition is heated. Because the cautery is from those things which aid in ending moisture. Therefore it is better to aid (him).
And after the extraction of the arteries, it is necessary that the place be filled with cooked old linen: and small pieces of freshly made wool should be placed on top.
And after the dissolution (of a wound), it is to be treated with dry medicines which cause flesh to grow, and with linen, until it heals.
If in the meantime while you are operating blood flow occurs from an artery, then hasten to cut it with a cautery, or fill the place with wax: and press your hand until the blood is cut off. If nothing of those things is present to you, then place your finger on the place until the blood freezes. And wet the place with water of intense coldness, until the sharpness subsides and it is constricted as required.
And because the vein which is lighter and easier to extract is to be cauterized with this cautery having two small blades: let the sharpness of the two blades be similar to amalgamated metal. Nevertheless, they are much less sharp than two small knives. Because if they are as sharp as two small knives, frost should be applied to both of them: and flesh will not be cut with speed. When there is a slight thickening [in the body], heat from fire should be applied, and the flesh should be cut off quickly; for this operation is better than any work, and easier, and lighter.
And this is the form of the cautery.
And let the space between the two knives be of the size of a finger's thickness, after you have marked two places with hot iron; place both very hot knives until they reach the bone and cut through the vein in two places: so that what is between its extremities will be removed. For this cautery does not solidify completely.
Chapter IV.
Chapter on the treatment of continuous sharp tears from the eyes.
When tears are persistent and run from the veins on the exterior of the skull at the top of the head: and no healing medicine is applied to them with medicines, and the face of the sick person turns red, and a movement like that of ants is felt on the forehead: and the eyes are exhausted, wet, so much that the hair around them has started to rot due to rotting: and the eyelids have been heated by the sharpness of tears: then the ancients resorted to this treatment for them, and they called it a cure with the knife.
And is it to instruct the sick person to shave the hair that are on his forehead. Then make three cuts on the forehead, each equal in length to the forehead, and let the length of the cut be about two fingers, and one of them should be centered at the middle of the forehead, and the second slightly below the movement of the arms, and the third on the other side: and avoid cutting arteries that are on both sides: and extend your hand from the continuation of the two jaws, and let the distance between all cuts be the width of three connected fingers: and have a piece of prepared sponge or dried cloth ready with which you will absorb blood.
Then introduce a spatula with two sharp ends, which is followed by the following shape: From the first incision that is at the temple, up to the second incision: and scrape with it all the skin that is between the two cuts, including the part above the eye. Then do the same from the middle incision up to the second incision. Then remove the spatula and insert another tool called a sharp scalpel, blunt on one side, but not blunt on the other side, into the first incision again. And this is its form.
And place its sharp side turned towards the flesh attached with skin, and its blunt side turned towards the bone: and push it in until it reaches the middle fissure: and cut off along with it all the vessels that descend from the head to the eyes: except for the incision should be continued up to where it appears on the skin.
Then make this, in the middle fissure until another fissure.
And when the quantity of blood flows out equal, squeeze places from the fragments of coagulated blood.
Then place linen cloth from old cooking on all the fissures and place upon them small lice soaked in wine, oil or vinegar. And see to it that no abscess becomes hot.
And on the third day loosen the binding and administer a large infusion with warm water. Then take care of it with basilicon ointment, and the rest that heal wounds, until it is healed.
Chapter 5.
Chapter on the care of sharp tears and catarrh for the eyes from the inner parts of the head.
When sharp catarrh or frequent and intense occurs to someone, you see their eyes strained, small, and the sight is already weakened: and the eyelids are ulcerated, and hairs fall out from them, and in the deep parts of the head there is acute pain, hurting and sneezing follows: then take the matter that comes from many veins, which sharp catarrh or these conditions do not occur unless from numerous veins.
A better treatment for them is this. And it should be ordered that a shaving of the forehead [should be given] to the sick one. Then make one incision in the middle of the forehead, or somewhat less wide, from the left temple to the right temple; and let the incision reach the bone; and move your hand away from the temples that are moved during chewing until when the bone is exposed; and dry up all the blood with a sponge.
Then separate the two lips of the incision with a heated iron or with scissors made of flax. Then bind them above with thread; and moisten the threads with wine and oil so that no hot abscess occurs.
And when you remove it, and see that the hot abscess is about to burst; then it must be scraped until flesh begins to grow in it.
Then treat it with astringent dressing that promotes growth of flesh; as if you were to take two parts of wheat flour and four parts of colophony; and prepare an ointment from them, and administer it for the growth of flesh in these wounds.
Chapter VI.
[Section on the treatment falling into the ear.]
Everything that falls into the ear is one of four kinds: either a mineral stone, or something similar to a stone like iron and glass: or it is from a plant such as peas and beans: or it is liquid, such as water, vinegar, and similar things: or it is some animal.
When a stone falls into the ear or anything similar to stones that do not grow within the ear and are not added, expose only the ear: if you see a stone, then pour something from broken oil or sesame into the ear. Then administer its extraction and make it sneeze with pepper and poppy seeds placed near the nose when you place around the ear fragments of cloth or wool and stretch the ear upward.
It often goes out (the stone) with this care.
If it does not go out, then administer its extraction with Geista (phenazone), that is, subtle pizigaroli: whose shape is as follows.
If it goes out with geista, it is good.
And if not, then administer its extraction with a subtle blind hook (forceps) a few times.
If it does not go out through that (the blind hook), then make a tube from metal and insert the end of the tube into the ear opening a lot and seal what is around the tube with softened wax so that there is no way for the wind to pass except by the tube: then pull it out with your strong force.
It often goes out (the stone) with what we have said. If it does not go out in this way: then take from helkalimbath or vinegar (acetic acid), that is, prepared gluten, which birds are caught with, a small amount of it: and put it on the end of a radius when you have placed the cup correctly over it: then insert it into the ear opening gently, after you have everted the ear from moisture.
If therefore it does not emerge with all that I have mentioned, then hurry to cut, before a hot abscess or spasm occurs.
The method of lancing is that the bloodletting instrument (phlebotome) should first be applied to the sick person, and then blood drawn from him according to its strength. Then make the sick person sit with his hands in yours, and turn his ear towards upwards, and make a small incision at the root of the ear in the fatty part of it, depressed to that place; let the incision be lunar shaped, until you reach the stone (earring); then remove it along with it, if possible using your instruments.
Then let the incision heal by itself and take care of it until it heals.
If something falling into the ear is one of the grains that grow and swell, then administer its removal.
But if it does not obey to come out by itself, then take a thin, fine probe of this shape.
And administer with it the removal of this kind of grains that fall into the ear and do not do it when you think that the grain is already damp from the moisture of the ear, until you put many pieces (of cotton) on it; then remove them with forceps, or with a fine probe, or by suction as we have said, for its removal will be relieved.
In water that enters the ear, the sick person should cough with it first; and his ear has already filled with some cotton of old age; and it lies on top of that ear where the water is. If therefore it comes out through this (the probe), it is good.
And if not, then take many small, soft, and warm stones about the length of a finger; heat them slightly with fire; and make the sick person insert one from those into the ear canal; and let him throw salt on his foot from that side and strike with another stone on the stone in the ear. Therefore, it should not cease to do that with stone and stone until all water comes out.
And the water now comes out in such a way that you take one from a brazier or from a reed and insert one end into the ear; and light the other end with fire until it is burnt as much as possible. Then take another reed and do this many times until all water comes out; and withdraw it with a cannula as described above in the stone.
In the extraction of an animal entering into it (if it is a small body, like a louse, and similar), care for it as I said in the division.
But if it is of a large body that appears to the senses: then administer the extraction of it with forceps and with hooks; and its removal is easier for all who hold it in the ear.
In the extraction of worms generated in the ear, when you care for it as I said in the division and in the treatment of distillations, and your care does not help: then it is necessary that you look at the ear in the sun. Therefore, if something appears from worms there, then withdraw it with forceps or with fine hooks.
But if nothing appears there, then take a cannula, whose shape is narrow below and wide above; and insert the fine end into the ear according to the size that the sick one can bear; then suck with strong suction. Do this many times until all worms come out.
But if they do not obey you to go out, then wrap the cannula with hops, as I said in the stone.
But if they do not come out with what I said: then administer the distillations that ancient people have been experienced in the treatment of worms; and you will find it in the treatment of distillations.
And let your flow [be] that you pour oil and medicines into the ear with this tool, whose form is depicted here. As you see, make it from silver or bronze, narrow below, with a small hole at the bottom and wide above.
So, let what is within the concavity of the tube [be] made of bronze, well-made. And if you wish, take the radium and wrap its end with a suitable winding; then pour oil or juice, or whatever medicine you desire into the tube; let it be in the ear; then insert the radium with the heated rod on top and squeeze it with moderate pressure until the oil is forced into the concavity of the ear, so that the sick person may feel it inside; and what is poured into the ear, let it already be slightly heated with a little fire; and beware not to pour anything that distills in it extremely cold, for medicines do not tolerate this.
Chapter VII.
[Title] Treatment of Ear Blockage.
When certain infants emerge from their mothers' wombs not pierced.
It also happens to some people that ear blockage comes from a wound or flesh born in the ear.
This blockage sometimes occurs in the deep opening of the ear that is not visible to the eye; and sometimes it occurs near the external opening of the ear that can be seen.
Therefore, that which occurs in the deep part of the ear and is not perceived by the eye, is difficult to cure in many positions.
And in the one that is visible to the eye, it is necessary to place the sick person's ear on the sun and look into it; then if you see the blockage appearing, open it with a fine spatula whose shape is as follows: its end should have a small notch, part of which is acute; and the rest of the spatula should be made of two flat sides to avoid damaging the ear.
If therefore the abscess arises from the flesh within the ear: then hold it with a fine hook and cut it out easily and forcibly until all the flesh is removed.
If therefore the abscess is deep within the ear: then take a fine and slender probe, heat it slightly with fire, and then send it into the ear.
If you should feel an abscess with the symptom that the person is weak and afflicted with hearing loss, make an incision of it easily: and beware lest you wound the nerves of the ear.
Then place linen in the ear according to the size of the opening you have made and wrap it with Egyptian ointment. Do this for several days until you are sure that the wound has healed.
Or take linen and soak it in rosewater, grind cinnamon into powder over it, and use it.
If you see the ear already suppurating: then you must remove the linen and allow it to be covered with another linen soaked in a pot made with rose oil, until the suppuration becomes warm; then take care of it until it is healed.
If, however, there is bleeding: then immerse sponges or cloths in cold water and place it on the ear; and use the remaining treatment that stops the described bleeding by distillation.
Chapter of Altheus on the Treatment of Eyelids.
Chapter VIII.
Those who occur in the eyelids of the eyes are sometimes moist and sometimes dry.
Therefore you must hold them with tweezers or with a hook and cut them from their roots. Then place cinnamon powder over the site.
If however blood flows from them, then cauterize them with a subtle lentil-shaped cautery.
To cauterize them is better after the incision. For many times they return when something remains from their roots. And when they are cauterized with fire, the roots are burned and do not return.
[Section on Treatment of Tumors of the Eyelids]
Section IX:
Often something happens in the eyelids resembling sand in its hardness and stubbornness, and for this reason it is called grain; and it is an accumulation of thick moisture in the upper eyelid and the lower one.
Therefore, the operation for this is to examine whether it is a grain coming out from the eyelid that appears, and to move everything around it, and its removal is easy.
Find then a crack over it in width. Then scrape it from every side with ease until it comes out. Then hang it with a hook and cut (or remove) it.
But if its removal is not prepared for you unless after you have penetrated the eyelid with a slight cut, then it hurts the weak in some way.
If the crack is wide: Then sew it up with suture; and care for it until it heals.
And if it is small, no harm will come to you from it. Oil indeed restores it and fills (or heals) it.
And if the grain is turned towards the inside of the ear and faces the inner surface, then turn the eyelid inside out, hang the grain with a hook; beyond that, you will need an incision, and press it from every side.
If the eyelid is stretched by an incision, then no harm will come to you from it.
Then wash the eye after the removal of the grain with salt water; and care for the place with it so that it heals, until the weak one is healed.
Chapter on the care of eyelids.
Chapter X.
Chapter X. On the care of eyelids. Axirnath is a crust that is generated in the upper eyelid; and it mostly happens to children; and it weighs down their eyes, and they get cataracts at dawn, and they cannot see the light of the sun, because tears flow towards them, and therefore you see them always lying on their faces, and on these they sleep, and their eyelids are always wet under the eyebrows, which have already swollen; and indeed, the appearance of Axirnath is visible to the eye, and when you press the place with your fingers, you feel Axirnath among them.
The method of his operation is that the sick man places his head in your bosom.
Then take a piece of clean cloth and prepare a bandage on it. And make from this cloth a circle according to the size that contains Axirnath in all parts. Place it on top of it and press with your fingers from all sides, so that Axirnath is gathered in the middle of the circle.
Then find in its center the moisture with a spathule penetrating fissures through its length, and let the fissure not be larger than that which occurs in phlebotomy in depth.
Or it is necessary that you find the entire skin until you reach Axirnath, for in many positions Axirnath comes out from the fissure according to the shape of a white butterfly's wing.
Therefore extract it with the cloth which you have soaked between your fingers to the outside. And you turn your hand to the right and left until it is dispersed, and be careful not to add in the fissure, lest you come with a spathule to the eye, and injure it.
If, however, Axirnath does not appear to you at the beginning of the fissure, you shall add a little in the fissure with ease, until Axirnath comes forth. Then extract it as we have said.
Then immerse the cloths in vinegar and water, and place them on the site, and bind it with small stones.
And among men there are those who grind salt and put it into the hollow of the fissure to dissolve what remains from that moisture.
Then care for it until it heals.
If, however, an abscess hot occurs at the site, then care for it with soothing plasters until it heals.
On the ways of the weakened eye, that is, when the eyelid becomes soft and it weeps as it should not.
Chapter XI.
When hairs grow in the eyelids beyond the normal course of natural hair growth and turn grey: then they harm the eye and cause illnesses such as constant weeping, softening of the eyelids, white spots (albuginea), until it leads to the destruction of the eye.
And indeed the weakened eye is treated according to four methods. Or by cautery with fire. Or with sharp medicine, according to what was mentioned in the chapter on cautery. Or the weakened eye is treated by incision and stitching. Or with reeds, according to what I shall say (i.e., as described in the following text).
The head of the weakened eye should be placed in your lap. Then turn the eyelid of the eye with your left hand.
If it is turned (i.e., if the eyelid can be moved), that is good. If not, move the other eye so and if it cannot be moved, insert the point into it (i.e., the eyelid), where there is a thread below the lower part of the eyelid, and let the point penetrate through the thread from above, so that it is close to the hairs themselves, that is, near the edge of the eyelid, where the hairs grow: and pull the thread towards the upper part of the eyelid, and turn it with a spatula.
Then find in the inner part of the eyelid, below the additional hairs, with the spatula penetrating from the greater tear duct to the lesser tear duct (i.e., across the eyelid).
Then pull out the thread, and place a small ball of wool or cloth under the eyelid; then mark the eyelid with hot wax, as if in the shape of a myrtle leaf (i.e., making a dot).
It is necessary that the figure be made according to the size and elevation of the eyelid; since it varies greatly among men.
From these [cases], there are those who need to be cut according to the large size of the eyelid, according to the softening that occurs in it.
Then, when you find the space between two lines which you marked, and begin from the greater lacrimal [canal] to the lesser one, and let there be a cleft nearby the natural hairs, as in the thickness of a radius.
Then insert the hook into one of the two angles of the skin. Then scrape it all [the area]. Then sew together the two lips with thread and a fine needle of wool; remove the blood and make the excess from the threads adhere to the eyebrows, if you wish to do so; otherwise, do not care for it.
Then release the suture and the threads for three or four days; afterwards, take care of it.
And if you wish, let the wound heal without stitching, and take care of it as it dries and contracts. Since the eyelid is elevated during the sealing of the wound and its suturing, but it will be better in the future.
This method of healing was taught by the ancients (Atrebas).
However, there is concern about the patient in this method, and it is from a good procedure, but there is no fear in it.
And another method is also found in Atrebas: it is to mark a figure on the eyelid like the shape of a myrtle leaf, as we have said before.
Then elevate the eyelid with three separated or combined hooks according to the following shape, then cut off what is excessive with small scissors according to this shape, with equal cuts.
If it is not possible for you to hold the hook, and it does not match that [description]: then take a probe with thread, and insert it into the middle of the figure; and insert another thread near the larger tear, and insert a second thread near the smaller tear; and gather the threads equally between your fingers.
Then move your hand evenly with equal elevation; and raise the skin over which the incision is marked, as we have said.
Then gather together the two edges of the wound with a stitch; and care for it until it heals.
If, however, an abscess occurs at your incision or tear: sew the abscess with linen and similar materials from ointments that soothe.
And sometimes even eyelashes may turn over.
Therefore, you must use the method that I have said for the incision; but stitching is more artificial [requires greater skill]. [Section] On the care of the axilla with dogs.
And it should be turned over that eyelash, and you should make an incision in the tear that is inside, as I have said. Then make two dogs or two thin sticks of the same length as that of the eyelid, and their width shall be less than that of a thumbnail; and you have already made an incision at both ends on both sides where you hold the threads.
Then gather both together with delicacy on top of the excess skin from the eyelid, and stitch the two sticks tightly on either side with a strong suture, and leave it for several days. For a constricted skin will die and darken and rot until it falls away by itself.
If it is delayed [in healing], then cut it with scissors. Then take care of her, until she gets well.
When it solidifies, raise the eyelid; do not pluck the hairs.
And this is the shape of two scoops, which you should make according to this figure, and their length and width.
Chapter 12.
On plucking hairs sticking in the eye with a needle.
The operation is to take a sharp thin needle and insert a fine silk thread gently into it. Then tie the ends of it and knot them both with a very thin knot; let the length of the threads be one palm (about 5 inches).
Then prepare another fine thread under it briefly and knot its ends if you wish.
Then the sick person should place his head in your lap and be near the sun so that the operation may be seen; because this is a delicate or minor operation.
Then insert the needle with the silk thread into the root of the eyelid and make it penetrate the eyelid quickly until you draw out the natural hair from above.
Then pull out the hair over the silk thread; and insert the hair into the silk thread; if it is one, or two, or three, do not more than that.
Then pull your hand with it until the hair comes out with the silk thread from the eyelid along with the natural hair.
If, however, the silk thread is pulled out and the hair does not come out with it; pull the silk thread downwards with the thread you have prepared in it, until the silk thread comes out from the upper opening, and you see it with the eye; then pull the silk thread and the thread, and extract both, and close the eye; and leave the closed one for two or three days, until the hair adheres to its place, and a flesh grows over it.
If the hair is short, then either combine it with a long hair from natural hairs and lift it together; or leave it until it grows out some space, and then lift it.
Chapter Thirteen.
When this Alzheimer's occurs in the eye, it is called Leporina.
And this Alzheimer's can be either natural or accidental.
Therefore, it becomes accidental from the congelation of wounds, cuts, burns, and similar things.
The method of treatment is to find that congelation and to separate the lips of it, and to place a linen cloth between them and tie it until it heals.
It is not necessary to use in its treatment things that dry and constrict; for if you do so, the Alzheimer's worsens rather than heals: but rather use softening things, such as flaxseed oil; and a syrup made with vinegar, in which althea has been cooked, along with flax seeds; and an ointment of dyaquilon, which has been melted with some oil; and apply a cloth soaked in it, and treat it with it.
And the storehouse of your treatment is to make every effort not for it to become congeled again, according to its original shape.
Indeed, the operation that we have mentioned is nothing but a correction of Alzheimer's, so that it does not return to its original shape.
On the treatment of Alzheimer's occurring in the lower eyelid, which is a swelling or contraction upward towards right and left.
Chapter Fourteen.
The Alzheimer's occurring below is the one that is truly called Alzheimer's. And it is natural, and it is accidental.
From wound, or fissure, or cautery, and similar things, it becomes accidental.
The method of operation in this is that you take the needle, which should have a double thread, and moisten it with flesh, and make it pass from the left tear duct to the right tear duct until the thread reaches the two ends of the skin.
Then stretch the skin upwards with a needle and cut it with a flat knife. If therefore the shape of the eyelid returns as required, it is good.
And if it does not, take the probe, and put it into the fissure, and turn the eyelid along with it; and cut two fissures on the inner side of the eyelid, and their ends should be from the two corners of the incision, until they converge and form an angle: until when they join together, this shape is formed, and it is a laudable Greek letter.
Then remove that skin to the extent of its lower sharp part, following the eyelid. Then bring together the separated parts: or bind them with a wool thread.
Then care for those (parts) with what I said, from soothing medicines and linens, until they heal.
If al-Khater occurs from the fissure, and suture, or cautery: then it is necessary to cut a flat scar under the eyelashes, even as before. Then separate between two lips with a linen cloth, as I said.
The summary of the discourse on the care of al-Khater, whether it is above or below, is that the operation should be carried out on it according to the preparation for the shape of al-Khater.
The artisan, being prudent, prepares his skill with whatever method is possible for him, until he makes the figure return to a natural form or one that is close to it, and himself being ill, according to what suits him from the operation and instruments in many dispositions.
Chapter XV.
On the adhesion of the eyelid with conjunctiva, or cornea.
Sometimes this consolidation happens to many people, so that the upper eyelid adheres to the white of the eye and prevents it from performing its natural functions.
Therefore, it is necessary that you insert the end of a radius under the eyelid and lift it up; or stretch it with a hook; then cut the adhesion with a subtle spatula, not with the sharpness of spatulas, but slightly blunted; so as not to disturb the sick person during the operation, and remove the spatula, and harm the eye with its sharpness; and let your incision be like you are excoriating that adhesion easily, until when the eyelid returns to its natural form, and the adhesion is healed completely.
Then pour salty water into the eye and rinse it; or drip it onto him from seives made of linen soaked with water.
Then separate between the eyelid and the eye with a linen cloth; and place wool soaked with white of egg on the eye; and use seives made of linen and solidified materials for three days until it is healed.
On the incision of nails and protrusions of skin around the eyes.
Chapter XVI.
You should know that a nail is according to two modes. Or is nerve-like: and it is similar to the hoof, tough, delicate. Or is not nerve-like, similar to frozen white moisture: which, when touched with iron, or when you try to grasp it with a nail, it breaks off and the nail does not take hold of it.
And both kinds do not begin, unless from the greater tear, until it slowly approaches the sight, and stops the light, and hinders the movement of the eye.
And the method of operation for cutting it is: that the weak one places his head in your armpit. Then open the eyes of the one, and lift the eyelid with your hand. Then grasp the nail with a pair of nails and extend it upwards. Then take the awl and insert it into her with a horse hair or oxen or sheep hair; let it be a thread, and bend the tip of the needle slightly, and pierce it in the middle of the nail and sew the nail with the thread and extend it upwards; and scrape with the hair the side of the nail following the pupil, as if you are squeezing it with the hair until the end of its socket.
Then cut the remaining part in the root of the tear with a thin spatula or small forks; and let the natural flesh of the tear escape, so that it does not happen from the cutting of it a constant flow of tears.
And sometimes the nail is extended with the nail alone; or with the thread, as we have said. Then it is scraped with a soft spatula in this form:
And beware that the spatula does not touch the corn layer and causes a crack in it and pierces the pupil.
After the incision, throw something crushed salt into the eye, or made from zinc, and leave it for another day. Then take care of it as necessary, until it heals.
If the nail is not nerve-rich and you cannot insert a probe into it nor set a wedge under it, then this type of nail should be repeatedly treated with these remedies and healed as I described in the division.
If you want to cut it (the nail), then open the eye of the patient and take a fine, soft, weakly sharpened probe, shaped like this. And file the nail from above with fineness. If you see that it is becoming rough and breaks, and if you grind it with the file, then distill hour by hour from zinc made from zinc ore or red pigment, or ground salt into the eye until another day.
Then repeat this procedure until the whole thing is removed. Unless it is a hot abscess in the eye: then leave it alone and treat the abscess until it heals.
Then repeat this procedure on it with a file until it heals.
But if the growth of flesh near the tear duct is harmful to the eye and causes great injury, it should be suspended with a wedge, and cut off that part of it; not at the end, so as not to interfere with the flow of tears.
Then distill red pigment or zinc made from zinc ore into the tear duct until it heals.
Chapter on Albucasis' incision and tissue born in the eye.
Chapter XVII.
A red mass composed or placed on certain human eyes is sometimes born, which covers the pupil, approaches it, presses against the eyelids, and perhaps turns the eyelids outward; resembling a rose bush.
And there is also an operation for placing the sick person's head in your armpit. Then open the eyes and collect all the tissue with suitable forceps; hold it with one forceps or a clamp.
Then cut the flesh first until it is completely finished with the scalpel. Be careful not to injure the eye during the operation; make your cut such that you cut the flesh only, or with a spatula as we described in the chapter on the nail incision, or with small forceps, as used for collecting asbestos, according to the shape it will have after this chapter.
When your cut is completed and all the alguardenici (fatty tissue) has been removed, then fill the eye with salt powder, or drip red powder or similar corrosive medicines into it; place over the outside of the eye a piece of cotton with white of the egg: to protect it from a hot infection.
If there remains some alguardenici or if you have a hot bleeding, and you fear a hot infection, then leave the eye alone, and treat it with whatever soothes an abscess.
Then repeat the operation over it until it heals.
And do similarly with the flesh that occurs in the eye of this kind.
Nevertheless, it is necessary to let strangers treat any weak eye from a natural or accidental way, by working with iron; do not insert your hand into any of these operations until you see that the limb can bear this operation.
Chapter on collecting asbestos from the eye.
Chapter XVIII.
Asbestos are red veins that cover the eye and prevent the operation from being seen; they weaken the eye with the passing of days.
It is necessary for you, firstly, to consider whether the eye where Sebel is, is strong, and if there is no illness in it besides Sebel; then gather Sebel from it.
And you should instruct the weak to place their head in your lap.
Then suspend those veins with one or two needles according to your discretion; let the needle be subtle and doubled in this shape, or let there be two needles graduated in the same body according to this shape.
Then collect those veins with subtle forceps and remove the blood by the hour; until you see those veins separated from the eye and resolved; take care not to harm the eye with the ends of the forceps.
Let your work be at midday before the sun, and let you be very firm during your operation; so that you do not cut except those veins.
And when you have finished, then distill into the eye either green or red; so that its acidity may corrode what remains of Sebel.
If however it is not possible for you to collect all of it in that hour, then plaster the eye with it, which relieves the pain of the eye; and leave it for some days until the pain subsides; and secure it with warm compresses; then repeat over it according to the same method until it heals.
And this is the form of the forceps.
Chapter on the reduction of Arissatum to the nose.
Chapter XIX.
The physician Arisatha treats a Fistula, which he cures with a cautionery or with a medicine burning sharply, according to the narrative that preceded it.
And if it does not heal, then there is no skill in it; except that you may incise above the abscess at its birthplace, and extract all moisture that is in it and pus, until the bone appears.
When therefore the bone appears, and you see in it corruption or blackness, then grind it with this instrument, whose form is as follows:
And it is called Asperi Capitis (Head Grinder).

If the place consolidates, and flesh grows there, and the flow of pus is cut off; and it remains for forty days, and is not renewed, and there is no abscess, and no accident occurs in it; then you know that it has been healed.

Chapter on the reduction of eyelid swelling.
Chapter XX (twenty).
When the eye bulges entirely and no harm or reduction occurs in sight: then it is necessary to dissolve the afflicted one; afterwards apply leeches to him; finally place warm poultices on his neck without incision, but with suction.

Chapter on Incision of the Eye Covering.
Chapter 21.
Chapter 21: When there is a rupture in the eye covering, it then bulges and protrudes beyond the eyelids like a grain of sand, and defiles the human form because of this, and desire to cut it; then the operation on him is as follows: insert a pointed instrument at the base of the eye from bottom to top.
