[Title: On the treatment of Alcomant.]
Chapter XXII.
This disease called Alcomant is not anything other than pus that accumulates in the eye, similar to descending water, and it is not the same as the eye itself.
And the method of operation for this is that you make the sick person sit on a prepared seat or directly.
Then take his head with your two hands, and move it until you see the pus reach the lower parts of your eyes. Then it is shaped, and does not descend, and the sight is purified; and the sick person sees as he saw before; if it does not descend further, know that it is water.
If, however, the descent of pus is not prepared as we have said, then make the sick person sit between your hands. Then take a thin spatula and cut it with it on the corn layer slightly near the junction of the conjunctiva with the cornea in the corona (or crown), until the pus comes out.
When it comes out, then pour warm water into the eye in which you have mixed honey; or hot water in which you have already boiled fenugreek and honey; then treat it with the rest of the treatment until it heals.
On the treatment of water that descends into the eye, or cataract.
Chapter XXIII.
We have already discussed the types of water in division, and what is suitable for piercing when it is declared and explained in speech, then receive the same thing according to health.
Then it is necessary that you make the patient sit between your hands square, facing the light, near the sun; and bind the healthy eye and squeeze it strongly; then with your right hand close the eyelid of the eye in which there is water, or with your left hand if the eye is on the right.
Then take your right hand, if the eye is left: or take your left hand, if the eye is right.
Then place the edge of your right hand near the crown of the eye, on the apparent side of the smaller lacrimal duct within the white part of the eye: then push your right hand with force: and you pull your hand with it, until it penetrates into the white part of the eye: and you feel that your right hand has reached an empty place.
And it is necessary that the measure of the journey of the hand to depth is the measurement of space from the pupil to the end of the darkening: and this is the crown of the eye. For indeed you will see it in the same pupil vision of the eye, because of the clarity of the cornea layer.
Then place your hand up to where there is water. Then press it repeatedly with one blow after another.
If water then immediately flows out, then the sick person immediately sees what is above and opens his sight, and the hand in his eye.
Then remain still for a little while. If water then flows out, then put it aside, but leave the hand to come out.
When it is tightened and does not rise up: then pull out the hand easily: and you slowly withdraw your hand.
Then dissolve something from salt in clear water: and wash the eye inside with it. Then place over the entire eye a piece of wool soaked in rose oil and white thread: and bind the healthy eye with it.
We and those who are of our time place over him camomile powder with white thread of the eye.
If the hand does not obey you to enter the eye because of its hardness, since it is a man whose eye is very hard: then it is necessary that you take Spatule, which is called Alberid, and this is its form.
Perforate therefore only the joint itself and not the tendon; and do not insert your finger into the hole; it is only to make a way to a subtle place.
Insert almagda (an instrument), as we have said previously.
For the completion of your work, prepare for the sick person a suitable sleeping place well made, in which he will lie on his back in a dark house; and let him be prevented from any movement, and from coughing; and place food for him that soothes his nature; and do not move his head to the right or left at all.
And let the bandage be according to its composition until the third day.
Then dissolve it in that dark house, and test his sight; and make him see things. Then return the bandage until the seventh day.
And it is not appropriate to do this at the time of treatment or immediately after cutting; rather, it should be given by others because water rises quickly through a strong wound.
If, however, there arises a hot abscess: then it is necessary to dissolve the eye before the seventh day; and correct this with what soothes the abscess until it subsides; then without his sight, and place on his oral cavity that which regulates his vision for several days, while he remains in that dark house.
Then gradually leave the house, and change into his cases.
And know that a student is not excused from viewing a dissection at times; then he dares to perform an operation.
Now indeed a certain one of those from Alayrach has come to us who said that it was perforated with a large opening in Alayrach, through which water flows.
Therefore, I have not seen anyone in your land who has done that; nor have I read it in any of the ancient books; and it is possible that it is new.
These are the forms of species from Magda, so that they may stand above him who knows them not.
Make them out of bronze; and let their extremities be with the same subtlety triangular and pointed.
Chapter XXIII.
[Section] On the care of a newborn's flesh on the nose.
When there are born in the nose diverse growths, of which some resemble many-footed scorpions; and from it is cancerous flesh, stone-like, dark colored; and from it is soft flesh, not dark colored.
In the soft flesh, not fraudulent, nor cancerous, it is necessary that you make the patient sit facing the sun with his nose opposite it, and open its nostrils, and throw a hook into those growths; then draw them out to the outside, and cut what you have grasped from them with a thin, sharp spatula until you know that all the flesh has been removed.
If something remains from that which cannot be removed: then shave it off with one of the subtle instruments with ease, until nothing remains from it. If blood dominates you, or a hot abscess happens: then apply whatever is necessary; or if it is from malignant abscesses, then hasten to cauterize him until the blood is removed, and all flesh is taken away.
Then pour vinegar, water, or wine into the nose after the incision. If the nostril opens and moisture comes out to the palate, then you know that he is now well.
If moisture does not penetrate as required, then you know that within it is flesh born in the upper bones of the nose, to which the instrument did not reach with the incision.
Therefore, it is necessary to introduce a thread of linen with some thickness and many knots; place between each knot a quantity equal to or less than a finger; make the patient weak, so that he sends out one end of the thread into the nose with the probe, or as possible for him after he has done this, similar to the case of Azer; draw out its smell until it reaches the cavity, and exits above the throat.
And indeed, many times boys make similar to this what Attomus does in schools; and it is easy for him who desires so.
Then place two ends of the thread, one that exits above the nose, and the other that remains in the nose. Then, with scissors, cut the flesh along with the knots that are on the thread. Do this until you know that the flesh is now with the knots of the thread.
Then draw out the thread; place in the nose after the withdrawal of blood linen which you have soaked in Egyptian ointment; do this for three days or more until the ointment has completely eaten away the remaining flesh.
Then, at the end, put a tube of lead into the nose for some days until it heals.
If it requires a cure that dries, use it.
To make the nose cure with what is distilled from olive oil and other medicines into the nose, make it of silver or copper; it should be similar to a small lamp, open like a snail shell, and its passage similarly.
And if you want to make a closed tube, like a reed.
And make the instrument for the head-lance completion, be it full, exposed: to which have a handle at its end, with which you hold it, when you heat oil or what you wish from juices and flexible things in it.
Chapter 25.
Often a boil arises at the end of the nose called Thelul, and it becomes larger and increases in size with days until its appearance is repulsive.
And because of that, it is necessary that you cut it at the beginning of its appearance and remove the entire thing. Then place on that location, either a cautery or a medicine burning in its place.
If its cutting is delayed until it becomes larger, then consider if it is made of stone, hard, dark in color and few senses: then do not touch it with iron, because it is a cancerous boil.
For often I have seen that someone cut an abscess with iron and great harm befell the one who had it.
And if the boil is soft when touched, not dark in color, and you see that it is possible to cut the entire thing, then evacuate the weak, and cut it without fear or hesitation; and take care of the place with it that drains and constricts until it heals.
Chapter 26.
Chapter on sewing the nose, the lip, and the ear.
Know that when there is a separation of the continuity of one of these cartilages, an operation does not have much effect unless in certain people.
Therefore, when something happens to anyone from it, you should consider if it is a recent wound with its own blood: and then apply double stitches on the wound with suturing; then take care of it until it heals.
If the continuity of the solution has already been separated and each part is now healthy: then it is necessary to cure every part from its apparent skin until it bleeds. Then join the two lips with suturing and sew them together, and sprinkle powdered dragon's blood over it along with pulverized opopanax; and place a piece of plaster containing diafinicon on top of the powders, as well as some other consolidated plasters; and leave it bound for two or three days. Then dissolve it, and change the medicine; and let it remain until the sutures have dissolved by themselves. Then treat it with an ointment until it heals.
The method of suturing is to join the continuity of the solution or with needles, as we have said in the suture of the abdomen; or join the solution with a thread, as I have taught you.
Chapter 27.
Chapter on the removal of lip tumors.
Many people have hard sores similar to grains of wheat growing on their inner lips; some of them are smaller and others larger.
Therefore, you must turn the lip over, and make an incision on every tumor of it; and hang it with a hook and cut it from all sides.
Then fill the place after the incision with sulphur until the blood stops flowing.
Then it is scraped with vinegar and the place where the sore is, until the wounds heal.
Chapter 28.
Chapter on the incision of the born flesh on the gums.
Often a mass of flesh grows on the gum that ancient people called abuluss.
Therefore, you must hang it with a hook or hold it with forceps and cut it at the root, and let pus or blood flow out.
Then place over the sore area crushed pomegranate peel or other styptic powders, extractive.
If the flesh returns after treatment (which often happens), then cut it again and cauterize it; for it does not return after cauterization.
Chapter 29.
Chapter on tooth extraction with iron.
When they (teeth) are gathered on the surfaces of teeth from both the inner and outer parts, and between gums and rough cortices, sometimes they turn yellowish or greenish, until that corruption reaches the gum, and the teeth become foul due to it.
Therefore, you should make the patient sit between your hands and support his head in your lap, and grind the tooth and root where the cortex appears to you like sand: until nothing remains from it, and similarly do with blackness, greenness, yellowness, and others until they are cleaned.
If therefore what is within them (teeth) is removed at the beginning of reasoning, it is good: and if not, then you should repeat the grinding process on them day after day, second and third, until finally your efforts reach what you desire.
And know that the tooth needs razors of various shapes and forms, many kinds, according to what is prepared for your operation: because the rasp that grinds the tooth from below is different from the rasp that grinds between the teeth, according to other shapes.
These forms of razors should be prepared by you, which you see.
Chapter 30.
Chapter on the extraction of tooth pain.
It is necessary to cure the tooth from its pain with all your skill, and to be slow in its extraction. For its place will not be supplied when it is extracted: since it is a substance that rises: until there is no excuse for its extraction, then if the patient is forced to extract it himself, he must firmly decide and assure you of a tooth in pain.
For often the pain deceives the patient and he believes that there is saha (a poison) in the tooth and extracts it himself: then the pain does not go away until the diseased tooth is extracted.
We have indeed already seen that from the operation of phlebotomists.
When therefore it is certain that the tooth itself feels hard, then it is necessary to incise around the tooth with a spatula, in which there is something of virtue, until it dissolves the gums from all sides: then move it yourself with your fingers, or with subtle forceps first, little by little, until you shake it.
Then place large forceps there with good positioning, and hold the head of the weak between your knees: what you have already firmly grasped, so that it does not move: then pull out the tooth in a straight line, so as not to break it.
If therefore it does not come out, then take one of those instruments and insert it under it from all sides with ease, and try to move it as you did at first.
If the tooth is pierced or rotten: then it is necessary to fill that hole with a cloth and tighten it with the end of a subtle radius so as not to break it during your constriction on top of it with forceps.
And it is necessary that you are careful when incising around the gums from all sides a lot.
And keep your strength so as not to break it, and a part of it remains, and returns on the weak from that malice which is greater than its first pain.
And beware, lest you do what ignorant phlebotomists do in haste and their own audacity regarding its removal, except that they administer what I have mentioned.
For many times they bring upon men great weaknesses, the more difficult of which are to break and all its roots remain or some of them: or to extract it with certain bones of the jaw as we have often testified.
Then it is to be scraped after its excision with wine, or with vinegar and salt.
If there occurs a bleeding from the places (for it often happens), then grind some alum and fill the place with it; and if not, cauterize it if you have no alum.
The handles of subtle forceps by which the hard tooth is moved should be long at one end, short at the other, thick, so that they do not split when pressed against the tooth; they should resemble the handles of large forceps, until when you press them with them, they do not bend themselves or split: short in length, and made of good iron or well-made steel, straight at their ends: and at their ends there should be teeth, some of which enter into some and tighten by proper constriction, strong.
And sometimes the ends are shaped like the beak of a bird called a ciconia and are strong in constriction.
Chapter XXXI.
Chapter on the extraction of teeth and breaking of fractured jawbones.
When a tooth remains after its extraction and breaks something, then one must put hot oil on the place for one or two days until the place becomes soft; then introduce alum or forceps into it, whose ends are shaped like the beak of a bird called a ciconia. The form of the forceps is as follows.
The ends of them should be shaped like a plane iron or an aliskilfe.
If it does not come out with these forceps, then you must cauterize the root, remove all the flesh and introduce an instrument called a small palanca, whose shape is as follows.
The extremity should be short and rather thick; and it should not be filled (or saturated), so that it does not break.
If the root comes out through that (incision), it is good; and if not, help with other instruments of similar form.
The first form is a triangle at the end, where there is some thickness.
The form of the subtle triangle (or pointed tip).
And with other instruments and tools which have come before (in the process of dental extraction).
Also help with this instrument resembling a large hook, with this form (triangular and twisted tip), having some thickness to avoid breaking; and it should not be filled.
And know that there are many dental instruments; similarly, the other instruments are not counted (or considered), and a skillful artisan, subtle in his craft, finds for himself the tool according to what the operation and the disease itself signify.
Because from diseases there are those for which no ancient instrument was made, due to the diversity of their forms.
If the bone breaks out from the jaw or from other bones of the face, or rots: then examine (or explore) on it in its place with that which suits it among the instruments and forceps I mentioned for root extraction, and help with what is being done, whose form is as follows.
Let there be some thickness gradually, in order to tighten or hold the bone with it so that it does not escape and move away until the bone comes out; and restore the place with appropriate medicines for that.
If there is a small rottenness (or decay) in the bone, then clean it from its own decay, and care for it until it heals.
De curatione alvii et de dentium extractione
On the serration of protruding teeth.
On the treatment of the jaw and tooth extraction. When teeth protrude not according to their natural course, it becomes foul due to that shape; especially when this happens in women and girls, namely, venereal.
It is necessary therefore to consider the following points. For if a tooth is born after another tooth and it does not settle or its serration or cutting is possible, then extract it; and if it is attached to another tooth, then cut it with this instrument, whose form is as follows.
It resembles a small beak, and is made from hard iron with an extremely sharp end.
And your cut should be such that you make the cut over many days due to the hardness of the tooth and so as not to disturb another tooth.
If it is protruding, exposed for serration; then smooth it with a rasp made of hard iron, whose form is as follows.
Let the entire instrument be made of hard iron and its handle have many small pointed teeth like a rasp with which to smooth the tooth gradually over many days with ease, so as not to disturb another tooth and let it fall; then soften it and finally grind it smooth with some rasps.
If the tooth breaks and injures the tongue; then it is necessary to rasp it until the roughness of the break is removed and it is made even; and to smooth it so as not to injure the tongue or corrupt speech.
De extractione dentium eosdemque remediationib
About the winding of teeth with threads of gold.
When there is shock and commotion of the anterior teeth due to impact or accident; and the weak person cannot bite down on what they eat so as not to let it fall; and you have treated them with medicines and bandages, but the treatment has not helped; then it is appropriate for them to be tied with a thread of gold; because silver becomes green and putrefies after days, but gold never changes.
The thread should be of a middle fineness and thickness according to its quantity that it may pass between the teeth.
The form of the rete is such that you take a thread and pass it twice between two healthy teeth; then you weave it with its two ends between moving teeth, either one or several, until you reach with the lance to the tooth of the other side. Then weave the fabric until you reach the part from where you started; and bind your hand with subtlety and wisdom until it is not moved entirely; and let your binding that binds the thread be at the roots of the teeth, so that it does not slip away.
Then cut the excess ends of the thread with scissors; gather both and turn them to each other; hide these under a healthy tooth and a moving tooth so as not to harm the tongue; then release it thus bound until it remains.
If it is loosened or cut, bind it with another thread and let it stand thus for the whole time.
And this is the form of teeth, and the figure of the rete of two healthy teeth, and two moving teeth, as you see.
And sometimes it happens that a tooth or teeth return after loss at their respective places and are retained as we have said and remain; this does not happen unless the skilled and experienced craftsman does it.
And sometimes a tooth is made from the bones of the cow; and it is made like the form of a tooth, and placed in the place where the tooth is braced and bound as we have said; and it remains and serves for a long time.
Chapter XXXIV.
When sometimes a ligament occurring under the tongue is either natural, with which a man is born, or accidental, from a wound that has already healed.
And the procedure for it is to open the weak bone of its head in your pocket, and lift up its tongue; then cut that nerve ligament through its width until it is released from its constraint.
If there is something hard and knotted in it, and it is from the consolidation of a wound; then throw a hook into it, and break through it across its width, until you cut the ligament, and the knot is loosened.
And beware, lest there be a split in the deep flesh, and you cut the artery there, and blood flow ensues.
Then it is rubbed with water of rose, or with vinegar, or with cold water.
Then place linen cloth beneath the tongue, which holds the weak one all night; so that it does not heal again.
But if blood flow occurs, then put on the place crushed lupine seeds. But if blood prevails, then cauterize the place with a lentigo-like cautery, which is suitable for that; afterwards take care of it with the rest of the cure until it heals.
Chapter XXXV.
Sometimes an aposteme occurs under the tongue which resembles a small ranula, preventing the tongue from its natural function; and perhaps it swells so much that it fills the bone.
And the procedure for it is to open the weak one's head facing the sun, and consider the aposteme.
If you see it of a dark or black color, hard, without any sensation to the weak one; then do not touch it, because it is a cancer.
If it is cut to the white part, where there is moisture, then throw in the hook and cut it with a sharp knife, and free it from all sides. If blood seeps out on your operation hour, then place a crushed zegi on it until the blood is cut off; afterwards return to your operation until you pull it out with its whole.
Then it should be washed with vinegar and salt; and care for it with an appropriate treatment until it heals.
Chapter on the treatment of double cheek amygdala.
Chapter 36.
Whenever glands similar to goiters occur near the throat, that is, the two amygdales: which, when treated as we have said, and do not heal, then consider.
If it is a hard aposteme of dark color with few senses, then do not touch it with iron.
And if it is of red color and its root is thick, then do not touch it even with iron, fearing bleeding, rather let it be until it matures. Then either pierce it yourself or it will burst by itself.
And if it is white in color, round and its root is subtle, then it must be cut.
And the operation on it is that you consider before the operation whether its aposteme has quieted down with warm completion or decreased somewhat: then let the patient sit facing the sun, and his head in your lap; and open his mouth and let a servant hold it between his hands; and press the lower part of his tongue with an instrument, whose shape is as follows.
Let it be made of silver or brass, which is thin like a knife.
When you press the tongue with it and the aposteme is shown to you and falls on top of it, then take a hook, and fix it in the amygdale, and pull it out as far as possible, taking something along with it from the tunics.
Then cut it with an instrument, whose shape is as follows. It resembles tweezers; however, its ends should be curved so that the opening of each is directly opposite and sharp: therefore care should be taken that it is made of iron or aluminum treated with resin.
If this tool is not present, then cut it with a spatula, whose shape is as follows. Sharp on one side, not sharp on the other side.
And after you cut one almond [tooth], cut the other one according to this same type of incision.
Then, after the incision, the sick person shall rinse with cold water or with vinegar and water.
If however there is a flow of blood, he shall rinse with water in which the bark of pomegranates has been boiled; or the leaves of myrtle and similar ones from other bitter plants, until the flow of blood stops: then take care of him until he is healed.
And sometimes boils other than the two molars arise in the throat. Therefore cut them equally according to what I said about the incision of the two molars.
And I myself have healed a woman from a boil that had arisen in her throat, which was drawing toward gangrene and had impaired her senses so that she could barely breathe through a narrow opening; and the woman had already been forbidden food and drink; and death was imminent if she had remained for one or two more days.
And the boil had risen so much that it had expelled two branches until they emerged through the two nostrils.
I therefore hastened and tied up one of them with a hook. Then I pulled it out, and a large portion came out with it.
Then I cut it off where it was taken from the nostril.
Then I did to it what came out of the other nostril.
Then I opened his mouth and pressed his tongue; then I tied a hook to the boil; then I cut off a piece of it, and only a little blood flowed out: the woman's throat was therefore healed, and she immediately began to drink water, then she received food.
I did not cease to cut from that ulcer many times over a long period of time: and the ulcer succeeded in the place which I was cutting, until it was prolonged too much and with it that.
I heated (or set fire to) therefore, and burnt the ulcer at the throat.
Therefore it stood firm after adding (something): then I went away from there, and I did not know what God had done with it after me.
Chapter on the incision of ulcers in the throat.
Chapter XXXVII.
When the catarrh descends to the throat and an ulcer forms that is long: then it is called the perpendicular; and if it is large and round in the lower part, then it is called a goitre.
When it is treated with what I said in the division, and the treatment does not work; and you see that the ulcer has become warm and soft: then it should be cut.
And what is gathered round from it, and is not long, and is bloody or dark red or black, and has no sensation: then it should be cut. For there is fear over the weak (person).
Therefore when you see it according to the way I said from whiteness, and its length, to make the weak person sit before the sun; and press his tongue with the tool whose use was previously described; then fix a hook in the throat, and pull it downward; and cut it with one of two tools which I mentioned in the incision of the two salivary glands.
And it should not be cut from it unless what is added exceeds its natural limit without additional treatment.
For if you cut from it too much, you will damage the voice and speech.
Then after the incision, use what was described in the incision of the two salivary glands; and care for it until it heals.
If the patient is afraid of incision: then it is necessary that you use your skill in cauterizing him without fear and cowardice.
The method of cauterization is not other than with sharp water: it is to place the head of the patient on your lap. Then press his tongue with the instrument that I have mentioned. Then take from the water that I have told you in the chapter on cauterization, and make a non-extinguished lump of it, not thick, nor thin, and fill the depression of this instrument with it, which has this shape.
Let the end where the medicine is placed be concave like the concavity of a seashell's edge.
Place the instrument with the medicine on the wound itself: and let the patient lie down on his side so that saliva from his mouth runs out of his mouth with the internal medicine, so that something does not drop from it to his throat and hurt him.
Then hold your hand with the medicine. And you from above apply it to the wound in quantity equal to half an hour until you see it becoming blackened and sedated by the bite of the medicine.
And if you wish to take a hot iron, and wrap it on the end of the ray, and pour the hot iron with the medicine, and introduce the ray with the heated iron into the canal from above until the hot iron adheres to the wound.
Do that often until you achieve what you want in the cauterization of the wound. Then let it go: for it burns and falls away after three or four days.
If you need to repeat the medicine, do so: and after cauterization wipe the wound with a hot iron dipped in butter, and clean it with what is around the wound from the medicine: and wash it with cold water.
And it is treated externally with embrocisions, and internally with gargarisms, until it heals.
This kind of treatment is healthier than incision and farther from fear.
And sometimes the windpipe is also treated with something more subtle than cautery and incision: it is treated with suffusion in this manner. Take calamus, hyssop, origanum, ruta, asafoetida, chamomile, abrotanum and similar herbs from the field: gather them all together, or some of them in a pot, immerse them with vinegar, boil it: the pot should be well coated with clay: and there should be a hole in the middle of the pot, over which a concave instrument is placed in this manner.
It should be made of silver or copper: and the tip, where there is a grain, is inserted into the sick man's mouth until the vapor rises to the windpipe through the cannula, until the windpipe becomes greatly obstructed.
Then repeatedly over it several times, until it burns.
And be careful, not to perform this treatment at the beginning of an abscess's arrival. For it is usually added to an abscess: and it should not be done except at the decline of the abscess's heat.
If this instrument is not present to you, then take a cannula and prepare the bark of an ox's horn at its tip: so that the sick man's bone is not burned: because the ox's horn bark prevents the vapor from burning the bone: and this is from good treatment with safety.
Chapter on the extraction of thorns and bones from the throat.
Chapter 38.
Often a bone or a fish's spine or something else adheres to the throat.
It is necessary therefore that you extract what appears visible on it where vision falls, after pressing the tongue with an instrument in the sun, and it is made clear to you that it is in the throat.
And what is not visible to you and concealed in the throat, it is necessary that you make vomit before the food is digested in the stomach. Perhaps therefore it will come out the attached thing by vomiting.
Or the sick person should swallow a piece of nutmeg, or the root of lettuce, or a crumb of dry bread; or he should take a piece of dried sponge (soft): and bind it with thread, then he should swallow it. When therefore it reaches the place where there are thorns or bone, and it is extracted, then it comes out.
If therefore it does not come out as I said; then use an instrument of lead in this form.
Let it be thicker than a finger joint, and at its end let there be a hollow, which he should introduce into his throat with ease; and let him have the head raised upward.
And let him be careful to avoid touching his epiglottis, so that he does not cough; and push the bone or thorn with it, or the physician may insert it with his hand.
But what the sick person inserts is better: because of his knowledge about the place of the attached thing; and he pushes it downward, or pulls his hand with the instrument upward, all of it according to its quantity that is prepared for him, until it comes out.
Section on Extraction of Leeches.
Chapter 39.
When a leech is treated with what I said in the division of cure with medicines, and it does not function; then consider in the throat of the sick person before the sun, or after pressing his tongue with the instrument that I told you about.
If therefore your sight falls upon a leech, remove it with a small hook, or with forceps carefully handled.
If not possible with them (forceps or hook): then take a concave cane, insert it into the throat of the sick person up to its throat; afterwards insert the hot iron into the hollow of the cane. Do this often: and let the sick person abstain from water all day.
Then let him take an enema full of cold water, and open his mouth in it; and clean his face with it, and drink nothing from it; and move the water one hour after another with his hand. For a leech indeed drops off immediately when it feels the water.
If it does not drop off with what has been said, then fumigate the sick person with bed bugs or with sand in the fumigation of the throat (as described earlier).
Do this often, for it will drop off by itself.
And the method of fumigation is that you take a pot with live prunes and fire; and let the pot be covered with a lid, in the middle of which there should be a hole; and arrange the end of the instrument in that hole.
Then throw the fumigation, and let the sick person place his mouth at the end of the cane, and close it, so that the fumigation does not escape, until you know that the fumigation has reached the leech. For a leech immediately drops off.
If it does not drop off, then repeat the fumigation often.
Let the sick person endure thirst, and eat salt and other foods, but drink no water.
Therefore it is necessary for it to drop off with this treatment.
This is the form of the instrument with which a leech is removed from the throat when it falls upon the eyesight.
The instrument is similar to forceps, as you see: except that it has this curvature which enters the throat. And its tip resembles a bird's beak called stork, where there is the roughness of a file: when it grasps something, it does not let go of it entirely.
On the opening of abscesses, their incision, and treatment in general.
Chapter XL.
The species of abscesses are many, according to their recollection, that is, one and one within this book: and they differ in the perforation of them, and cutting of themselves by two methods.
Of these, one is a species of abscess within itself, and it is grasped from humidities.
The second method is due to the places where it occurs from the body.
Since a tumor occurring on the head is different from a tumor occurring in the anus: and a tumor occurring in a fleshy place is different from a tumor occurring in joints: and each of them has its own judgment according to the operation.
And from tumors there are those which should not be pierced unless after the ripening of pus in them, and the completion of it: and there are those which should be pierced while they are raw, and do not ripen according to the completion.
As tumors which are near joints.
Since a tumor which occurs near a joint, and prolongs itself until it rots what is around it possibly corrupts the ligaments or nerves of that joint, therefore it is the cause of the limitation of that member.
Or it is a tumor near the main member: since if you delay piercing it until it ripens, it will harm either that member or through the main member.
Or it is near the anus, then pierce it while immature: and it is not necessary to pierce a raw tumor, not completed digestion, unless it is near the anus, so that it does not rot deeply, and extends to the interior of the anus, and becomes a fistula, or becomes at its end which does not heal.
It is necessary that you know the hour of piercing the tumor, which has ripened according to completion: and it is in sedation of pain, retreat of fever, and decrease of redness, and pulsation, and acuity of headache of the tumor: and the remaining signs.
And it is necessary that you make the same incision in the lower place of the tumor, and more prominent: and the incision should be going in length of the body, if tumors are in parts of hands and feet, and places of arms, shoulders, cords, nerves, arteries, and finally in all places equal to those where there is no reflection.
In those (things) that are reflected, proceed with a perforation according to that member.
If the abscess is in fleshy places, it is better to delay the perforation until its digestion is confirmed, as we have said in fullness.
Because if you perforate it before that, the course of the virus from it is prolonged, and there are many filths and impurities, and perhaps its edges harden and its depth increases.
Some abscesses are to be perforated according to the width of the body in necessity, or according to that part where a member is needed.
And it is necessary that you administer small perforations to small abscesses, and large perforations to large abscesses, or many sections according to the similarity of the size of the abscesses.
And among abscesses, there are some in which the skin should be concaved: and cut when it has become like a cloth and made at the end that is already dead, as happens often with buboes and scrofula.
And among these (abscesses) there are some which are to be cut by a section having three angles. And from these (abscesses), one is to be cut like the figure of a myrtle leaf.
Like an inguinal abscess.
And among these (abscesses), there are some in which a round incision is administered and a crescent-shaped incision, and similar ones from sections.
However, that which has no head, such as superficial lenticular abscesses, it is necessary to perforate it by a shallow perforation or only superficially.
And it is necessary that when the abscess is large and has collected a lot of pus, you perforate it so as not to expel all of the pus at once during that hour; rather, extract a part of it from it. Then open the boil until another day. Then draw out something from the pus again.
Do it often according to the degrees, until it is expelled: especially if the patient is weak or of poor vitality, or a woman who is pregnant, or a young child, or an old man in decay: for the animal spirit is many times resolved with the discharge of pus: and perhaps the sick person may die, and you will not benefit.
Be therefore very careful about this chapter.
And after your puncture, which you make on the boils, it is necessary to clean the wound: and reflect upon it. If the wound of the boil is small, or the incision is flat, then apply linen cloth or an old bandage. And if the boil is large, and there are many cracks or openings in it, then you should insert linen into every crack until they meet on the other side.
And if you have cut off a piece of skin from the boil, or hollowed out its surrounding area: then it is necessary to fill it with an old bandage, or as when fabric is woven, or shorn of linen wool without moisture: and tie it up for three days.
Then expel it, and care for it with what is necessary from the ointment, until it heals.
If however bleeding occurs during your operation, then administer cold water and vinegar, after it has been absorbed by the cloth: and place it on the site of the bleeding many times.
If the bleeding continues, then it is necessary to administer treatment and care, and powders, as I have mentioned in many places of our book, and by division.
If it is winter time, and the site of the boil is near many nerves: then it is necessary to pour powders with wine and warm oil on them, and place them on the areas.
If it [the wound] is during summer and the places are fleshy: then it is necessary that you place lice soaked in water, or oil, or in wine and oil, and all of that cold. Until the third day, as we said before, then it is necessary to dissolve the abscess, and remove it, and administer for its healing what is suitable for it until it heals.
This is therefore what is universally necessary in the knowledge of abscess treatment.
In fact, regarding the method of distinguishing [the type of abscess], as I have said about every abscess, how the way to treat it is done step by step has been set out individually.
Chapter XL (40).
Chapter on incision of abscesses occurring on the skin of the head.
Small abscesses occur on the skin of the head, and are of the kind called knots, which are contained by the membranes that are sacs for them: they are as if they themselves were poulticed by chickens.
And their [the abscesses'] kinds are many.
Among them [the abscesses] are fat ones: and among them are those that contain a moisture similar to mud: and among them are those that contain a moisture similar to roasted and poulticed things: and similar to these, and among them are hard stone-like ones.
And in the incision of all [abscesses], and their removal there is no fear, as long as it does not make a contradiction with an artery at its incision.
And the operation in their [the abscesses'] incision is that you try it with the tool whose shape comes later, which is called "Intromissum", until you know what it contains.
For if it [the abscess] contains moisture, then cut it with a longitudinal incision according to the superficial section of this shape.
And begin with a cut along line b to line g. Therefore, when the moisture is evacuated, then scab over the cyst that contains that moisture, and do not allow anything to remain deeply within it.
For many times, if something remains in it, it will return.
Then immerse the wound in Egyptian ointment if it is present; and if not, in water and salt; and fill the wound with it and leave it until another day. For it eats away what remains from the cyst.
Then repeatedly apply Egyptian ointment on the wound twice, and thrice, and as much as needed, until you are sure that nothing remains from the cyst; then take care of the wound with the ointment until it is healed.
If the boil contains a thick knot: then cut it in this shape, with a cross-like incision; and insert probes between the folds of the incision, and scab over it from all sides; and strive for your strength in the extraction of the membrane that contains it.
If an artery opposes you, then do what I will tell you later.
And similarly do for a boil that is hard (or solid), through incision and the same treatment, as we have said.
Incision on a hard (or solid) boil is easier because there is little blood and moisture. Sometimes there are such boils on the head of some people where there is no deep moisture.
This is: because I have made an incision on a woman's old boil on the head, and found the boil to be as hard and solid as a stone, rough, white, which could not be broken; and if anyone struck it with force, he would wound himself.
In other cases of boils in the head, except for those boils that occur in children's heads and near the roots of ears, a section of all of them should be a surface cut.
Always make a perforation from below their part (boils) to alleviate the course of pus towards lower areas.
Then, care for this (the wound) with whatever is suitable for it in terms of treatment.
Section on the Strangulated Hernia in the neck.
Chapter XLII.
These boils often occur in the neck and under the buttocks, and sometimes they occur in other parts of the body.
Above these (boils) that occur on the neck are one and many; they originate from one another; and every strangulated hernia among them is within its own sheath, as is the case with knots and boils of the head, as we have said.
And the types of these (strangulated hernias) are many. For among them there are those that are stone-like; and among them there are those that contain moisture; and among them there are malignant ones that do not obey treatment.
In the good one that you see among them, whose manifestly close to the skin color and moves in all directions, and is not attached with the neck muscles, nor with the buttocks, nor with the artery, nor deep; it is necessary to cut it through a surface cut from its upper part to its lower body part along the line b to the line g. And scrape it off from every side: and spread the two skin flaps with a scalpel or multiple scalpels if necessary, as we have said for boils of the head, and remove it gradually.
And it is advisable to be careful not to cut a vein or nerve.
And let the lancet not be very sharp: so that it does not cut your hand with the incision, or disturb the sick one, and you shall incise what is necessary.
If you cut a vein or an artery, or it prevents you from operating, then place in the wound alum powdered, or certain powders that absorb blood, and tie the wound, and leave it alone until the sharpness of the abscess subsides and the wound becomes soft: or if it begins to rot.
For the blood is withdrawn, cut off the tunica. Return then to your operation until you have finished.
Then examine with your index finger if there remains anything of the Strophulus (sutures) or small ones: therefore cut them and clean them.
If there is a large vein in the root of the suture: then it must not be cut from its root; instead it must be tied with a strong double thread and left until it falls off by itself without harm.
Then fill the wound with old linen cloth that you have previously soaked in Egyptian ointment. Then take care of it (the wound).
If the suture is cut off completely, then the wound edges should be brought together: and sew it immediately, after you see that there is no superfluity remaining.
If you see that there remains superfluity due to the size of the suture, then it must be intended to cut off its root and extract it: and administer the suture as I have said.
And what contains humidity among the sutures, perforate it with a superficial perforation: so that the place of its maturity appears to you: and place the perforation from where it follows below the body, as I have said.
Then administer after perforation linseed with ointment, and similar ones, to corrode what remains from corruption, until when you see the wound already clean: then care for it with regenerative flesh ointment, until it heals.
Chapter XLIII.
On section of Epiglottis due to gangrene occurring within the throat.
The ancients spoke of this section in the Epiglottis, and I have not seen anyone in our land who has done it; this is their writing.
However, in those with synanchema (a type of choking), it is necessary to avoid section of the Epiglottis: because no benefit arises from it, for all veins and lungs are weakened.
However, in those who have a hot gangrene in the mouth, or throat, or both molars, when there is no discomfort in the nasal cavity, it is necessary to use section of the Epiglottis to escape from the danger that arises due to suffocation.
Therefore, when we wish to do that (section of Epiglottis), it should be done under three or four rings of the Epiglottis, with a small section along its width, in the place between two rings by quantity, which is the section in sifac (a cartilage) not in cartilage: and this place is suitable for section because it lacks flesh, and the blood vessels from it are distant.
If the physician is afraid, then it is necessary that he stretches the throat skin with a spatula. Then divide the skin until you reach the nasal cavity: avoid blood vessels if you see anything from them.
Then cut the sifac as we mentioned: and it is signified by the phlegm that comes out of it, with what breaks open, and separation of the voice.
Let the open wound heal at some time.
When the hour is removed when fear of putrefaction exists, bring together two lips of the wound skin, and either that alone without cartilage.
Then administer medications that cause flesh to grow until it is healed.
Says Albucasis. The sum of this discourse which I have told is an explanation only when it appears that one of these abscesses has already opened the throat of the sick: and he is raised up on death, and wishes to be cut; they go to the Epiglottis to breathe, so that the sick person may breathe over the place of the wound by a certain breathing, and be saved from death: and for this reason they commanded to let the open wound, until the malignancy of the disease is consumed, and the malignancy of it is for three days and almost as if itself: then therefore they commanded to sew up the wound, and care for it until it is healed.
And that which I saw myself is that a maidservant took a knife, and sent it into her own throat, and cut a part of the windpipe.
And I was called to treat her, and found her to moan, as is the moaning of the dead.
I then uncovered (the wound), and found blood that had come out from the wound to be little. Therefore I was reassured that she had not cut the vein nor artery: and wind came out from the wound.
I therefore approached and sewed up her wound, and cured it until she was well: and nothing happened to the maidservant, except a hoarseness in her voice: and she returned after days to a better state of health.
Therefore I say: that there is no fear in cutting the Epiglottis.
On the operation for hernia of the neck (of the intestine).
Chapter XLIIII.
This is called a hernia of the neck (gutturis), which is a large abscess, according to the color of the body; and it occurs in women much.
It follows two ways: for it is either natural or accidental.
In the natural, it certainly is not a congenital condition.
The accidental (one) is of two types: one of which resembles fatty nodes. And the second type, it is similar to an abscess which occurs due to the knotting of an artery. And there is fear (risk) involved in it, and it should not be presumed to cut it with a knife unless it is small; examine it and investigate it using a probe. If you find it similar to a fatty node and it is not suspended with any veins; then cut it off as knots are cut off, and extract it along with what contains it from the cyst, if there is one in the cyst; and if not, then explore the entire area thoroughly. Then care for the place (area) with what is required for healing, until it heals.
Chapter XLV.
Chapter on Surgery of Nodes.
There are many kinds of nodes, and I have already said all their species in division; it is necessary that I here explain the difference between a node and an abscess, as there may be doubt about it.
Therefore, when an abscess is present, there is heat, fever, and intense pain, until the boiling of excess fluid subsides and the putrefaction is completed; then the fever and heat subside.
A node, however, is not accompanied by heat or fever or pain; it contains them in a cyst or sac proper to them, which is of the color of the body; and it develops like a chickpea (cicer) or a pouch (batecha), and it can be large or small.
And they are according to two types: either fatty; or containing moisture. Colors of moisture are many, as I have said in the division.
Therefore, when you come to the treatment of a Node, it is necessary that you examine it first and investigate it with the instrument called Probe, according to its form which will be found in the chapter following this.
The method of investigation for boils and all nodes is that you take this instrument, and insert it into the moist place which you find in the boil: and you rotate your fingers with it gradually until you know that the instrument has already penetrated the skin. Then, place your hand on it according to the measurement of the size of the boil.
Then remove the Probe and observe what comes out with its trace.
If moisture flows out running with any color, then cut it off by a superficial incision as I said in the other boils.
If no moisture flows out with the trace of the Probe, then you will know that it is fatty; cut off above it with an incision in the shape of a cross as I taught you: and peel the skin from all sides with ease: and protect the box if possible on top of it to draw out the healthy one along with the Node.
If the box bursts during the operation and it is not possible to draw out the healthy one, then remove it in pieces until there remains something from it.
For if a little or much remains from it, the Node returns most frequently.
If it overpowers you and a little remains from it: then fill the wound at its completion with some corrosive sharp powders: and tie the wound, and place hot on top of it where the boil sits and cure it with the rest of the treatment until it heals.
If therefore it is a large knot, then its two folds (or lips), and take care of it along with what surrounds it as it becomes inflamed.
If it is a pulsating vein or non-pulsating vein for you: then approach (the area), fill the place with linen cloth, and leave it compressed for two or three days until the wound rots and the boiling of blood subsides; afterwards return to cut what remains from the knot.
Chapter XLVI.
Â§ On the tools for cutting and piercing (incision and perforation).
There are forms of probes, and there are three kinds.
Among them is the large one, among them is the medium-sized one, and among them is the small one.
Let them be made of iron in a square shape at the ends properly, so that they can quickly enter into the cavity (or incision).
And these are the forms of probes, and noses (or perforating tools): one of them is called a beris, which means piercing; they are three kinds.
Among them is the large one, among them is the medium-sized one, and among them is the small one.
They come together to be inserted into cavities (or incisions), and for emptying out boils and fistulas, and abscesses that are between the bones.
And others are round, smooth, and flexible, such as the large needles that are used for sewing; they are made of citron (wood), or brass, iron, or silver.
The better ones are those which are made from citron (wood).
And probes are also made of black lead, which come together to be inserted into the concave part of the fistulas so that they can be reflected with their smoothness along with those reflections.
They are again three kinds. Because among them are long ones, medium ones, and short ones, according to the quantity of the fistula's or constriction's width.
The forms of veins, and there are many species.
Because among them are simple ones, that is, those with one opening; and there are three species as you see, Large, Medium, and Small.
And among them are blind veins; and there are three species.
And among them are veins having two openings; and there are three species of these: and among them are veins having three openings; and there are three species of these; and all of these are necessary in their place.
And these are the shapes of scalpels, with which knots and swellings are cut and scraped; and there are three species: because among them is large, medium, and small.
The extremities by which the section is made are sharp, other extremities are not sharp; and they are not placed thus except for assistance in scraping knots near fear of vein or nerve incision; and so that the weak may be healed by it, and find temporary relief from the heat as found during the scraping of swellings.
They are made of copper and are similar to a syringe with which alcohol is made; and at the wide end there is a hidden hole called Spatumilis; and it runs inside or outside as desired, as you see.
The form of the Spatumiliums hidden among the fingers for perforating swellings; and these are not taken by the sick; and there are three species, large, medium, and small.
The shapes of the Ventosarum with which blood flow is cut off; and there are three species, large, medium, and small.
Make round ones from copper or brass, slightly shorter in length as you see, and let them be delicate.
These (species of) ventosas should be large and small with you, so that you can cut blood quickly in case of need, and then when there is no medicine present for you.
However, do not use them (ventosas) for the cutting of blood in every part of the body, and do not use them except in fleshy places: such as arms (lacerti cruris), thighs (coxae), arms (lacerti brachiorum), breasts (mammillarum), abdomen (uentris), groin (inguinum), and similar (places) from fleshy parts, wet.
And sometimes they (ventosas) are made into small instruments similar to the fists of boxers, according to their shape, with which blood is cut when it flows from the site of phlebotomy or incision of a vein or artery; and sometimes they are made round in this shape.
Chapter XLVII. (47)
Chapter on the care of human breasts, which resemble the breasts of women.
Sometimes the breasts of some men swell during sleep (that is, when they begin to become dirty in sleep), until they resemble the breasts of women and remain as foul wounds.
Whoever dislikes this (condition), let him cut the breasts with a lunar incision, according to this shape from line 'a' to line 'b', and then scrape off all the fat 'g'. Then fill the wound with a healing ointment. Then gather two lips of the wound with suture and take care of it until it heals.
If the breast has descended towards the lower part and softened due to its size, as happens with women; then it is necessary to open it in two upper sections like a lunar incision, each of which contains the other at their ends so that the larger line encloses the smaller, according to this shape from line 'a' to line 'b', and then scrape off the skin between the two lips, remove the fat, and apply what has been said about suture and powders necessary for healing until it heals.
If however you do not close the incision as required because of the restlessness of the sick, or because of bleeding: then it is necessary that you fill the wound with a linen bandage soaked in a corrosive ointment, and leave it until it corrodes what remains of the fat. Then care for it until it heals.
On the Perforation of an Aboarted Boil, which happens under the armpit.
Chapter XLVIII.
These aborted boils which occur under the armpit are of the type of cysts that contain coagula, and among them are those containing liquids.
Those which contain liquids should be opened by a lunar incision according to this form, from line b to line g. When everything within the abscess has been evacuated through draining, then fill it with an old linen cloth and leave it until the next day.
Then remove the linen cloth, and treat it with a suitable ointment until it heals.
If the abscess is of the type of knotty cysts, then cut it open as we said regarding incision on cysts equally.
If the wound extends so as to emit pus, then administer cautery to it, according to what we said regarding cautery in the preceding section.
Chapter XLIX.
On incision of an abscess which occurs due to an artery and vein.
When an artery bursts and the skin above it thickens, there often results an abscess; similarly, a vein can also break, causing an abscess and swelling to occur in it.
And the signs by which an abscess and swelling are recognized as being due to an artery or vein are: because when the abscess is due to an artery, it is long and aggregated in the depth of the body; and when you press the abscess with your fingers, it feels like a grating sensation.
That which is for the Vein, is round in the evident body.
And the incision above this abscess is an error, and particularly so when it is under armpits, groins, neck, and in many parts of the body; and it is very large. Therefore, care with the iron should be avoided from it, and what is also on its extremities, or in the head, should be avoided.
Therefore, over that which is due to the swelling of the artery opening, find an incision in the skin in length. Then open the incision with scissors, afterwards the artery; and free it from tunics until it is exposed.
Then insert the point beneath it and make it penetrate to the other side, and tie the artery with double thread in two places, according to what I taught you regarding the extraction of two arteries that are in the temples.
Then prick the place which is between two ligaments with a lancet until all the blood that is in it flows out, and the abscess is solved.
Then administer a treatment that generates pus until the ligaments fall; afterwards take care of it with appropriate ointments until it heals.
If the abscess is due to a vein incision, then you must hold with your hand what you can from the abscess with the skin. Then insert the point beneath the place you held with your hand, and make it penetrate; and let there be a double thread in it until you draw it out from the other side. Then tie the abscess with a good ligament; according to what I told you regarding a vein ligament, from two parts with two ends of the thread.
If you fear that the thread will be drawn out, then insert another point with another thread under the entire abscess near the incision; press and tie your threads in four places.
Then cut the aphthmoma (boil or abscess) in the middle of it, until what is inside comes out; then cut off the excess skin and release what is bound from it.
Then place upon it the louse which you have submerged in wine and oil. Then administer the treatment, which is made with linseed and ointments, until it heals.
Title: Chapter L.
Chapter on an aphthmoma (boil or abscess) that occurs from twisting of the nerves.
As an aphthmoma (boil or abscess) occurs in the artery and vein, similarly it occurs in nerves; this occurs by blow or excessive labor, and similar causes; and it happens most often in places of joints, such as the heel or any place where joints move; and the aphthmoma is severe.
It resembles the color of the rest of the body and is in several dispositions without pain; and when it is tightly pressed with great force, it feels weak, like numbness.
And the aphthmoma is not aggregated in the deep parts of the body, rather it is under the skin; and itself moves to all parts, and does not go to the front or anterior areas, nor to the rear or posterior areas.
What is present in the joints, therefore, should not be penetrated with iron. Perhaps it will occur that constriction (occurs).
In that which is present in the head or forehead, incise the skin with a lancet. If therefore the aphthmoma is small, then hold it with forceps and cut it off from its root.
If it is large, then suspend it with a hook and scrape it; then remove it, and make an ulcer with suture; and treat it until it heals.
De sectione apostematis, quod accidit
On the section of an abscess, which occurs in the belly.
Chapter LXI.
The root of them is subtle, and their head is coarse, and their lips are turned back. And there is something small among them, and there is something that is greatly magnified among them.
And I myself have seen a man, and within his belly there were two growths which resembled other fungi more than usual: they were not distinguished by any whiteness or small root; their lips turned back and closed up, and moisture ran out of them constantly.
I therefore cut them, and found that one weighed about 8 and 8 ounces, and the other about 6 ounces. The operation in cutting them is as follows: you should consider whether the person is weak and moist, and the growth is white, soft, with a subtle root: then you should cut it with a broad spatula, and have cauteries ready for use in your presence.
For many times blood is often expelled during the cutting of it: therefore be careful if you are overpowered by the blood, then cauterize it.

If the growth has a thick root, then there is some fear and trembling in cutting it out; this is especially so when it is in the belly.

Chapter LII.
On the care of umbilical hernia.
An umbilical hernia occurs for many reasons. Or it arises from fissures (of the abdomen) that are above the belly; and (the hernia) comes out of it either an althub (intestine), or the intestines, according to what happens in other ruptures. Or it arises from blood that flows out of a vein, or an artery, according to what was stated before. Or it arises from a distended belly (obstruction) in it.
If, however, it is due to a fissure (of the abdomen) and an outlet for urine; then its color is similar to that of an aposteme; it is loose, without pain; and it appears in various positions. And if it is due to the protrusion of the intestine, then its position is, with what we have mentioned, of more violent diversity. When you press it with your fingers, it is hidden; then it returns and perhaps there is a sound; and it expands greatly at the entrance of the bath, and the pain is intense.
But if it is due to moisture, then it is flaccid; therefore, when you press it with your hand, it does not hide, nor does it tighten up, nor does it swell.
If it is due to blood, then with these signs appears an abscess darkening from the hernia.
But if it is due to a born flesh: then the abscess is heavy, large, hard, and punctured according to its size.
If it is due to windiness, then when touched it is flaccid.
And the operation on it is to consider then whether the protrusion of the navel is due to blood from an artery, or vein, or windiness; then it is necessary to forbid its treatment. For in it there is fear and dread, as I taught you in the chapter where I said that abscesses due to an artery and a vein.
If the protrusion of the navel is due to intestine, or hernia: then it is necessary to command the weak one, that he holds his breath and stands stretched out. Then mark with the brand around the entire navel. Then command him to lie on his back between your hands. Then surround with a broad band around the navel over the place which you have branded with fire. Then extend the middle of the abscess to above with a large hook. Then bind him around tightly with thread or cord from strong silk; and the knot of the ligament should be loosened.
Then open the extended middle part of the abscess above the ligament. If you find it (the foreign body) already caught by the ligament: then extract the cauterized one, and insert your finger into it, and push the intestine towards the inner part of the abdomen; if you find a stone, then take it with a hook, and cut off its superfluous part.
If, however, an artery or vein is encountered, then surround it much. Then return to your surgery (procedure). And take two needles and insert strong threads into them; and insert the needles into the stitch you made around the abscess in the manner of a cross, which you make pass through.
Then suture the abscess in four places with the needles; and if you wish, remove the needles and leave a gap until the rotten flesh extends itself and falls off on its own; or cut it when it becomes soft and rots.
Then take care of it with whatever is appropriate from the unguents until it heals.
If the projection of the navel is from the raw flesh or moisture in it, then it must be hollowed out, as we have said. And you extract blood or moisture that you find in it.
Then take care of it to heal the place.
Title LIII.
Chapter on the treatment of cancer.
We have already said about the species of Cancer in division, and how to cure it with medicines: and it should be avoided when curing it with iron, so as not to ulcerate: and we have said that Cancer is generated in the matrix, and warned against cauterization of its cure.
And the ancients said that sometimes Cancer is in a place where its removal is possible; such as Cancer in breasts or hips, and similar limbs, to be removed completely: especially when it is just beginning small.
But when it becomes ancient, and is large, it should not be approached.
For I was not able to heal anyone from that; nor did I see anyone before me who succeeded in reaching it.
And the operation on it, when located as we said, is to precede and release a weak person from black cholera several times. Then, if you find phlebotomy itself with obvious congestion.
Then prepare the weak one with a preparation in which the operation is to be performed.
Then thrust the awls that fit into Cancer. Then hollow out Cancer from all sides with skin, according to the examination, until nothing remains of its roots: and let the blood flow, and do not cut it quickly, rather press out the places, and remove all thick blood with your hand, or as possible there with instruments.
If on the other hand, a flow of thick blood from an incision in the artery or vein opposes you; then cauterize the vein until the blood is cut off. Then cure Cancer with the rest of the treatment, until it heals.
[Chapter] On the care of Hydrophobia.
Chapter LIV. We now describe the division of Hydropisis species, and how water accumulation occurs; and all signs of each species, and its cure along with the medicines.
And that which is cured with iron, is only the species of asclitis; it does not approach with iron the species of timpanitis; nor deeply with the species of hyposarcae; for it is deadly.
When you have been treated for this species of Hydropisis with medicines and the treatment did not help: then consider it. For if the patient has already come to weakness or there is another illness with it besides Hydropisis, such as a cough, or diarrhea, and similar ones: then beware of treating him with iron; for it is dangerous.
But if you see a patient who is overflowing with strength and there is no other illness with it besides Hydropisis alone, and he is neither a child nor an old man: then the method of operation in him is that you lift up the patient standing between your hands, and the servant following behind him presses his abdomen with his hand to drive water towards the lower part of the chest.
Then take a pointed spatula, in this shape. Let it have two sharp parts, long, and pointed ends like a spatula. However, there should be something of shortness in it, so that you do not penetrate it during the operation up to the intestine and injure him.
Then consider it. For if the generation of Hydropisis is from the intestines, then it is necessary to extend with a section from the navel by the length of three fingers downwards over the chest.
But if the generation of Hydropisis is due to liver illness: then let your incision be on the left from the navel by three fingers.
If its generation is due to the spleen, then let the incision be on the right side: and it is not necessary that there should also be an incision on the side towards which the sick person is to lie, so that superfluidities do not run to that weak place.
Then pierce the skin with an instrument entirely. Then insert into that incision and separate your hand with a probe between the skin, and ligature, as if you were coring it; let the quantity that is being cored be of the size of a fingernail or approximately that.
Then bore the ligature (sifac), until the probe reaches an empty place; and that is a watery place. Then remove it (the spleen), and insert an instrument into the opening, of which this is its form. It is similar to a cannula; it is made of silver, brass or copper, linen, cleaned; at the lower part of it is a small opening, and on its sides there are three openings, two on one side and one on the other; and the end of it is slit, in the manner of an incision of a reed, as you see; at the upper end of it is a string.
For when the instrument reaches water, then it immediately descends upon the instrument, therefore evacuate from the water a half measure.
Since if you evacuate more than is necessary from it, perhaps the sick person may die from loss of his animal spirit; or he may experience a syncope that approaches death.
But evacuate from it according to its strength and according to the signs that indicate to you the dispositions of the sick person from the force of his pulse, and from the quality of it (the spleen).
Then remove the instrument, and retain the water.
That is because it (the water) is retained immediately because of the skin which retains the opening that is on the ligature; about this I told you to bore it in that manner.
Then repeat the operation on the second day, if you see the patient can bear it: and extract even a small quantity from water.
Repeat that procedure on several days without fear, and be careful to avoid error: until there remains only a small amount in water.
If you fear for the patient and let out a large amount from water: then care for him with warm sand, much sweating in a bath and sun, and watch for thirst; and care for him with drying medicines until he is cured: and cauterize over the stomach, spleen and liver, after the extraction of water: as I narrated in what preceded.
Chapter on the care of infants born in places where their bladder are not pierced.
Chapter LV. (Chapter fifty-fifth.)
When any infant comes out from his mother's womb and the head is not pierced with a lamb's bone, or the opening is narrowed or in an incorrect position.

Those in whom the opening is in an incorrect position are injured. Because from those who are born, the opening is at the end of the spine: hence it cannot urinate towards the front until it raises the spine with its own hand towards higher parts. Chapter 66.
