Chapter LVII.
On the purification of infants and treatment for error occurring to them.
Circumcision is not a solution to continuity, as with other wounds: however, since it is from our operation, by our will, and its use is specifically for boys, it is necessary that we mark in it a better procedure, and a lighter way leading to health.
I say therefore, that the ancients did not speak of circumcision in any of their books: since they do not use it in their laws, and it is only what we have acquired through experience.
It is because I found the majority of artificers and phlebotomists to use purification by circumcision with a knife and with scissors: they use algued, ligature with thread, and incision with the nail.
And I have indeed tested all these methods, and did not find a better purification with scissors, and ligature with thread.
Since in circumcision with the knife, the skin often escapes. Since the foreskin has two skin layers: perhaps the upper skin is cut, and the lower layer is torn: it is therefore necessary to make another incision in order to cut the other one, and pain will result. And with the purification that is done by the algued, that is, the digital method, which tailors use, is not cut at the extremity of the masculine member: since perhaps it enters its opening.
However, in circumcision with the nail, perhaps iron slips out and spoils your operation: and indeed the skin of a boy is short by nature, and often they are born like that, not needing purification: and I have already seen this.
The purification with scissors and ligature with thread has shown to be a good experiment for me: because the blades are proportional to the incision: therefore, the sharpness that is above is like the sharpness that is below. When therefore you press your hand, two sharp edges correspond and cut according to one operation at the same time; a compression of similar shape is made, containing the skin of the staff from all sides, with which no error whatsoever can fall.
And the method of your operation is that you should make him examine, primarily a boy who understands something, if he is from those who understand briefly, which you do not do unless you tie the thread on his own staff only; and then you will release it for another day.
Then make him rejoice and be happy in every way possible from you because he receives understanding of himself. Then make him stand between your prepared hands with the stature and let him not be seated; and hidden scissors in your hand or under your foot, so that the boy does not see them at all, nor anything from the instruments.
Then insert your hand to his staff, and blow on the skin, and draw it upwards until the head of the staff comes out. Then cleanse it from this because dirt has gathered in it.
Then tie the marked place with a double thread. Then tie below it a little ligament at the same time. Then hold with your index finger and thumb the place of the lower ligament in a good grip, and cut between two ligaments. Then peel the skin quickly upwards and take out the head of the staff. Then let the blood flow slowly (it is better) and put powder on top; and above the powder, a cloth in which the boiled lamb's fat has been spread with fresh rose oil; and let him be on it until another day; and take care of him with the rest of the treatment, until he is healed.
The form of the scissors for cleansing is as follows.
The two extremities are blunt, and they are incised: let not the branch of the nail go forth into them: and let the length of the two points be equal to the length of two handles equally.
The falling error in excision is because perhaps the entire inner skin escapes, or a part of it at the incision point.
Therefore, it is necessary to stretch it out from your side with your nail before the excision of the location, and cut it evenly.
If you cannot hold it with your nail, then pull it out with a tweezers and cut it.
If three days have passed and what is under the abscess remains inflated, excise it: then leave it until the abscess settles down and becomes warm, and peel off the scab easily and cut it as prepared for you: be careful not to cut the base of the abscess. For it will not harm him that.
Take care of that with him as it consolidates the wound with the powders we mentioned in the chapter on powders: and if it is cut deeper than the measure and reaches the superficial layers, it will not harm him even then.
Take care of that with him until it heals.
Chapter LVIII.
Chapter on the extraction of a retained bladder in the bladder.
Retention of urine in the bladder, occurs due to a blockage made from stone, frozen blood, pus, flesh born, and similar things from what we mentioned under methods of treatment in division.
If urine is not resolved and you see that its retention is due to a stone already in the neck of the bladder: then it is necessary for him who is ill to be bent over his knees. Then place his feet on top of his back, and let him stretch out his abdomen from the upper part of his back, and he should compress his breath as much as possible for him. Therefore, when the neck of the bladder is compressed towards the back, the stone in the bladder is expelled; thus, urine is released.
If it is not resolved with what has been said and the patient is strong on the sick man: then it is necessary to administer extraction of it with an instrument called syringe, whose form is like this Sit from silver, and be subtle, flexible, concave as a feather quill in subtleness of radius, long in the likeness of one and a half palms: to which a small-bore tube should be attached at its head.
And the method of urine exit through it is to take a double thread, tie at its end wool or cotton, good binding: and insert the end of the thread into the lower part of the syringe; and cut with scissors if there is any excess from the wool, but introduce into the tube with force, like squeezing.
Then grease the syringe with oil or butter, and lard, and egg white: let the sick man sit on a chair, and anoint the bladder, and his penis with moist oils, olive oil, and warm water.
Then insert the syringe into the vein with ease, until it reaches the root of the vein.
Then fold it twice above the navel.
Then push the syringe inside it until it reaches the bladder, and feel that it has already reached the empty space: this is not done according to this order unless because the channel through which it goes is where there is a twisting.
Then extend the thread slowly with wool. For it follows wool (as in the direction of).
Then pull it out and make the vein run through the urine way: and repeat the syringe, and do not stop doing this until the bladder is emptied, and the weak person finds relief.
Chapter on the quality of clysters for the bladder with a clepsydras (water clock).
Chapter LIX (99 in Roman numerals).
When there is an ulcer or blood congeals or pus collects in the bladder and it desires to discharge waters and medications into it: then it should be done with an instrument called a clepsydras, and this is its form.
It is indeed deaf (or closed). And in it there are three openings, two on one side and one on the other side, as you see.
And the hollow place where that which pushes it is located should be of such a size that it can hold it without addition until when it is pulled out with something from the humidities it is attracted: and when it is pushed, with it it is expelled to a great distance: this is how a clepsydras works, by throwing naphta (or Greek fire) in the war of Mars.
Therefore when the desire is to throw the waters into the bladder, insert the end of the clepsydras into the water and pull it out with that which pushes it towards the upper parts: for the water is drawn into the hollow of the clepsydras.
Then insert its end into a rod, as we previously described in a syringe. Then push the moisture with it, because that moisture immediately reaches the bladder, so that it feels weak.
Make a thin suppository for bladder cleansing.
Make it from silver or gold: its head should be like a calk (a hollow cylinder) with a small hole in it, and under the hole there should be a space for the string to pass through.
Then take the bladder of a ram and place the moisture in it, which you wish to use for bladder cleansing. Then tie it with a strong ligature between two spaces using double thread, and heat the moisture slightly over fire.
Then insert the end of the suppository into a rod, then press your hand on the bladder with the moisture and tight stringer until it feels weak, because that moisture has already reached the bladder.
If the bladder is not present for you, then take a piece of parchment and make a circle out of it, and pierce it completely from its entire roundness. Then insert the thread forcefully into those holes as they are turned. Then roll up the circle like a scroll; when you put into it what you wish from the moistures, oils, and waters.
Then bind it with the tool; and do with it as you did with the bladder by pressure with your hand until the moisture reaches the bladder.
Chapter 60.
Chapter on stone extraction.
We have said about the division of a Stone's species, and its treatment with medicines; we have mentioned the difference between a Stone generated in kidneys, bladder, and signs of its entirety; we have said about a Stone operated upon by hand and section; it is a stone generated in the bladder properly speaking; it is that which forms in the urinary canal; I am telling this with a clear explanation and abbreviation.
A stone generated in the bladder most often happens to children.
And among its signs is that urine leaves the bladder like water in its subtlety; and there appears within it white sand, and a weak man rubs his urinary canal, and labors with it, and often hangs down. Then it rises up, and is expelled together with it in many of them (the cases).
The healing of children is easy as long as they do not reach the age of fourteen. It is difficult in old people. However, it is moderate in young men, because it is between that (difficult and easy); for the one whose stone is larger, healing is easier; but if it is small, the cure is more difficult.
When we come to treatment, it is necessary first to cleanse the sick person with an enema, which will remove all the feces that are in his intestines; indeed, at times it prevents the discovery of a stone during examination.
Then the sick person should be received with his feet, shaken and moved to the lower part; so that the stone descends to the depth of the bladder or rises from a high place several times.
Then make him sit between your hands which are under his buttocks; so that the bladder becomes entirely empty towards lower parts.
Then examine (him) and touch him from outside.
If therefore you feel a stone [in your body], then hasten immediately with incision upon it.
If it does not fall under your touch at all, then you must lay the index finger of the left hand on it, if the patient is weak; or the middle finger if he is a full grown man; and introduce it into its [the stone's] own anus, and inquire about the stone, until it comes under your finger; and turn it gradually towards the neck of the bladder.
Then press upon it with your finger, and push it towards the outside against the place of section which you wish; and command the servant to press the bladder with his hand, and command another servant to extend the testicles of the right hand upwards; and let one servant remove the skin that is below the testicles in the part from the place where the incision is.
Then introduce the Spatula incising, whose shape is this [as depicted]. And find it which is between the anus and the testicles, not in the middle, on the left side of the natal opening; and let the incision be upon the stone, and your finger be in the anus; and let the incision be transverse, so that the incision be broad externally and narrow internally, according to as much as the exit of the stone from it is possible, not larger.
For perhaps the finger which is in the anus presses the stone at the incision, and exits without difficulty.
And know that from the stone are its angles and edges, wherefore the exit of it is difficult because of that [fact].
And it is smooth and round like a grape, and its exit is easy.
To him who has angles and edges, add [to the incision] in the fissure.
If it does not exit thus, then you must bore upon it; or you shall bind it with a well-placed ligature whose end is as the Moon, which binds above the stone and does not slip off from it; or you shall introduce beneath it a sharp instrument, curved at its end.
If however you cannot extend it over [him], then enlarge the opening slightly. If something from his blood beats you back, cut it off with the saw.
But if the stone is larger than one, then push the large one into the bladder first. Then cut upon it. Then push a smaller one after that; and do the same if there are more than two.
If it is very large, then ignorance is to cut through it with a great incision. Because it happens to the weak one of two things, either that he dies, or there is a continuous flow of urine; therefore because the place does not solidify at all.
But administer its expulsion, until it comes out; or force its fracture with forceps, until you extract it piece by piece.
When you have thus completed your operation, then fill the wound with turpentine, aloe, and dragon's blood; tie it up, and place over it a cloth soaked in oil and wine, or rose-oil, and cold water; so that an abscess may be seated warm.
Then turn the weak one on his back onto his neck, and do not loosen the bandage until the third day. When you release it [the wound], moisten the place with oil and much water.
Then treat it with diaphinicon ointment, and basilicon ointment, until it is healed.
If an abscess hot and corrosive is added to the wound, and similar things; as if blood congeals in the bladder, and urine is prevented from it; and this is recognized by the outflow of blood with urine. Then insert your finger into the wound, and draw out the blood. If it remains, it provokes the corruption of the bladder and its putrefaction.
Then clean the wound with vinegar, water, and salt; and apply any remedy suitable for its cure until it heals.
Moreover, during the entire period of treatment, it is necessary to bind two thighs together and press them, for the cause of the medicines placed on the spot.
If the stone is small and is in the neck of the bladder and causes obstruction to urine flow, then treat it with what I mentioned earlier before resorting to cutting. For many times you will be excused from the cutting in this treatment, since I have already proved that.
Also take the Perforatorium from iron altar, whose shape is triangular at the end and sharp, fixed in wood.
Then take a thread, tie it to the penis under the stone so that it does not return to the bladder.
Then insert the perforating iron into the penis with ease until the Perforatorium reaches the stone; and rotate the Perforatorium by hand in the stone gradually; you will force the perforation of it until it pierces through from the other side.
Therefore, urine is expelled immediately.
Then press your hand on what remains of the stone from the outside part of the penis. It breaks and comes out with the urine, and heals the sick one.
If this treatment is not prepared for you due to some reason that prevents it; then tie a thread under the stone and another thread above the stone. Then cut across the stone on the penis between the two bindings. Then remove it (the stone). Afterwards, untie the binding and clean the congealed blood that forms in the wound.
And it is not necessary to tie a thread under the stone, unless to prevent its return to the bladder: and another thread on top, unless when the thread is loosened after the stone's exit, the skin returns to its place, and seals the wound: and for this reason it is necessary for you, when tying the upper thread, to raise the skin towards above, so that it returns at the completion and seals the wound, as we said.
Chapter LXI.
On the Extraction of Stones in Women.
The Stone is less generated in women.
If however it happens to any of them that a stone occurs, then the cure is difficult, and it is forbidden on account of many conditions.
One of these is: that the woman perhaps is a virgin.
And secondly, because you cannot find a woman who will expose herself to the doctor when she is chaste or married.
Thirdly, because you cannot find a woman well skilled in this art, especially the operation with the hand.
And fourthly, the distance from the place of the stone: why it requires deep incision, and there is fear in this.
If necessity compels to this, then it is necessary that you take a skilled woman; and one is hardly found.
If you lack this, then seek a chaste doctor, subtle and present obstetrician well-learned in women's matters, or a woman who is knowledgeable about this art: make her present, and especially tell her to do everything that you instruct her regarding the examination of the stone.
Firstly, to see if the woman is a virgin: then it is necessary that you insert your finger into her anus and search for the stone.
If he finds it, then twist it with his finger and then tell the obstetrician to insert her finger into the weak vulva and examine the stone, after she places her left hand on the bladder and compresses it with good pressure.
If therefore a stone is found, then it is necessary that it be slowly moved from the opening of the bladder towards the lower parts with great care until it reaches the root of the hip with it.
Then it is to be cut above it at the opposite middle of the wound near the root of the hip, from whatever side it is prepared for him, and he feels the stone in that place; and his finger should not be removed from the stone, bent under it; and let the cut be small at first. Then a probe is inserted into that incision.
Then a probe is inserted into that incision. If he feels the stone, then add to the incision according to the size proportional to which the stone exits from there.
And know that there are many types of stones. For these reasons it is small, and large, smooth or rough, long, or round having branches.
Know its type so that it may be shown to you about the one that you wish.
If blood conquers you, then add in the place a burnt charcoal and hold it for an hour until the bleeding stops.
Then return to your operation until the stone comes out; and make sure that you prepare yourself with the tools which I have said for the removal of stones in men, so as to assist you in your operation.
If the flow of blood conquers you and you know that the bleeding is from an artery that was cut; then place flour on the place and bind it with a fitting ligature; do not move that; and leave the stone alone, and do not remove it. Perhaps a weak woman may die. Then take care of the wound.
When the sharpness of the blood subsides after days and the place becomes corrupt, then return to your operation until the stone comes out.
De modo in quo super herniam aquosam scindendum
On the incision of a hydrocele (hernia).
A hydrocele is not a tumor, but an accumulation of moisture inside the albovaginal (albocoelom) sac that contains the testicle and egg: and it is called the albovoaginal sac.
And sometimes it is within its own pannicle (fat) that nature has prepared for it near the testicle until it seems like an egg; and this is another egg, and it is between the albovaginal sac and the testicular skin which we mentioned earlier: and this does not occur frequently.
And indeed, the production of this growth is due to weakness that occurs in testicles; therefore, this material flows out into them. Sometimes it arises from a blow to the testicles.
And this moisture has many colors. For its color is often sloping towards yellow, or it is reddish, or dark, or watery white, and this is the most common.
And the signs by which it can be known where the accumulation of moisture is, are these. For if it is in the albovaginal sac that we mentioned earlier, then it is an abscess round and somewhat larger than the shape of an egg; and the testicle cannot be seen because moisture keeps it contained from all sides.
And if the moisture is within its own pannicle (fat), then it is an abscess round with a part of the egg; and therefore man is troubled because it seems like another egg.
And if the moisture is between the skin of the testicles and the albovaginal sac, then it falls under suspicion.
When you desire to test the color of the moisture, then probe the color of the moisture in an abscess with a square probe, whose shape has been described earlier. Therefore, according to what comes out in the track of the probe, judge about that which is between it.
When we therefore come for treatment with iron, then it is necessary that you command the sick person, if possible for him, to be bled and see his body full.
Then he shall lie on his back upon a high place slightly, and put many cloths beneath him.
Then you sit on his left side, and command the attendant to sit at his right, who shall extend his arm to one of two sides of the skin of the testicles, and to the part of the flank of the abdomen.
Then take a broad lancet and cut the skin of the testicles from the middle along its length, up to near the comb; and make the incision according to the straight line dividing the skin of the testicles, until reaching the white fat enclosing it; and scrape it off and observe it, or be careful not to sever it; and let your scraping be from the part that hangs more with the egg; and examine subtly with the scraping according to the quantity that is possible for you.
Then pierce the white fat full of water through a wide perforation and extract all the water.
Then separate the two lips of the incision with scissors and extend the white fat towards the top, and do not touch the skin of the testicles enclosing it; and cut the white fat in any way that is possible for you to cut it, either completely or piecemeal, especially the subtle side. For if you do not examine and scrutinize, there is no certainty that water will not return in the incision.
If however an egg appears externally from its skin during your operation; then when you complete the incision of the white fat, bring it back. Then join together the two lips of the skin of the testicles with suture.
Then take care of him as the other wounds, until he is healed.
If you find an egg corrupted by other blackness, then it is necessary to tie vessels that are suspension-related, fearing bleeding.
Then remove the testicle with its suspension, and extract the egg; afterwards take care of it as I said.
If water is gathered in two parts, then know that there are two branches; cut off the other part equally as you did on the other one.
And if it seems to you that the operation should be one, then do so; afterwards remove blood. Insert a thread submerged in oil or pink oil, and place another thread outside that was soaked in wine and oil; spread it over both testicles, inspect the intestines; place double cloths on top, which are called puluilli; tie them with a ligament that has six knots according to this shape.
Then take two cloths and wash them, fill them with carminated cotton according to this shape; make the ends which are pressed with wool or wet thread; attach them with a strap at the hips; one end should reach from anus to the back, and the second from the neck part; the two ends below should be attached to both thighs, and the other two ends to both groins; attach the whole strap at the hips.
Sometimes this branch is artificially treated with a cautery in place of the section with iron; you should take a subtle cautery knife and cut through the testicle skin with it; it should be lit as we described earlier until white albumen containing water appears; then take the cautery according to this shape.
Compared to Greek letters.
Then pierce it with that and burn it until all moisture comes out.
Then extend the sifac with forceps, and scrape it with a subtle cautery heated, and cut it as much as possible for you, until you remove the entire thing.
And be careful not to touch the egg, lest fire should do harm to it.
Know that this operation is safer and more distant from bleeding, and better than the operation with incision.
If, however, the operation opposes you at the time of incision, or at the time of cauterization an abscess is heated, or bleeding, or something else: then it is necessary that you take care of what opposes you from that with a cure suitable for it, according to what has been mentioned above.
If, however, the patient is feeble and fearful, and does not await this operation on account of its horror: then administer a lancing according to what I have told you; and there it is.
When it is confirmed to you by what we have said about the meanings that it is a watery branch: then it is necessary that you make the patient sit on an elevated seat.
Then lance the abscess on its lower part with a wide cupping glass; and place the lancing along the length of the body, and let the opening be wide until all the water flows out.
Then place a warm cloth over the spot, and bind it, and allow it to flow out the remaining water; then take care of it until the wound heals.
If, however, an obstacle is present to the outflow of water at the time you lance it; and this is not because a white cloth opposes the opening of the wound and prevents the outflow of water: then it is necessary to introduce a feather or an instrument with which water is extracted from hydropic swellings, whose shape has been mentioned earlier; or add in the operation of the wound a small amount.
And know that water returns and accumulates after six months, or approximately that period. When it accumulates, then it is to be pounded in the same way and the sick days will pass through.
Chapter Sixty-third.
Chapter on the treatment of fleshy roots.
Know that in the incision upon this root [Rhizoma], there is danger of slipping into destruction in many positions. Therefore it seems to me that its abandonment [of the incision] would be beneficial.
And I am recalling the operation in it and the appearance of the cauterizations.
Therefore I say that many cauterizations occur in bodies from which testicles are composed; this happens for various reasons such as.
Or from an excess of acute or sharp fluid that flows towards the testicles. Or from a blow [causing an injury].
And the color of the cauterization corresponds to the color of the body and no pain is found; it is a grave cauterization.
Perhaps it is a stone-like cauterization, whose color is dark, and there is no sensation in it.
Sometimes it occurs from a swelling of the arteries and their inflation; as I have already reminded you before; or from the inflation of veins.
What is known from these as being due to an inflation of the arteries, is recognized by the disposition of the cauterization, when you compress it with your fingers. And one should not touch it completely [throughout].
However, that which occurs from the inflation of veins is not dispersed by compression with the fingers.
And now it is possible that an incision can be made upon this appearance and upon the remaining flesh; and it is that the skin of the testicles is to be incised. Then stretch the egg upward and extract it along with a white silken thread; free the suspender from the water and tie the vessels; and incise the suspender after you have released it from all parts of the egg.
If therefore an egg is hardened with those born flesh, then it is necessary that you pull out the egg, and cut it.
And if there is an attachment between something from the siphunculus, or within a vessel: then it is necessary that you release the entire attachment, and cut it with a round incision.
If however there is the growth of flesh at a place of attachment which is behind: then it is necessary that you cut the whole of it, and pull out the egg, as we said.
When therefore your operation is finished, then fill the wound with wool soaked in rose oil and wine; afterwards care for it with the rest of the treatment, until it heals.
Chapter LXIII.
Chapter on the Care of Twigs, which is with Vines.
A tumor is enclosed by a certain enclosure resembling a bunch of grapes when the testicles are softened; and it becomes difficult for weak movement and exercise, and walking.
And in the treatment of this disease is fear due to the memory of what preceded it.
But it is necessary that we say the operation in it according to what the first ones did.

Then scrape off from every side, as we said to you in the extraction of arteries that are in the temples.

Take care of the wound along with the other wounds where pus is generated, so that the vessels which nourish one testicle fall out. It is not bad by that means.
If it happens that the vine grows on all the vessels, then they must be removed for this reason: so that the testicles are not deprived of nourishment by the incision, and it rots or burns and is no help to them.
Chapter LXV.
Chapter on the treatment of intestines.
The outlet of this intestine is from the incision which happens in the siphon stretched over the abdomen in the inguinal part of the stomach.
Because the intestines descend from that rupture to one testicle. And this rupture is either in the siphon or its extension.
These two types of ruptures occur for various reasons: either by striking, jumping, shouting, lifting heavy objects or similar causes.
And the sign is when it is from the extension of the siphon. It happens gradually over a long time and does not happen suddenly; it is an abscess equal to the turned-over deep [intestine]; because the siphon presses on the intestine.
And the sign of this [type of rupture] is when it is from a section of the siphon, because it causes intense pain from the beginning suddenly; it is an abscess different, appearing under the skin close by; and that is due to the outlet of the intestine and its course to the exterior of the siphon.
And sometimes it comes out with the intestine called "zirbum"; and this is called an intestinal ramus and "zirbia", and sometimes it occurs with ventosity (inflammation of the abdomen).
And sometimes fecal matter runs into the intestine and is retained there; it brings with it danger to the sick, because it causes pain, especially when it is pressed.
And in the treatment of this disease by iron there is fear; therefore care must be taken to avoid accident in it.
The method of operation is that you order the sick person to bring his intestine back with his own hand to the inner concavity of himself, if he obeys the return. Then he lies on his back on his neck between your hands; and elevate his legs.
Then stretch the skin that follows the skin towards the upper part and cut the skin of the testicles completely along the length. Then fix two hooks on the edges of the cut, according to what you need to open the cut with them; and the incision should be according to the amount that it is possible for an egg to come out from it.
Then scrape the sheep's bladder, and what is beneath the skin of the testicles until the albumen of the sheep's bladder becomes hard on all sides; then insert your thumb into the part that follows the testicle, into the part that is between the albumen of the sheep's bladder, which is under the skin of the egg, and between the folds, and without any adherence to it in the posterior part of the egg.
Then move with the right hand to the inner skin of the testicles and at the same time stretch the sheep's bladder albumen upward with the left hand; and lift the egg along with the albumen to the part of the incision, and command the attendant to stretch the egg upward; and you loosen the adherence that is behind the complete solution.
And examine with your fingers if there is nothing there from the intestine rolled up in hard albumen of the sheep's bladder. If you find something from it: then push it into the lower abdomen.
Then take the point, in which there is a thick thread made from linen of ten threads, and insert it at the last layer, that is, the tunica, which follows the skin of the testicles: then cut the ends that project from the thread until there are four threads. Then compose some of them on top of others in the shape of a cross and tie it with alsifach, which we mentioned earlier, as it is the strong ligament under the skin of the testicles: until no waste that nourishes them can send anything to them; so that a hot abscess does not occur there. And place the ligament again beyond the first ligament, at least two fingers away from it. And after these two ligaments, release from the alsifach, which is under the skin of the testicles, a quantity equal to the size of a finger: and cut the rest entirely in the round shape, and remove the egg.
Then cut the skin of the lower part of the testicles with a cut, from which blood and pus flows, as we said in that which was mentioned before.
Then apply wool soaked in oil and place it in the wound: and apply the ligament which we mentioned. And sometimes the alsifach is burned white, which we said, after its incision, fearing a flow of blood. Often this happens. And release the ligament until it falls by itself.
If the case persists, then fumigate with hot water: and place on it what we said until it falls.
Then take care of the wound with the rest of the treatment for wounds, until it is healed.
Head LXVI.
On swollen anus.
In this swollen anus, I have not seen anyone who dared to treat it with iron.
And first they said that it happens as we mentioned in the swollen anus that is accompanied by piles. What should be done is to tie the containers after cutting it below easily; then cut in the middle, and treat it later with what opens it itself, until the containers fall out; and treat the wound, as we said, until it heals.
Head LXVII.
On the rupture that occurs in the groins.
When rupture occurs in the groins, as we have said, and a place protrudes out, and nothing from the intestines descends to the testicles; and if it does descend, it is little and returns in all hours; but if this persists for a long time, a fissure is added in the scrotum until the intestines descend into the scrotum.
And this happens due to extension of the scrotum, as we have said in the groins. Because the scrotum extends; then it is softened, and the place is pushed out.
And its treatment is with cautery, as we have previously said about it.
Sometimes it is treated with iron, according to this method: and it is to lie weak on his back between your hands. Then cut the place of rupture and protrusion, with a cut across its width, according to the length of three fingers.
Then tie up the scrotum and what is beneath the skin, until the white part of the scrotum, which is beneath the skin following it, is exposed.
Then take the cautery and place it on the protruding part of the scrotum and press it deeply into the abdomen.
Then sew together two protuberances on the end of the radius from the shaft, and then extract the extremity of the radius.
And do not cut the shaft at all, nor draw out the yolk, nor anything else, as I told you in the treatment of the intestinal branch.
Then treat that with a wound cure. When you cut the threads, clean it and restore the wound until it heals.
For sifach contracts and does not add to a rupture.
And cautery is better in this place, because it is closer to safety.
Chapter LXXVIII.
Chapter on the softening of the scrotal skin.
The scrotal skin is often softened in some men, because the flesh between it becomes soft and its appearance becomes foul.
Therefore it is necessary for the one who asks to be treated for it, that he makes the affected one lie on his back and cuts through all the softened skin to the normal skin.
Then sew together the two flaps with a suture: and if you wish, or rather, trim away the excess softened skin with three stitches, or four, and make a firm stitch.
Then cut in between the stitches.
Then treat with wound cure the other wounds until they heal and the threads fall out.
Chapter LXXIX.
Chapter on castration.
You know that castration is prohibited by our law, and therefore it would be permissible for me not to mention it in this book; but since there are two methods, it is necessary for me to remember it.
One of these is that it should be in the knowledge of the physician when asked about it: and that he knows the treatment for it which happens to him.
Another method is that we often need to castrate certain animals for our benefit through it, such as sheep, goats, and cats, and similar ones among animals.
Therefore, I say that castration is done in two ways. Or by attrition. Or by a cut and division.
In that which is done by attrition, the method of operation is as follows: that we make the animal sit in warm water until its testicles soften and become limp, and then hang it; afterwards, rub them with your hand until they dissolve and no longer appear under touch.
In the castration by a cut and division, it is necessary that you hold the animal, and press the skin of its testicles with your left hand.
Then tie the suspensorium, and cut above all the egg with a single section until when two eggs come out: then cut that after you have scoured both, and do not leave anything over it except a small amount of thin sifaket on the vessels.
And this method of castration is better than that which is done by attrition because attrition possibly leaves something from the testicles, for which the animal desires coitus.
Then take care of the wound until it heals.
Chapter 70.
Paragraph on the cure of a Hermaphroditus in two ways.
A Hermaphroditus is from men according to two ways. One of them is because there is a space or gap, or in the skin of the testicles, between the two testicles, which has the shape of a female vulva, in which there are hairs; and sometimes urine runs out from that which is in the skin of the testicles.
In women there is one kind and it is the woman's vulva on top of the crest like small testicles of a man, projecting to the outside; of which one is like Priapus in a man, and two like two testicles.
And the treatment of the three kinds, two from men and one from women, is as follows: Because it is necessary to cut into the added flesh until the impression disappears. Then treat them with the care of other wounds.
In the second kind for men from which urine originates, which is in the skin of the testicles, there is no operation, nor is there any treatment at all.
Chapter LXXI.
Chapter on the incision of tentigines and projecting flesh in the vulvas of women.
A tentigo is possibly added over a natural thing until it becomes disfigured and its appearance becomes disgusting: and sometimes it is enlarged to such an extent in certain women that it expands like in men, and reaches copulation.
Therefore, one must hold the excess of tentigo with the hand or with a hook and cut it: and not cut to the extreme, especially in deep roots, so that bleeding does not occur.
Then take care of the wound itself until it heals.
But the flesh that arises is the flesh born in the orifice of the matrix until it fills it: and perhaps it comes out to the exterior like the tail; and for this reason some call the disease caudated. Therefore, one must cut it as one cuts tentigo and treat it until it heals.
Chapter on the treatment of a woman's alratch, which is not perforated.
Chapter LXXII.
The alratch is the swelling of a woman's unperforated vulva or a small opening. And it can be natural or accidental.
Accidental is when it results from an illness that has come before: and it itself is made either of flesh born added, or of sifach subtile, or spisso; and it is made either deep in the matrix, or in its sides, or on top of it, or below it: and it prevents coitus and impregnation, and childbirth, and perhaps menstruation.
The recognition of this is made through the examination of an obstetrician if the opening appears to be nearby.
If it is not apparent, then search for it with your fingers or with a rod.
If the opening is from sifach subtile and is near to two lips: then pull it and tear it apart.
And it is to place two lentils on top of the lips.
Then place your fingers of both hands together, and let the woman be on her back with her legs spread open. Then stretch out the two lips forcefully until the cervix is torn (or ruptured) slightly, and the opening is exposed.
Then take some wool and soak it in oil, and place it on the spot. Let the woman do this every day to prevent it from becoming sealed (or congealed) with something else.
If the cervix is thick or large, then it is necessary to remove it with a wide-blade spatula similar to a myrtle leaf.
If the opening is of flesh origin, then hang it with hooks and cut it; have medicines on hand that stop blood flow without causing pain, such as acacia, dragon's blood, and wax mixed with cow's milk fat.
Then apply a wide cannula made of lead to prevent the wound from healing quickly, hold it for several days; then apply linen cloth, and treat the rest with the usual remedies until it heals.
And sometimes there is a birth of flesh other than the baby from the womb; it is necessary to cut them in this manner: do not let it become an abscess (or cancerous), as cutting a cancerous abscess in the womb will create an absolute contradiction with iron.
Chapter LXXIII (73).
Chapter on Hemorrhoids, by Athehelil and Bothor concerning women's ulcers.
Hemorrhoids are the openings of veins from which blood constantly flows in large amounts.
When hemorrhoids have been prolonged, they become thrombus; I have already said about their types and signs in the previous section, and here I will mention what is cured by them and what is not.
I say, therefore, that hemorrhoids which are in the vaginal opening and are not perceived by touch: then there is no cure with iron for it.
But those which are above the vaginal opening, concerning which sensation falls, are those which can be cured.
Therefore, it is necessary that you enter the woman into a cold house. Then stretch the anus with forceps or with rough cloth, and cut them from their roots.
Then sprinkle powder on them near the flow of blood from one cut without biting: like ashes of acom, dragon's blood, and frankincense, and similar to these.
Then press his feet against the wall for an hour. Then lay her down in cold water.
If the bleeding continues: then make her sit in a decoction of sumac, and the bark of pomegranates, and gall nuts, and similar things.
Then take barley flour, and knead it with honey and vinegar, and make a plaster with it on his back.
If the blood is cut off with it, it is good: and if not, let adhesive winds and breasts, without scarification.
Then take wool and immerse it in the juice of thistle, or the juice of argus, or the juice of the leaves of alumroot, that is, agalantha, wine of Pontus, and let it stick to syrup.
When the abscess has ceased, then care for the place with ointments until it heals.
But Albath is red and resembles the head of an onion, and has a rough appearance.
Therefore, it is necessary to cut what appears from it, according to what I said about thalil equally: and care for it until it heals.
De Perforatione Matricis et Ovarii, cum haec operatio
On perforation occurring in the womb (womb = uterus).
On perforation of the womb (uterus) and ovary: There are many kinds of ulcers that can happen in the womb, such as cancer, stone-like abscesses, sores, abulleti, alekilati (herpes), fistulas, hemorrhoids, ragadiae, and apostema calidum.
And I have indeed said all these diseases and their kinds, and the signs of each one, and their treatments, in division: it is necessary that I say in this treatise about the hot abscess that occurs in the matrix, when it is one of the abscesses that collect pus, and to know how its opening with iron is done.
Therefore, you should consider. (This is a translation of a later part of the sentence.) Then if the pain of the abscess in its beginning is sharp with striking, and burning, and fever; and you see it redden; if it falls upon the sense, then do not pierce it with perforation; and heal it with what helps for maturation, until when the acuteness of the occurrences subsides.
Then it is necessary that you make the woman sit on a chair with two arms, and recline, or lean against her back, and put her feet to the lower part of the belly; and her hips should be spread out, and she puts her arms under her knees, and binds both with a suitable ligament to that.
Then the midwife should sit on the right side, and administer the instrument for opening the matrix's orifice.
And it is necessary that when you are to administer this instrument, you fashion the point of the probe deep into the woman's matrix: so that what goes in from the instrument is not more than the depth of the matrix, and harms the weak.
If it is an instrument more than the depth of the matrix, then it is necessary that you place feathers on top of the deep part of the matrix: to prevent the whole instrument from entering into the depth of the matrix; and it is necessary that you place a twisting thread, which runs in the instrument, on the upper side; and to hold the instrument, and to turn the twisting thread by an assistant, until the deep part of the matrix is opened.
When therefore it appears to be cut out and is touched with the hand, and it is soft and tender, then it is necessary that you separate it from its head using a broad spatula.
When therefore pus is evacuated, then it is necessary that you place a linen cloth dipped in rose oil on the wound, or green oil with some styptic substance; and place the linen cloth, and remove the incision in depth of the matrix.
And put on the outside over the matrix and on top of the comb, a clean wool dipped in water in which figs have been boiled.
Then it is to be treated with an ointment suitable for that purpose for two days until it heals.
And sometimes the matrix and wound are washed so that they are cleansed with water and honey; then with water in which the root of the garlic or long aristolochia has been boiled; then return to the ointment.
If the wound is hidden internally in the matrix, then it is necessary to prevent treatment with iron; instead cure it with what was said before for incisions.
Chapter LXXXV.
Instructions on obstetrics: how to treat living fetuses which have been born abnormally in shape.
It is necessary for an obstetrician to first know the shape of a normal birth.
Therefore the signs of this are that when you see a woman being pressed towards the lower parts, and she longs for air, and there is urging on her in childbirth, and the fetus eagerly desires to come out; then you will know that this birth is according to the natural shape, and it comes out at the head of its own and second one along with it: or suspended, or hanging from the navel.
When you see these signs, then it is necessary to press the womb in order that the fetus comes out quickly.
When it descends upon his head, the second one also descends with it, and it is to be cleaned from those superfluities with good cleansing.
But that which is beyond this delivery, is unnatural, inadmissible.
For sometimes the fetus emerges over its feet and the body of it comes out before its head and its feet and one hand, or one foot alone: or its head and one hand emerge: or the belly emerges, and perhaps it turns on its neck, and similar unadmissible figures.
Therefore it is necessary for the Midwife to be wise, skilful in all these matters, and to guard himself from error and deception; and I am showing every figure of them, and how the intelligence is in it, and it is indicated by that, and it will stand over him.
When the fetus emerges over its head in a natural delivery and becomes strong against the woman, and the delivery becomes difficult to her, and you see her virtue already weakened; then make her sit on a seat or women hold her: and warm her vagina with fennugreek water boiled and with moist oils.
Then the midwife introduces a small spatula between her fingers, and she splits the second one with it, and cuts it with her nail until what is in it from moisture runs out; and presses the woman's belly until the fetus descends.
If it does not descend, then it is necessary to enema the woman with fennugreek mucilage, with sesame oil.
Then command her after the enema to be pressed: and make her sneeze with pepper and hold her nose and mouth for an hour. For the fetus will come out immediately.
If two hands of the fetus emerge first, it is necessary to pull them back gently and gradually. If it does not yield upon entrance (of the fetus), then place the woman on a seat, and lift her feet upward; then strike the seat on the ground; and hold the woman, so that she does not fall during the striking.
If the hands do not emerge and the fetus dies, then cut them off and extract the remaining fetus; tie his hand with cloth and extract him equally; for he will come out himself.
The exit of the embryo is over the feet. When the fetus emerges over his feet, then it is necessary to push them upward; then turn the fetus gradually; afterwards equalize him.
Then take one of his feet and stretch it out gradually.
When they come out up to the hips, then order him (the fetus) to be pressed and make her sneeze with the help of incense; for he will come out if God wishes it.
And if he does not come out as we have said, then pull the fetus back gradually until you place him in the natural position. For he will then come out with an easy birth.
If it is forbidden as we have said (to extract the fetus): then take some latex of aloe, and sesame oil, and dissolved gum; and grind all of them well with a good pestle; then apply linseed with it to the woman's womb, and below her intestines. Then make her sit in warm water until she is about to give birth.
When you see that her lower parts are now warm, then give her (to sniff) some myrrh and place it under her nose. When the hour has passed, then make her sit on a seat. Then make it sneeze: and tie its own mouth and nose: and press the lower part of the abdomen with easy compression. The feces will exit immediately.
Exit of the fetus above the knees and hands. When it exits in this manner, then insert your hand gradually. Then the woman will lie down on her neck, and let her feet hang towards the bottom: and she herself should be lying on the bed, and clasp her hands together. Then press above its abdomen gradually. Then extract what is under her feet from the anus, until it is prepared below. If the fetus does not come out, then take its feet and move them with strong movement. Then press what is above the pubis gradually, until the fetus ascends to the upper parts. Then insert your hand and press the fetus gradually: and tell the woman to compress herself until the fetus comes out.
The exit of the fetus hanging laterally from the hands. Insert your hand for the reduction of its hand. If it cannot be reduced [the fetus], then lift the woman and make her walk.
If she cannot walk, then make her lie on the bed: and strike its legs with strong shock.
Then administer the ointment which you have prepared from mucilages.
If she takes it as childbirth, then make her sit on a seat. Then strive for the reduction of its hand, and press the fetus according to its natural shape: and make the woman sneeze, and tell her to compress herself until it comes out.
The exit of the fetus on its neck, with its hands spread apart, and its face towards the back of its mother. The obstetrician should hold the fetus and then gradually turn it with ease.
When it is turned equally, then place oil and mucilage upon the area mentioned earlier.
Then command him to move slowly. When you have done that, then make her sit on a chair and command her to lean towards the right side. Then command him to compress (it) and make her sneeze with powder.
The preparation of the fetus is for the side. When the second stage (of labor) descends to the mother's opening in this manner with the childbirth pouch, then cut open the childbirth pouch with your nail until it is evacuated by moisture.
If the fetus and its neck are hanging over the face, then cut it from the navel so that it is not retained and will die.
Then push the fetus towards the inside until you place it as needed; and command the woman to compress herself several times; for it will come out easily through the birth passage.
The delivery of twins or multiple fetuses. Know that twins often give birth and sometimes triplets and even quadruplets. However, such a thing is foreign and rarely occurs.
Five are indeed outside nature and do not live long; they are contained by the afterbirth though they multiply, for the afterbirth envelops them all at their navel; and they are separated by a siphac, distinguishing between them that is tied to each one's umbilicus.
And sometimes they come out just like a single fetus through the natural easy birth passage, and they come out in an unnatural way as we have described earlier.
If some of them have difficulties during childbirth and reach what we have described in the unnatural figures, then care for them as we have described; and let the midwife be skilled, and do what she does with ease and slowness, and adapt herself to every figure with the one that is prepared for her by her skill leading towards salvation.
Recollection of that which forms in the womb from embryos and are aborted.
Sometimes one, two, three, four, five, six, seven and more than ten forms in the womb: and it has been verified by me that a woman has expelled seven, another fifteen, all formed.
That which was done by measurement of the wise man.
Therefore, this entire matter must be in the knowledge of the obstetrician. Perhaps it may come to a similar one of his: therefore, let him oppose it with what is necessary.
Chapter LXXVI.
On the extraction of the dead fetus.
When you take care of a dead fetus along with what I said in the division of medicine and it does not come out, and you will have to operate with your hand, then you must consider.
If the woman is healthy and not with any accident from which it is feared that death may occur to her: then she must lie down on a bed on her back, and her head should be inclined downwards, and her legs raised: and a servant should hold her from both sides, or tie her to the bed, so that her body does not move during the extraction of the fetus.
Then the mouth of the womb should be moistened with olive oil mixed with gum arabic and fenugreek seeds and flax seed.
Then the obstetrician will wet his hand with these oils and gums: then he should insert it easily into the womb. Then he should ask where to place hooks on the fetus and where they are suitable for that.
Therefore consider then if the fetus is prepared to descend onto its head: then fix hooks in its eyes, or its neck, or its mouth, or its palate, or under its beard, or in its armpits, or near its ribs and under its hips.
If it is a descent below his feet, then incise on his chest, and in the middle of his ribs.
And it is necessary that he hold the hook with his right hand: and place his wound in that which is between the fingers of his left hand: and insert with his hand easily, and fix the hook in one of those places that we have said, until he reaches empty space.
Then fix another hook or third one, if necessary: so that the contraction is equal, and it does not lean to one side.
Then stretch with an equal extension, and let the extension not be only in a straight line, but move it to all sides, so that the outlet is relieved: as when using a tooth for its extraction.
It is necessary that between them there is softening of the extension. If a part is held back from it, then it is necessary that the midwife puts some fingers with oil and insert them on the side to turn what is held back along with them.
If then a part of the fetus is coming out, then the hooks are changed to another higher place: do this until the whole fetus comes out.
If then a hand is coming out before the others, and it cannot be returned because of its bending: then a cloth should be wound around it. Then pull it out completely until when the whole one comes out, cut it at the junction of the foot or the elbow: and so you must do with the other hand, and in both feet.
If the fetal head is large, or there is bending at its exit, or water has accumulated in its head: then it is necessary to insert a pointed spatula between the fingers and break the head with it, and pull out the water: or tear it apart with the instrument called Almisdac; whose shape comes after the shapes of the other instruments in the chapter following this.
Similarly, make an incision if the fetus is of large head nature, then it is necessary to separate the amniotic membrane: or pull him out with forceps, as we said. Then draw the bones with forceps.
If the head comes out and becomes stuck at the neck, then it is split open until the moisture that is in the chest is released.
If [the fetus] does not become entangled, nor yields to delivery: then make a shallow cut in the head as much as is possible for you.
If there is a protrusion lower in the abdomen or it has hydropsis: then it must be pierced until the moisture runs out of it.
If [the fetus] is above its feet, then pulling it out will be easy and directing it towards the maternal bone will be simple.
If it becomes stuck in the abdomen or chest: then it must be pulled out with a cloth you have wrapped around your hand, and the abdomen or chest should be opened until whatever is inside runs out.
If the remaining limbs are taken away and the head returns: then the midwife shall insert her left hand. If the maternal bone is open, then insert your hand deep into the womb and feel for the head with it and pull it out with your fingers up to the maternal bone: then insert a hook or hooks and pull it out with them.
If the maternal bone is stuck because of a hot abscess that has happened to it: then one should not exert pressure on it, rather one must administer a flow of liquid medicine and ointment, and sit in baths that soften and moisten.
If [the fetus] is on its side, it can be leveled out: then administer what was said for a living fetus.
If it is not possible to do that, then it should be cut piecemeal and extracted.
And it is necessary that you do not leave anything inside the second part at all.
When you have completed your operation, then administer what we said regarding the treatment of hot tumors that occur in the womb.
If there is bleeding, it should descend into warm waters of stiptics, and administer the remaining treatment.
I myself have seen a woman, whose womb contained a dead fetus; then she became pregnant again over the same one, after which another dead fetus also occurred. Therefore, after a long time an abscess occurred on her navel, which swelled until it was opened, and began to discharge pus.
I was therefore called for the treatment of this woman, and I treated her for a long time; but the wound did not heal.
I therefore placed on it some strong adhesives; and the bone came out from its place. Then a few days passed, and another bone came out. I was therefore amazed that there was no bone in her womb.
Therefore, since the fetuses were from bones.
I therefore cut the wound and extracted many bones when the woman was in good health; and she lived in such a way for a long time, and emitted little pus from its place.
I did not strengthen this foreign substance here, unless because there is knowledge and aid for it from the physician-artist when treating.
Chapter LXXVII.
Chapter on the forms of necessary instruments for extracting a fetus.
The form of the Spiral which opens the matrix.
Here below is the form of a Pincer, to which books are equal, having two equal spirals at the ends of two pieces of wood. Moreover, this Spiral should be finer than the Pincer: and it is made so, either from Ebony or from Boxwood.
And the width of all the wood is like two fingers: and the edge of each one is like a single finger, and the length of each is a palm (and half): and in the middle of the two pieces of wood are two additions of the same kind of wood, which have already been strengthened in both, whose length is half a palm and less: and the width of each is like two fingers or less.
And these two additions are inserted into the mouth of the matrix (to open it when you rotate the two Spirals).
Another form similar to this, finer and lighter.
Make it from Ebony or Boxwood, according to the likeness of the Pincers. Nevertheless, at the end of it there should be two additions as you see here above: and the length of each addition is a palm: and the width of each is like two fingers.
When you want to open the matrix with it, then have a woman sit on the bed, with her feet hanging down, with that which is between her thighs opened. Then insert these two additions connected together into the matrix: and you hold the lower end of the instrument between her hips. Then open your hand with the instrument, as you do with the Pincers, equally according to the amount you want by opening the mouth of the matrix, until the Midwife does what she wants.
Form of Dizziness Other Than That Which the Ancients Called Form of the Pushed Fetus.
The Form that breaks the large head: it resembles a pair of forceps, having teeth at its end, as you see.
And sometimes it becomes sloping, like forceps according to this form, as you see, having teeth like those of a saw, with which it cuts and crushes.
The Form having one spike.
The Form having two spikes.
The form of Spatulum (spoon-like instrument) having two ends for separating the head.
The form of two wide spatulas (spoon-like instruments).
These instruments are exercised, and the more numerous their kinds, and the more prepared they are by the craftsman, the quicker they are for the operation, and higher in the eyes of men, due to their quantity.
Therefore, do not despise any instrument from among them, but prepare it for yourself. Indeed, the necessity of them is unavoidable.
Chapter 78.
Chapter on the second extraction (cesarean section).
When the second (fetus) is retained during childbirth, then you must command the weak, to retain their breath. Then make her sneeze with a pinch and press your hand on her mouth and her own nose. If it then exits through this (incision), that is good.
If not: then take a pot and pierce a hole in the covering (of the incision), and put in them (herbs) opening the womb, such as camomile, root of rutabaga, fennel, chamomile, cassia wood, centaury. Take all these herbs or some of them, submerge them in water, and place them on fire.
Then place an embolus of reed upon the opening of the copotorium pot's hole, and another end into the bone of the matrix; hold it until the vapor reaches the concavity of the matrix.
Then make it sneeze, as we said. For secundina will come out easily.
If it remains after this treatment and does not come out: then command the midwife to immerse her hand in sesame oil or marshmallow (althea mucilage). Then insert into the vagina and search for the Secundina with it. When you find it (Secundina), then receive it and gradually stretch it out.
If it (Secundina) is attached deep within the matrix, then insert your hand as we said, until you find Secundina and pull it out gradually in a straight direction so that the matrix does not fall down due to strong attraction; indeed, it must be gently moved sideways right and left: then more should be added to counteract the attraction. It (Secundina) will then obey, and it is saved, and it goes out from the adhesion.
If the bone of the matrix is contracted as we have already said: treat it with sneezing and from the treatment of the pot with herbs.
If it (Secundina) does not come out with everything we said: then beware not to tire yourself by repeatedly trying the extraction.
But it must be bound to the woman's hip as it comes out from the bone of the matrix. Then cleanse her with the ointment called tetrapharmacon. For it (Secundina) will rot her after days and dissolve and go out.
But when it rots, the foul smell rises to the stomach and head and harms the weak. Therefore, it is necessary to administer suitable fumigations for that purpose.
Some of the ancients have already found out that fumigation with nasturtium and dried figs is effective.
The shape of the instrument used to fumigate a woman during retention of second stage labor and menstruation.
Make it similar to an alcamea or a ceramic vessel, and let the broad end be over the fire; fumigation should be placed on plums (or prunes); hold it until the fumigation is consumed, then repeat with another one.
Chapter LXXIX.
Chapter on the treatment of an unperforated anus.
Many boys are born, and the ani of theirs are not perforated, which the sifac subtle already has circumcised. Therefore, the midwife should perforate it (the circumcised boy) with her finger: and if not, she should perforate him with a sharp spatulum: and be careful not to touch the foreskin.
Then place over it (the circumcised boy) a linen cloth soaked in wine and oil. Then take care of him with ointments until he is healed.
If you are afraid that it may become infected, then put a leaden cannula into the opening and remove it when the boy wants to urinate.
And now it happens that circumcision of the anus also occurs from the hardening of the wound or abscess. Therefore, it must be cut away (the hardened tissue), then treated with what I said before using lead.
Chapter 80.
Chapter on the treatment of fistulas that occur in the lower part.
Fistulas that occur in the lower parts are Nodatio and Grossitudo that happen near the anus outside: or in the space of one part: and it is a Fistula one, or more than one.
Since the old Nodatio (abscess) opens up, watery white fluid or subtle pus flows out from it.
And sometimes these fistulas penetrate through. Therefore, when the fistula is penetrating, it is recognized by what comes out during the discharge and windiness, when a person uses laxative; perhaps a worm might come out from them.
And there are fistulas when they are in the space that penetrates up to the bladder and up to the scrotum of the penis. And there are fistulas that penetrate up to the junction of the hip, and up to the sacrum.
From this it is known that the penetrating fistula up to the anus can also be recognized by inserting your index finger into the anus; and inserting a probe (slender instrument) into the fistula from outside (air or iron), when there is no twisting (tortuosity).
If there is twisting (tortuosity) in it, then insert a slender probe made of lead or horsehair into it until you feel the probe or hair on your finger.
If you do not feel it deeply and nothing comes out of the discharge from the opening, or there is no windiness, or worms as I mentioned; then you will know that it is not penetrating, so proceed to treatment.
And when the fistula penetrates to the bladder or to the urine scrotum, its sign is the outflow of urine from it; and the prevention of this is that the location should be sealed with medicines.
If it penetrates to the junction of the hip or to the pelvis bone, then its sign is that a probe reaches there if there is no twisting up to the bone; and pain at the site, and pus always flows from it, and medication does not help in it, nor is it consolidated with ointment.
In these fistulas that penetrates, there is no cure at all; and the cure of them is pain and futility for him, upon whom it is formed by foolish physicians.
But the one that does not penetrate, and is not old, hopes for healing with a lancet: according to what I tell you, and I have already proven; and it is that he lies sick among your hands upon his back; and you raise his legs up to his hips, and his hips are inclined toward the belly of himself. Then insert a lead or air if there is twisting in the fistula, until you know where the probe has arrived.
If the sick person feels it around the anus, then it is necessary that you insert your finger into the anus.
If you feel the probe already penetrating by itself what has been detected with your finger, and between your finger and the anus or flesh; then certainly you know that it is penetrating; therefore do not labor on it, because there is no cure for it, as we have said.
They say that flesh heals in some people and the remedy by which they hope for help is to cauterize with a subtle iron, according to the size of the fistula, as has been said before, and then insert it into the fire, until it reaches around the anus. Then repeat that twice, or thrice, until you know that all the added fleshes that have been filtered and are similar to the reed of a bird's feather, are burned.
Then care for that with linen wrapped in butter until the burned flesh comes out; then care for it with ointments that make and strengthen the flesh.
If it heals, it is good.
And if not, then it will never be cured with any other treatment.
If it goes out and does not reach your finger that is in the anus, and there is a thick membrane from flesh or sifac between the two; and you see a Fistula on what follows the skin surface, then cut the skin from the beginning of the Fistula, and you go cutting with the tenta (probe) what is in the fistula until the incision reaches the end of the tenta, and the tenta is released and falls.
Then clean those fleshy parts resembling the feathers of a bird's quill, so that there is nothing left from them.
If blood overwhelms you and loosens between yourself and the procedure so that these fleshy parts separate, then it is better and quicker to aid, to cauterize it with fire or with sharp medicine.
Because cautery with fire brings good habits, burning of these fleshy parts added, and removal of blood, and drying of moisture.
Then treat that with linen wrapped in butter or boiled cabbages until the place emits pus, and those burned fleshy parts go into the pus.
Then treat the wound with consolidating ointments that produce hard flesh; there are medicines in which there is styptic and drying.
For when they are restored, then it will be cured; do not fear the repetition.
If the fistula has already reached the depth of the anus and is stretched from the body's excess: then insert your finger into the anus, and feel with it.
If you therefore feel a membrane between yourself and it, which is from sifac or flesh, and it is near penetration: then there is no operation in that unless according to the way of trust and hope.
The substance is that it [the ulcer] is administered in one of three ways: either to cauterize it, as we have said; or to excise it, until you reach its concavity, so that it is possible for you to insert a linen cloth and treatment from the adjacent area. And proceed not too much with the excision, so as not to cut into the skin containing the anus, and thus a harmful discharge occurs without consent. Then treat that [ulcer] with what I have said.
For perhaps it [the ulcer] will be cured: or remove the scab from it; and clean it after cutting it close to the anus, as we have said, or with a bag, or with some other sharp-tipped instrument. Then clean those fleshy parts filtered out during the incision, as far as you can with examination.
Then try the restoration of the whole wound with the incision and the upper opening where it is consolidated; and there remains an open fistula in the inner part of the anus, and it will be easier on the patient.
And sometimes a fistula is drained in this manner: and it is when you insert a bag into the fistula; and it is on the side of the anus near the surface of the body with skin and edge of the anus; then take a perforated-tip bag, which is like a needle, i.e., prepared from calfskin, in this shape. And insert into it [the fistula] a thread wound up from five threads and around that. Then insert the bag with the thread into the fistula, until you reach its concavity.
If it [the fistula] penetrates into the anus's margin internally, then extract the thread from that hole; so that you insert your finger into the anus and extract the end of the thread, and bind both ends together; and tie each one separately, and let it stay for one or two days; and the more the thread cuts into the flesh, tie it well, until those fleshy parts between the two ends of the thread fall off and disappear; then care for the wound until it is consolidated and healed.
If however the orifice of the Fistula is not penetrating: then make it penetrate in whatever way prepared for you, unless it is very deep. For you there is no need to do so, because not to cut the muscle itself.
Then perform as we have said, until it heals.
The form of a spiny spatula with which the Fistula is cut, whose sharpness is very acute on one side and the other side is not acute, so as not to cut what is not necessary, as you can see.
Chapter LXXXI.
On the suture of Hemorrhoids from which blood flows from their incision and care of fissures.
Hemorrhoids are of two kinds. Or they are within the anus, similar to cherry-stones or raisins; or they seem to be like grains of wheat themselves. And some are small and large; and blood flows from them always, and there is one and many of them. And they are outside the anus, and at its extremities.
However, those that are outside the anus, are for the most part moist, from which lemony water or a little blood flows continuously; and they are according to the color of the body.
And the treatment of those that are within the anus is to command the patient to eat a laxative; and it is expressed until it appears through the anus, and the feces appear to you. Therefore also, tie them with tweezers; or hold them with your nails. Then cut them at their roots.
If they cannot be held in them with tweezers, due to their moisture and softening; then grasp them with a rough cloth or with a glove made of coarse wool, and extract them with your fingers. Then cut them (the vessels), and sprinkle some warm powders over them after cutting for them to remain in the place of the cautery. Or cauterize them according to what has preceded in the chapter on cauterization. Then care for them with the rest of the treatment until they heal.
If the anus does not obey to the evacuation, then enema the sick person with a small purgative enema, so that it cleans what is in the anus, and let it obey to the evacuation quickly when the sick person evacuates.
If however they are foreign bodies outside the anus, then their matter is light, easy: and it is to be that you grasp them with your nail, or grasp them with a hook, and cut them. Then care for them as we have said, until they heal.
And whoever shrinks from cutting with iron, then it is necessary that you administer their suture in this way. Take thread wrapped around and insert it into the point (the wound). Then pull out the foreign bodies upward, and make it penetrate with the point into the root on the other side: and wrap the ends of the thread around the tip of the needle, and let them be wide: and sew the foreign bodies tightly with a strong stitch. Then tie the thread and pull out the needle.
Do this with all foreign bodies, and leave one of them: do not sew it, so that the excess blood may flow out from it.
Then place a cloth soaked in rose oil or pitch over the anus and put it on the anus: and order the sick person to rest. Then let him go until he falls asleep.
When foreign bodies fall out, care for them with ointments and the rest of the treatment, until they heal.
On the care of fissures. For they often occur due to drying out of feces and tightening of nature.
If they become old and medicine does not help: then it is necessary to shave them with a spatula or your nail until they become moist, and remove the upper bark which prevents their healing. Then care for them (the wounds) until they heal as required.
If they do not heal: then again treat them with a stronger solution than the first, until they bleed much, and then care for them until they are healed.
On the treatment of ulcers, both inverted (or round) and not inverted (or linear), and on scirrhus (or cancerous tumors) and Formicae (or ant-hills, a type of swelling).
Chapter LXXXII.
Know that Almirmar is not anything but a round node similar in color to the body, like a nail head; and it occurs throughout the body, especially in the lower parts of the feet and fingers; and it happens that pain occurs during walking.
Therefore, it is necessary to cut what is around the nail, hold with forceps or with a hook, and uproot from its root.
Then care for that, and if you wish to cauterize it as previously mentioned in its chapter.
An ant-hill (scirrhus) from the dry part is a small elevation, rough, filtered, round on the surface of the body. And they often occur in the hands of children.
And its treatment is to stretch (the ant-hill), and cut it; or stitch it with silk thread; or with hair, until it falls off. And if you wish, cauterize it with fire or with a sharp medicine as previously mentioned; and now ant-hills (scirrhus) that are inverted and not inverted can be uprooted with the tool I will describe.
Formica is also a small, filtered elevation that is rough and deep-rooted; when cold is found on it, it feels like the bite of an ant; and it occurs throughout the body, but it is most often found in the hands.
The treatment is to take a cannula from the feather of a goose or strong vulture; and place it over the worm, until it contains a circle by its parts. Then turn your hand with the cannula until it withdraws what is around the worm; and you will place it in deep flesh, and you will pull out the worm by its root.
And if you wish, do this with an air or iron cannula, according to this shape.
Let the upper end of the cannula be pulled upwards, drawing the deaf and rolled one, so that it is released from its grasp and its reversal.
And if you wish to cauterize the worm as stated in the cauterization of Athelil in the chapter on cautery.
Chapter LXXXIII.
Chapter on the shapes of instruments used for enemas in diseases of the anus, and the solution of the abdomen, and of the colon.
When an enema is made from silver, or brass, or copper fused, or beaten.
And sometimes it is made small, and large, according to those for whom it is administered.
Therefore that which is given for the cure of small children should be small; and for those with weak or painful anuses, so too should their enema.
Large enema.
The cannula of this, that is the upper part to which the uterus is tied, should be wide according to this method; and it should have a distinction so that the uterus can be tied as you see, and its lower end, which is introduced into the anus, should be deaf, that is not open, soft, very fine, pulling towards subtlety; and on one side of it there should be two holes, and on the other side one hole.
And let the size of the hole be according to the size of fingers, and it should not be too thick, and it should be a uterus in which the medicines are placed, which is from animal bladder; or from the skin of an egg, which should be similar in shape to that of a small onion; whose root should be one palm.
It should be pierced with many holes as it is rolled, and let the space between each hole be as thick as a finger. Then insert into it the thread, which is made of ten threads or approximately that, and bind it with a knot like an onion. When placed in it, the uterus should be tightened at the head by strong constriction with a purgative cord. Then purge it.
And this is the shape of the circle depicted here and the holes.
